# NewUM Product Roadmap

:tools:1f6e0🛠️#FFF0B3PAGE UNDER CONSTRUCTION BY THE PRODUCT TEAM

12falsenonelisttrueNewUM Version 1.0 - Product Scope

NewUM Version 1.0 establishes the foundational platform for OncoHealth to deliver fully delegated chemotherapy utilization management services in Mainland across Commercial and Medicare lines of business. It achieves functional parity with existing OneUM platforms while introducing meaningful improvements in user experience, implementation efficiency, and clinical workflow and decision making. V1.0 enables OH teams to reliably intake, review, determine, and communicate decisions for chemotherapy treatment requests to health plans, providers, and members&mdash;within compliance timeframes&mdash;using a standardized, rules driven platform.

This is not the final version intended for a live health plan launch. Instead, V1.0 delivers a broad enough scope to stand up a health plan in a production-like environment and conduct extensive user testing with complex cases&mdash;a critical step to de risk the first real health plan migration to NewUM. The target completion, per the SOW and project plans, is June 2026.

This document is a product scoping guide for product, operational, and technical teams to make Version 1.0 decisions. It is intentionally concise and does not capture all product details; those will be managed with stakeholder input in Product Requirement Documents (PRDs) and NewUM roadmap artifacts.

End-State Capabilities

NewUM Version 1.0 Product Scope

NewUM Version 1.0 - Functional Releases

Version 1.0 to be completed within Phase 2: March 3-July 31

Total Sprints in Phase 2: 11

Release 1: Sprints 1-3 (Mar - mid-Apr)

Release 2: Sprints 4-6 (mid-Apr - end-May)

Release 3: Sprints 7-9 (Jun - early-Jul)

Hardening: Sprints 10-11 (Jul)

:tools:1f6e0🛠️#E6FCFFRelease 1: Foundational Intake & Case Creation

Link to Release Doc: <TBD>

Functional Business Requirements

Support all current case submission channels (fax, phone, web)

Implement the chemotherapy case data model for protocol details

Apply guardrails for treatment details

Ingest and validate member and provider files from health plans

Surface AP clinical configs (drugs, regimens, diagnoses, PA status, formulary data) in workflows

Deliver the core case view shell and edit screens

Provide initial work queue infrastructure and basic routing rules

Enable case search using standard identifiers (reference number, member name, etc.)

Stakeholder Capabilities After This Release

OH teams have a fully functioning intake pipeline and a case shell ready for clinical review workflows.

Submit chemo PA cases through all support intake channels

Capture treatment details in a standardized, structured format with data guardrails

View and complete protocol details (drugs, regimens, diagnoses, dosing schedules) within a new unified case experience

Rely on Admin Portal configurations and formulary files as the authoritative source of clinical and plan data

Automatically route cases to simple work queues using configurable ulres

Access basic case attributes in the reporting layer

:stethoscope:1fa7a🩺#EAE6FFRelease 2: End-to-End Case Review

Link to Release Doc: <TBD>

Functional Business Requirements

Deliver full clinical review workspace, including documentation of clinical notes and interventions.

Implement drug‑level determination workflows with plan‑specific rules surfaced in‑flow (PA, NP, step therapy, formulary logic).

Support auto‑determination logic for PA Exempt, Out‑of‑Scope (OOS), and indication‑based approvals.

Enable automatic case completion and notification package generation when all drugs qualify.

Integrate the Turnaround Time (TAT) engine with TAT indicators displayed during review.

Enable queue sorting and filtering by TAT deadline.

Trigger outbound authorization files for medical and pharmacy benefit drugs.

Provide read‑only case access for health plans and provider offices.

Support health plans with appeals workflows (non‑delegated).

Ensure data from all determination workflows flows into the reporting layer for OH standard regulatory and compliance reports.

Stakeholder Capabilities After This Release

OH teams can now fully process, determine, and communicate decisions for chemotherapy cases with all required compliance timing and operational workflows in place.

Process chemotherapy cases end‑to‑end from intake &rarr; review &rarr; determination &rarr; notifications.

Perform medical necessity reviews with full documentation of notes and clinical interventions.

Apply drug‑level determinations with full visibility into plan rules (PA, NP, step, formulary).

Automatically complete cases when all drugs qualify for auto‑determination (PA Exempt, OOS, indication‑based approvals).

Meet Commercial and Medicare TAT requirements with clear in‑case deadlines and TAT‑based queue prioritization.

Communicate determinations through letters, IVR, and outbound authorization files to plans and PBMs.

Provide read‑only case visibility to health plan and provider users.

Support health plans with appeals, even though OH is not delegated to make appeal determinations.

Access case‑level data in the reporting layer for regulatory, compliance, and operational performance reporting.

:white_check_mark:2705✅#E3FCEFRelease 3: Medicare, Rules and Audit

Link to Release Doc: <TBD>

Functional Business Requirements

Support full health plan UM program configuration in the Admin Portal (policies, formularies, rules, delegations, networks).

Deliver a configurable rules engine with semi‑technical editing, rule versioning, and rule‑change audit history.

Provide a detailed case‑level audit log capturing data changes, timing, user actions, and applied rule versions.

Make operational KPI dashboards available for supervisory oversight.

Enable supervisor queue management tools (reassignment, load balancing, visibility).

Support all required Medicare workflows: AOR, Untimely (deemed denials), IRE packet generation, IDN, Reopens, Dismissals, Reconsiderations, D‑SNP rules, Multi‑Language Insert (MLI) and accessibility requirements.

Stakeholder Capabilities After This Release

OH can now configure, operate, audit, and oversee chemotherapy UM for Commercial and Medicare in a production-like environment, meeting operational, regulatory, and plan-specific needs. 

Configure a full health plan&rsquo;s UM program in the Admin Portal, including policies, formularies, delegation rules, benefit rules, and networks.

Manage routing and determination logic using a configurable rules engine with full versioning and rule‑change history.

Trace the complete history of a case using a detailed audit log tracking what changed, when, by whom, and which rules/versions were applied.

Operate and oversee UM performance using supervisor queue tools and operational KPI dashboards.

Support all mandated Medicare workflows, including AOR, IRE, IDN, D‑SNP, reconsiderations, dismissals, and MLI requirements.

Rely on fully integrated data in the reporting layer to support regulatory, compliance, and internal operational reporting.

:bricks:1f9f1🧱#FFFAE6Release 4: Hardening & Readiness Testing

Link to Release Doc: <TBD>

Functional Business Requirements

Conduct end‑to‑end regression testing across all workflows (intake &rarr; review &rarr; determination &rarr; notifications &rarr; reporting).

Resolve backlog defects, workflow inconsistencies, and integration gaps across NewUM, Admin Portal, letters, auth files, and queues.

Execute production‑like testing with complex chemotherapy cases across Commercial and Medicare benefit types.

Finalize all Medicare exception path coverage (untimely, dismissed, reopened, reconsideration).

Confirm data quality and completeness across reporting layers and operational dashboards.

Validate outbound integrations (auth files, IVR, letters) for accuracy, timing, and routing.

Stakeholder Capabilities After This Relase

Release 4 ensures NewUM Version 1.0 is stable, tested, and production-ready for a simulated health plan, de-risking the real migration by validating workflows, data quality, and all regulatory requirements. 

Test a full health plan end‑to‑end in a production‑like environment using complex, real‑world case scenarios.

Rely on a stable, high‑performing platform that has been validated across all major workflows, integrations, and exception paths.

Use NewUM confidently for large‑scale user testing, clinical scenario evaluation, operational dry‑runs, and training.

Confirm all required Medicare workflows (including exceptions, denials, reconsiderations) behave predictably.

Trust the accuracy of data across reporting, dashboards, audit logs, and outbound files.

Assess readiness for migration of the first live health plan with minimized risk.

NewUM Epics

To scope NewUM effectively, we need a structured framework that brings clarity to:

The end-to-end case lifecycle

What each user persona needs to see, decide, or act on at each point

The underlying data complexity required to support our health plans

Our goal is to ensure that each Epic represents real work domains and not arbitrary system components. 

Epic to Feature Relationship

Our Epics are large, long-running thematic structures that drive NewUM vision - features drive the incremental steps. Each Epic will contain a set of features. We&rsquo;ve established two key principles:

Features must be fully delivered within a single release.

Epics can (and will) span all releases. 

Epic Definitions

Epic

 | Category

 | Definition

 | 
1 | Case Intake

 | Case Intake & Entry

 | Defines how cases are sent into Onco for review - including channels, intake validation rules, and request initiation date. Current intake methods include Phone, Fax, Email, and Web entry - future method needs to include API. 

 | 
2 | Case Entry (General)

 | Case Intake & Entry

 | Covers the core capabilities for entering case information that is consistent across all treatment types. Includes capturing member eligibility information, provider details, clinical documentation, and baseline data required for downstream processing before the case has been submitted for review. 

 | 
3 | Case Entry - Chemotherapy

 | Case Intake & Entry

 | Specialized case entry workflows and data required for chemotherapy cases. Includes regimen details, protocol-driven data elements, odsing details, and clinical criteria specific to chemotherapy. 

 | 
4 | Case Entry - XRT

 | Case Intake & Entry

 | Support radiation therapy-specific case entry needs - including treatment modality, boosts, and required attachments unique to XRT cases. 

 | 
5 | Case Entry - GMT

 | Case Intake & Entry

 | Support case entry workflows unique to genetic molecular test cases - covering test-specific data requirements, lab details, etc. 

 | 
6 | System Case Assignment

 | Case Processing & Determination

 | Automation and management of how cases are routed to the appropriate reviewers. Covers assignment logic, queue manangement, load balancing, escalation paths, and rules that determine which user or team receives a case. 

 | 
7 | Case Review - Processing

 | Case Processing & Determination

 | Encompasses the activities performed by clinical or operational staff while reviewing a case. Includes task management, criteria review, clinical notes, documentation review, and workflow steps leading up to a determination.

 | 
8 | Case Review - Determinations

 | Case Processing & Determination

 | Supports the workflow steps and guardrails that surround final determinations for a case. Includes decision capture, rationale entry, additional reviews, and compliance-aligned determination workflows.

 | 
9 | Outbound Determination Notifications

 | Notifications & External Communication

 | Manages all outbound notifications following a determination. Covers generation, formatting, delivery, tracking and logging of provider, member, and health plan notifications across all communication channels - fax, email, IVR, etc.

 | 
10 | Authorization Files

 | Notifications & External Communication

 | This Epic covers the creation, management, and delivery of structured authorization data files used by health plans and PBMs. It includes defining the data elements, formats, triggers, and transmission mechanisms required to support claims adjudication.

 | 
11 | Health Plan Reporting

 | Reporting & Analytics

 | Delivers reporting capabilities needed by health plan clients. Includes all OH standard reporting capabilities, including any contractual or regulatory reports.

 | 
12 | Operational (OH) Reporting

 | Reporting & Analytics

 | Supports internal operations with reporting and dashboards covering workload, productivity, timeliness, staffing needs, audit results, and internal KPIs required for daily and long-range operational oversight.

 | 
13 | Additional UM Programs

 | Case Processing & Determination

 | Covers the setup and workflows required for any additional UM programs that Onco offers beyond our standard offering (e.g. Site of Care, Gold Carding, etc.). Includes unique rules, data and workflow needs.

 | 
14 | Post Denials Module

 | Case Processing & Determination

 | Supports activities and workflows that occur after a denial, such as reconsiderations, appeals, additional documentation review, and any downstream tasks or reporting associated with denial management.

 | 
15 | Provider Data

 | Data, Rules, & Configuration

 | Manages all provider data elements required for case processing, including provider lookup, validation, network checks, and integration with external provider directories or data sources.

 | 
16 | Turnaround Timers (TAT)

 | Data, Rules, & Configuration

 | Implements the logic and monitoring for regulatory and plan‑specific turnaround times. Includes clock start/stop rules, timers for different case types, alerts, escalations, and reporting to ensure compliance. Includes additional views for internal and external users

 | 
17 | User Roles, Security, and Management

 | Data, Rules, & Configuration

 | Defines role‑based access, permission structures, and user management functionality. Ensures the right users have the right visibility and capabilities while maintaining compliance and security.

 | 
18 | Admin Portal Enhancements

 | Data, Rules, & Configuration

 | Covers any enhancements that need to be made to existing Admin Portal functionality to support NewUM vision.

 | 
19 | Configuration & Rules Engine

 | Data, Rules, & Configuration

 | Provides the underlying rule-based logic that drives system workflows, case routing, criteria application, and program-specific requirements. Supports flexible configuration without code changes.

 | 
20 | Migration Pipeline

 | Platform Enablement & Migration

 | Defines the processes and tooling needed to migrate legacy cases, provider data, and reference data into NewUM. Covers data mapping, transformation, validation, and load workflows.

 | 
21 | External User Case Views

 | Notifications & External Communication

 | Supports views and functionality for users outside the internal operations team (e.g., providers, health plans) to access case information. Includes visibility rules, status updates, and documentation access aligned to privacy and compliance requirements.

 | 
Feature Breakdown

The product team will be managing the list of features and how they map to Epics, Versions, and Functional Releases in this document:

NewUM Roadmap

 Product Team&rsquo;s Release Proposal: Shift Release Cadence to 6-8 Week Increments

ec7435e8-d942-46a2-a916-508c0d03464bdbc959a3-e7b4-4528-9485-dce816b6e240DECIDEDProduct, Technical, and Project Leadership agreed to the proposal during Product Working Discussion mtg on 2/4.Product, Technical, and Project Leadership agreed to the proposal during Product Working Discussion mtg on 2/4.
Current State

The operating agreement specifies 3 large releases with general scoping recommendations. In order to more effectively manage scope, we recommend incremental releases prior to the full release.

Current Release Definitions:

R1: Core Platform

R2: Clinical & Benefit Expansion (intended for first client migrations post-hardening - Phase 3 on 11/30)

R3: Advanced Workflow

Challenges with the current model:

Release definitions are vague for downstream stakeholders and Product teams, making scoping decisions difficult

We currently have 71 features, expected to grow as large buckets (ex: Post-Denials, System Case Assignment) are further decomposed. 

~80% are essential for case processing - either for functional parity or to meet industry standards

~10% are strong &ldquo;should-haves&rdquo; or program-specific requirements that may be needed to support client migrations

Aligning large releases to PI planning creates heavy pressure for the product team to fully complete PRDs upfront

The current model leans more toward waterfall, not iterative development

Longer release cycles place more pressure on stakeholders and increase risk that design issues could go unchecked

Recommendation

Move from three large releases to 6-8 week incremental releases with iterative planning and scope definition. 

Approach

Begin with baseline requirements & happy-path workflows, then progressively layer in complexity. 
Example: Start with ability to enter a case with drug integration and dosing

Add health plan configuration

Add NP rules and auto-determination logic

The product team will determine which features included in each incremental release, based on readiness and priority

Benefits

Better PRD quality for PI planning

Increased flexibility - shorter cycles allow us to pivot when new info emerges, scope changes, dependencies shift, etc.

Improved stakeholder management 

Short, repeatable increments create steady delivery rhythm.

## Product Governance Process Overview

Product Releases are 6-8 weeks

NewUM Version 1.0 targeted for August 2026

Hardening phase will be from Aug-Oct

 

Product Team Decision Log will be used as framework to capture NewUM product decisions. (Owner: Alison Stamp)

Decisions will present as 3 sizes, Small, Medium and Large.

Small items will be discussed at the product team level. Venky and Erik are to be informed.

Medium items will be discussed internally with the team. These items will require consent from Venky and Erik. The Executive Steering Committee will be informed.

Large items (major changes to scope, time, or cost) will require Executive Steering Committee review and decisioning.

Product Team Norms

The product team will track all business decisions within this confluence page and supporting NewUM Product Decision Log.xlsx. The purpose of this log is to ensure that we are efficiently tracking all open decisions that need to be made and keeping a record of all decisions that will be made throughout the NewUM Project.

Decision Log Definitions

Status 

Status

 | Definition

 | 
New

 | Logged, needs triage

 | 
Open

 | Shaping decision & options

 | 
In Review

 | Stakeholders are evaluating - Brief has been shared with stakeholders, pending final decision

 | 
Final

 | Decision recorded and communicated

 | 
On Hold

 | Temporarily paused with reason

 | 
Size of Impact

Size of Impact

 | Definition

 | 
Low

 | Affects few stakeholders or only internal OH users

Minimal workflow disruption; cosmetic of small improvements

Reversible with little/no cost

No material affect on customer or business outcomes

 | 
Medium

 | Affects specific user group or subset of teams

Noticeable workflow changes but low operational risk

Some rework might occur if direction is wrong

Moderate influence on product experience

 | 
High

 | Affects multiple stakeholder groups or key workflows

Significant workflow changes and potential for disruption if done incorrectly

Harder to reverse; could require engineering rework

Influences customer experience or operational scalability in a meaningful way

 | 
Critical

 | Impacts mission-critical workflows used broadly across the organization

High operational, customer, or business risk if handled poorly

Not easily reversible; strategic consequeneces

Drives cross-team alignment or has regulatory/compliance implications 

 | 
Urgency

Urgency

 | Definition

 | 
Low

 | No timeline pressure; can be decided later

Work is not blocked

Deferring has no downstream consequences

 | 
Medium

 | Should be decided within a few weeks or within the current planning cycle

Some work may depend on it later, but nothing is immediately blocked

Moderate risk of inefficiency if decision drags on

 | 
High

 | Must be decided soon (days or within a sprint)

Delaying will create rework, inefficiencies, or uncertainty across teams

Work may be partially blocked

 | 
Critical

 | Requires immediate attention (today or this week)

Work is fully blocked without the decision

Delay directly causes timeline slippage or risk to a release, contract, or dependency

 |

 | Milestone Description

 | Studio@Newfire delivers project plans for iteratively redesigning critical interface components in Phase 2, based on user research and analysis

 | All system configuration requirements for the initial default implementation are completed, including first drafts of respective client configurations and configuration guides.

 | Studio@Newfire iteratively redesigns NewUM's most critical components using a dual-track agile approach

 | First fully functional replacement for the MATIS admin (MVP), including: Case Intake and major UI modules (e.g., Dashboards & Queues, Clinical Information, Case Entry). New capabilities for Reopen, Withdrawal, data correction, and partial approvals. New capabilities to easily find other cases for the same member and enter new provider data in the UI.

 | 
2

 | NewUM Core Milestone

 | Data model sufficient for a standard, unconfigured payer, proving the concept for simple case chaining. Case state machine implemented with a configurable rules engine, providing basic automation and guardrails. REST API abstracts all case engine internals. Event subsystem with stubbed or partially-implemented integrations.

During case intake in NewUM, there may be times when an eligible member cannot be found in the system. This may be caused by both data, technical, and process issues. 

Current state: in MATIS, &ldquo;if we already tried to look for the patient by starting a new prior auth and is not popping, depending on the health plan, we either create the patient or redirect back to the plan with their full name and DOB. For Sentara, CRSs check Availity for example but unsure if they use it for other health plans as well.&rdquo; - Nicole Santiago

Description

 | Do not build the ability to create a new member on the fly. 

If member is not found during intake, follow a manual only process (i.e. contact health plan, tracking outside of UM system of record).

Auth is only created if the member can be located using standard member search in UM system.

 | Create system functionality to create a new member on the fly.

If member is not found during intake, the UM system will allow a temporary member to be created to allow an auth to be started

Case must pend to member verification queue to follow predetermined workflow depending on payer-plan-LOB (workflow could be automated or manual)

Final case disposition dependent on if the member is eligible. If eligible, auth will continue for review. If not, the case must be updated based on the payer-plan-requirements.

***How will discrepancies between backend member data and temporary member be resolved?

 | Real-time eligibility check with payer via API

If member is not found during intake, the SYSTEM would leverage a payer eligibility API to perform a real-time check of member eligibility

API&rsquo;s allow for real-time access/ verification via API for confirming eligibility. This could be used for verifying the eligibility of an existing, ineligible member or for adding a new member.

 |  Decreased system complexity

 Abrasion with clients who desire the ability to create a member 

 |  Improved customer service and automation potential

 |  Aligns with interoperability standards

 Background

MATIS:

Original case: treatment end date is updated to the day before new assignment ; original assignment is marked as &ldquo;discontinued&rdquo; ; re-trigger auth

Option

 | Tool Tips

 | 
Modify Regimen

 | Request new supportive medication(s) or edit existing supportive medication(s) on the existing prior authorization.  Select this option if treatment dates of desired medication(s) overlap treatment dates of the existing prior authorization.

 | 
Submit New Cancer Regimen

 | Request new chemotherapy protocol(s) to replace existing chemotherapy protocol(s) already approved and on file.  Select this option if treatment dates of desired protocol(s) overlap treatment dates of the existing prior authorization.

 | 
Submit Reauthorization Request

 | Request an extension or additional time for use of a regimen that is already approved/in-use for patient.  Select this option if treatment end date needs to be pushed back (later).

 |

XRT & GMT

DX = PET Scan (?)

Chemo Cases with the following protocols:

Main = No Primary Assignment

Provider Data Issues Impacting Authorization &rarr; Claims Processing (added by Marisa)

Theme

 | Common Manifestations

 | Examples

 | Client‑Side Impact

 | Why This Happens

 | 
Place of Service (POS) & Site of Care Ambiguity

 | POS codes missing, defaulted, or not enforced at auth creation

Care setting inferred from provider record instead of explicitly captured

Single auth spanning services performed in different settings

 | Inpatient hospital vs outpatient hospital

Hospital outpatient vs physician office

In‑home infusion vs freestanding infusion center

CAR‑T or radiation support services performed at a different site than the primary treatment

 | Claims reject because POS on claim &ne; POS on auth

Claims require manual override or resubmission

Increased post‑service reconciliation and provider abrasion

 | POS treated as optional metadata instead of a required adjudication field

Intake assumes a 1:1 relationship between provider and site of care

 | 
Facility Type & Designation Not Explicitly Modeled

 | Facility designation missing or inferred

Facility classification not retained over time

 | Rural Health Clinic (RHC)

Critical Access Hospital (CAH)

Quality Care Center / Center of Excellence

Hospital‑based vs freestanding facility

 | Incorrect benefit application (professional vs facility billing logic)

Claims deny when facility designation on claim conflicts with auth context

Retroactive corrections when payer reclassifies the facility

 | Facility designation derived indirectly (address, TIN, contract) rather than stored as a first‑class attribute

No historical tracking when a facility&rsquo;s designation changes

 | 
Over‑Reliance on TINs to Infer Provider Relationships

 | TIN used as proxy for organizational structure

Provider relationships inferred instead of explicitly modeled

 | Multiple providers sharing a single TIN

One provider operating across multiple facilities under the same TIN

Facility and professional entities collapsing into one inferred &ldquo;provider&rdquo;

 | Auths tied to the wrong billing entity

Claims voided or rejected due to TIN mismatch

Inability to distinguish rendering vs billing vs requesting provider

 | TIN prioritized over explicit role modeling (requesting, rendering, servicing)

Address and site‑of‑care data treated as secondary

Provider systems (e.g., Salesforce) limited to one address per provider

 | 
Requesting vs Rendering vs Billing Provider Confusion

 | Provider roles not clearly distinguished at intake

Single &ldquo;treating provider&rdquo; used to represent multiple roles

 | Request comes from one provider, service rendered by another

Ancillary services (markers, infusions, imaging) performed by a different entity

Facility bills, but auth is tied to an individual clinician

 | Claims reject because billing NPI/TIN &ne; auth provider

Requirement to split or reissue auths post‑service

Increased client support effort and rework

 | Intake does not consistently capture provider role per service line

Provider data model assumes a single provider per authorization

 | 
Provider Attribute Granularity Insufficient for Claims Use

 | Provider selection lacks detail needed for claims matching

 | Specialty vs subspecialty not distinguished

Site‑specific address missing

Facility vs professional indicator unclear

Network tier or contract type not visible

 | Incorrect provider selected at intake

Claims reject even though &ldquo;a provider&rdquo; was selected

Loss of confidence in auth as a claims‑ready artifact

 | Intake UX optimized for speed, not claims fidelity

Backend data exists but is not surfaced or enforced

 |

Intro:

CHRONOS | Lucidchart

i'm thinking payer specific configuration should live in admin portal and will support both products.

TaT timers fall into different categories: compliance, informational, (potentially others)

For Compliance based timers, there are different levels of regulations (federal, state, or payer), we operate using the one with the shortest duration

Actions happen on a case, it may or may not impact TaT

Certain actions cause timers to be "paused" (e.g. requesting additional information pauses the case deadline timer for X days, or until a response is received)

Other actions cause a timer to be "completed"

Secondary actions can be triggered when a timer expires

Meeting notes

TAT Config files hosted in cosmos DB

Creating new timers and updating existing configurations will require engineering effort

Audit will be DB-based. It will be possible to see who made the change, when and implicitly extract what was changed from comparisons of new/previous state

Rollback - possible, will require engineering effort

Plan includes migration of current times from old to new system

No configuration management UI is in scope for Neal's team

If it needs to happen, suggestion is that it's placed in Admin portal

### Meeting Minutes - 02042026

Product Working Discussion

Date: February 4, 2026

Participants: Alison, Erik, Ashley, Venky, Rachel, Sandy, Keeley, Vika, Inna, Caitlin, Lauren

Summary

The team met to refine discuss product process including releases and governance. The team aligned on more agile, version-based framework with shorter release cycles vs large &ldquo;MVP&rdquo;. 

Discussion Points

Release Strategy & Versioning

Terminology: The team is moving away from "MVP" and agreed on using Product Release (targeting 6-8 weeks) and Version 1.0 (targeting Aug 2026).

Addressing Planning Weight: Alison expressed concerns that planning for an entire version at once is too heavy and resembles a waterfall approach. Agreement was made that work will be broken down into 6&ndash;8 week release cycles (3&ndash;4 sprints).

This allows for better collaboration with Ashley&rsquo;s team to vet requirements and ensures documentation is ready for PI planning.

Governance / Reporting

Governance should not create "duplicate work."

Sprint goals and planning outcomes from scrum teams will serve as the primary content for reporting.

Decisions: Decisions will present as 3 sizes, Small, Medium and Large.

o   Small items will be discussed at the product team level. Venky and Erik are to be informed.

o   Medium items will be discussed internally with the team. These items will require consent from Venky and Erik. The Executive Steering Committee will be informed.

o   Large items (major changes to scope, time, or cost) will require Executive Steering Committee review and decisioning.

A new Product Group series kicks off Feb 25th. This series is weekly, alternating Tue/Wed &ndash; only 30 minutes. 

Milestones

Phase milestones should be made available for the team to review.

Posting within NewUM Product Team space

PI Planning scheduled for Feb 23.

Next Executive Steering Committee session scheduled for Feb 24th

### Product Requirements Document (PRD)- TEMPLATE

Template guidelines:

This page should be used as the source of truth for high-level feature requirements. Details should be linked out from this page. 

We should remain flexible in this format - if a feature requires a different structure or additional sections, we are at liberty to do so. 

All templates should be reviewed & signed off by product manager. Additionally the product manager will specify which SMEs/Stakeholders should also sign off on the content (specifically the functional requirements & UX).

This template is meant to be collaborative, however we will have certain areas of responsibility:

Project Specifics: BA - R; Prod Mgt - A; UX - C

Goals & Objectives: BA - R; Prod Mgmt - R,A; UX - C

Background: BA - R; Prod Mgmt - R,A; UX - C

Functional Requirements: BA - R,A; Prod Mgmt - R,A; UX - C

User Stories: BA - R,A; Prod Mgmt - I; UX - C

UX: BA - C; Prod Mgmt - I; UX - R,A

Out of Scope: BA - R,A; Prod Mgmt - R,A; UX - R

Rules Repository

Goals & Business Objectives

This document outlines the requirements for a high-performance rules engine designed to support complex oncology workflows, manage multifaceted payer hierarchies, and ensure compliance with the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services (CMS) Interoperability and Prior Authorization Final Rule. Scope of the document are features for initial NewUM release (v1.0).

Key business objective for NewUM rules engine is to enable semi-technical (non-engineer) users to implement changes through a centralized administrative configuration file or interface, and those changes to be implemented without need to code changes and time-consuming SDLC.

Other primary goals is to increase visibility into configuration options and rule setup, decrease time-to-update and enable robust audit log.

reduce number of tickets/request to engineering

reduce rule change implementation time

rule error rate

rule autocompletion rate

Measurable outcomes:

TODO add success metrics and KPIs

Few suggestions:

reduce number of tickets/request to engineering

reduce rule change implementation time

rule error rate

rule autocompletion rate

Background & Current State

The industry has shifted toward the adoption of sophisticated, database-driven business rules engines (BRE) that externalize logic, allowing for near-real-time adjustments to clinical policies and payment models. The primary functional driver for a modernized rules engine is the elimination of the deployment bottleneck inherent in legacy code-based system.

Identified pain points and bottlenecks of OneUM:

OneUM system, which often relies upon hardcoded logic within core application repositories, is no longer sufficient to meet the agility requirements 

In current environments, simple modifications to a clinical policy or a payer-specific authorization requirement need to traverse the full software development lifecycle (SDLC), requiring code commits, regression testing, and production deployment

Links to research documentation

Assumptions to confirm - NewUM - Confluence

BRE-Rules-FULL 1 - Copy.xlsx

Rules Engine Edge Cases.docx

Data and Configuration Granularity (Draft v4)

Rules Engine - NewUM - Confluence

Behavior-Change Library (Draft).xlsx

Rules Prototyping: Discuss & Document Learnings - NewUM - Confluence

Standard Configuration Guide - Copy.xlsx

MATIS Payer Configuration Reference Guide - Copy.docx

Client Implementation Guide_ Draft_082025 - Copy.xlsm

In NewUM, General PA workflow does not need to be configurable on client level, and always comprises of following steps:

Case Intake

Case Entry (answers 5Ws)

Who ? (which patient PA request refers to and what providers are going to participate)

Why? (what is the diagnosis PA is requested for)

What? (what regimen and dosing is requested)

When? (when is the treatment taking place)

Where? (place of treatment)

Case Assignment (to OH processing queue)

Case Processing

Case Finalization

Outbound/Outputs

These steps remain true regardless of health plan, treatment type, etc. However, some forking in logic might be required within steps for individual payers.

General PA workflow is scope for v1 for NewUM, but in the future additional workflows will need to be supported (e.g. appeals etc.).

Example: Certain payers or health plans might require additional manual approval of processing results before final determination can be made.

In order to facilitate NewUM configurability requirements, we will introduce 2 different approaches to controlling product behavior without changing code:

Configurations - Simple parameters of the system that don&rsquo;t change often. Used for predefined options such as UI settings, TAT setting, Letter templates, simple Boolean or enumerated values setup, defaults, environment specific behavior etc.

Examples: letter templates, Member ID input formats used in patient search, messages that should be displayed for OOS drugs etc.

Rules - rule engine evaluates IF-THEN conditional logic at specified runtime and navigates system behavior based on conditions and drive process to expected business outcomes. Rules are executed on case level and are used when input parameters need to be evaluated to produce an dynamic output. Rules support complex scenarios, branching, prioritization, chaining and nesting of multiple rules. Rules are expected to be changed to accommodate evolving business needs of the client and OncoHealth, and changes may or may not be transparent to the health plan. 

Examples: Set Keytruda as non-preferred drug for health plan A, LoB=Commercial, when member has colon cancer, stage 4

Functional Requirements

note7d432589c79fAssumptions:

CONFIRMEDGreen  NewUM does not need to support distinct configuration options for Puerto Rico and mainland

Final determination list is global and final - does not need to be configurable. Depending on the health plan, some of determinations will not be available. Determination states should be configurable based on health plan and LOB. 

For example, if we are not performing network checks for a health plan, then we will not need the Denial - Admin determination and therefore would not want it to appear 

Term User refers to a Semi-technical OncoHealth employee with administrative access to configuration and rule management. Term Semi-technical is used to describe a person who is not an software engineer but possesses certain degree of computer literacy and is comfortable managing configurations and rules via structured-text languages.

Requirements marked with must haveRed  priority are required for initial version of NewUM, other features could be delayed in theory. Changes in priority are subjectable to change after engineering review.

Configuration and rules will be saved in NewUM database in form of JSON data type. Depending on solutioning details, configurations could be saved all in one JSON file or split in multiple JSON files. This will enable NewUM rules engine most direct and rapid access, ensuring best performance and reducing complexity by removing need to access other systems databases to fetch configurations and rules.

LLM generated example of a configuration of simple workflow with defined rules based on Case Management workflow.xlsx :

For the v1 of NewUM, we have envisioned a simple what-you-see-is-what-you-get editor. Ideally this editor would be placed as an UI option within NewUM and access to it would be limited. We suggest having a dedicated configuration administrator role for this, but this access can be managed dynamically using RBAC features.

Example of WYSWYG JSON editor

A default configuration and rule set will be created that can be used as a starting template for new payer tenants.

Create Rules engine

 | must haveRed  

 | Engine is able to receive inputs, evaluate them according to rule definition and produce an output

The engine should also support exception logic to handle anomalies in the workflow without requiring developer intervention.

Example: if the rule engine gets stuck for whatever reason and can&rsquo;t move case to any future state in X hours, assign case to manual review queue

Engine needs to be able to mediate control between rules engine and human users 

Block case editing while rules engine processing

UI should show &ldquo;please wait&rdquo; during rule execution

Rules engine releases control at pause states

Configurations

On a very high level, NewUM system must support general system configuration options on OH level that are valid for all payers and custom configurations on payer organization level defining validation and expected behavior for each step in the process workflow. Further granulation is possible on LoB, Plan Type and Employer Group level.

For v1 rule engine will need to accommodate only Commercial and Medicare LoBs

Examples: Configuration Repository 

This means that users need to be able to manage following configurations:

 | 
General system configurations 

 | must haveRed  

 | Business rules related settings defined on OH level that are valid for all payers

These configurations apply to all health plans utilizing NewUM software to support their PA workflows.

Suggested categories: Configuration and rules categories  

This is the highest level configuration, and as a rule, any lower level configuration overrides it

 | Example: 

OH&rsquo;s setting allows treatment start date to be (today)-1month

BCBSKA&rsquo;s setting allows treatment start date to be (today)-2months

When rule engine evaluates treatment start date validity, it always looks for a lowest possible level configuration, meaning that for BCBSKA&rsquo;s members allowed treatment start date is (today)-2months

 | 
Payer specific configuration

 | must haveRed  

 | Payer specific configuration and behavior feature flags

Business rules related settings

These can be drilled down further to LoB level->Product line level->Employer group level

Suggested categories: Configuration and rules categories 

 |  | 
Configurations are hierarchical and hierarchy can be configured 

 | must haveRed    

 | Users need to be able to configure hierarchy of level (parent-child relationships)

Lowest level configuration always takes precedence

Rules

Rules and rule engine components should ideally be decoupled from the user interface and the primary case management database. It should operate by receiving a structured data packet of input parameters and evaluating parameters against a repository of active rules.

Rules evaluate conditional logic at triggering event and impact system behavior based on defined executable outcomes. Akin to programable business logic but with no code.

Rules are triggered on specified step of the workflow (i.e. Case Entry) and can be triggered on a specific event within a step (i.e. when UI is loaded, when certain value is entered, when certain button like &ldquo;submit&rdquo; is clicked&hellip;) 

Example: 

Step: CaseEntry
Event: OnSubmit
if PARAMETER1 = true do ACTION1 

 Rules Repository 

 | 
Rule engine has to be able to accept input parameter package

 | must haveRed  

 | Please note: following list of input parameters may vary depending on the step of the workflow and is not final!

Individual rules can have distinct input parameters.

Inputs:

Case State

Workflow step, event, current case status

Payer

Payer Name, Parent Organization, Payer IDs

Member

First Name, Last Name, DOB, ID, State of Residence, Eligibility record ID

Provider

Ordering provider NPI, NPI type, State of Residence (practicing location) , network (INN/OON),  

Performing/Servicing provider NPI, NPI type, State of Residence (practicing location) , network (INN/OON),  

Treatment details

Treatment type, regimen, medication codes, amount, dosage&hellip;

Flags: ancillary, generic/brand, step therapy&hellip;almost all elements within MDL or PDL

Configuration parameters

Various values related to step or business rule

 |  | 
Rule engine has to enable users to determine when rule should be triggered

 | must haveRed  

 | Need to be able to define step in which is rule to be executed (e.g. on Case Entry)

Need to be able to define event within step on which is rule to be executed (e.g. onValueChange, onSubmit, onEdit&hellip;)

Multiple rules can be linked and nested with logical operators (AND, OR&hellip;)

 |  | 
Rule engine has to be able to evaluate inputs according to specification defined by user

 | must haveRed  

 | Must support conditional logic (and, or, xor)  that validates input parameters and executes defined actions (if-then, case, not, elseif &hellip;)

Results of execution of one rule can be used as input parameter for following rule

 |  | 
Rule engine has to support action execution

 | must haveRed  

 | Support execution of expected outcomes. 

Support action execution. 

Suggested categories:Configuration and rules categories  , each category is tied to action rule engine should be able to execute

while triggers and conditions are highly configurable, actions that rule engine can execute are limited to pre defined list based on rule categories. Adding new actions/categories is possible but it will require engineering effort. 

Display errors or informative messages

See use cases in https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5127569409/Rules+and+configurations+functional+specification#Rule-engine-must-be-able-to-gracefully-handle-when-rule-cannot-be-executed  for example behavior

When evaluating regime, rules can be executed on drug level

Individualizing the approval or denial for specific drugs within a multi-drug regimen, rather than rejecting the entire case.

 |  | 
Rule engine must be able to gracefully handle when rule cannot be executed

 | must haveRed    

 | Rules can be categorized (or tiered)

Tier 1 - outcome (result) of the rule execution is required for process to proceed. If rule cannot be executed (e.g. due to missing inputs) or fails to complete (e.g. cannot complete required action) , a critical error is logged and thrown, and case cannot proceed.

Tier 2 - outcome of the rule execution is not required to proceed. If rule cannot be executed (e.g. due to missing inputs) or fails to complete (e.g. cannot complete required action) , a non-critical error is logged and displayed to end-user (CSR, CSS, provider&hellip;) asking them to explicitly confirm that they with to proceed.

Tier 3 - outcome of the rule execution is not required to proceed. If rule cannot be executed (e.g. due to missing inputs) or fails to complete (e.g. cannot complete required action) , a non-critical error is logged, nothing is displayed to end-user (CSR, CSS, provider&hellip;) and case is allowed to proceed.

 |  | 
Rule grain ranking  has to be configurable on payer level.

 | must haveRed    

 | Default configuration:

Order

 | Grain Level

 | Typical Use Case

 | Configuration Context

 | 
Highest

 | Global

 | Industry standards

 | OH business driven rules that can be applied to any payer that doesn&rsquo;t require customization

 | 
 | Payer Parent

 | Federal Regulatory Compliance

 | Foundational HIPAA and standard TAT rules

 | 
 | Payer Organization

 | Broad Network Policies

 | Default medical necessity criteria

 | 
 | Line of Business (LOB)

 | Medicare vs. Medicaid vs. Commercial

 | Regulatory variations (e.g., Medicare Advantage)

 | 
 | Plan Type / Product

 | HMO vs. PPO Benefit Design

 | Specific patient cost-sharing and referral logic

 | 
Lowest

 | Employer Group

 | Custom Negotiated Benefits

 | Special drug formulary or site-of-care rules

 | 
 |  | 
 Rule engine has to support rule grain ranking.

 | PENDING CONFIRMATION  

 | The rules engine must support a grain ranking inheritance model that allows for the definition of "coarse-grain" rules at a high level while permitting "fine-grain" overrides at the local level.

Rules engine logic must prioritize the lowest level grain available. I.e. if a rule for a specific chemotherapy drug is defined at both the Line of Business (Commercial) level and the Employer Group (General Motors) level, the engine must execute the Employer Group rule

 Even tho some configuration level can be shared (e.g. LoBs), each configuration/rule should be tied to specific payer org they apply to

 |  | 
Rules engine needs to support Effective Dating

 | must haveRed    

 | (Valid from and Valid to metadata parameters)

This will enable more flexibility in planning by enabling of scheduled activation ad deactivation of rules vs &ldquo;live changes&rdquo; 

Ideally, this would also automatically deprecate older version of the rule

Business suggests this as &ldquo;must have&rdquo;, open to eng. pushback

Audit & Rollback

 | 
All configurations have to be versioned and changes logged

 | must haveRed  

 | The system must maintain a 100% audit trail of all changes. Every modification to a configuration or rule must generate a new version number and store metadata about the change (who made the change, when and what was changed)

All changes over configuration need to be logged for auditing

Scope of the audit can be only configuration that are technically within NewUM. This means that we probably won't be able to explicitly audit TAT, letters and payer level configuration from Admin portal, and requirement to audit those should be coordinated with teams that are owning them.

 |  | 
Collect change metadata

 | should haveYellow  

 | for v2

Enhance config management UI: Enable OH configuration admin to enter rational for change,  reference ticket number on link to change log

 |  | 
All rules have to be versioned and changes logged

 | must haveRed  

 | The system must maintain a 100% audit trail of all changes. Every modification to a configuration or rule must generate a new version number and store metadata about the change (who made the change, when and what was changed)

All changes over rules need to be logged for auditing

 |  | 
Rule execution has to be logged on case level.

 | must haveRed    

 | What rule, with what parameters and with what results has been executed for each case.

 |  | 
Configuration updates have  to be reversable (rollback)

 | must haveRed  

 | OH needs capability to instantly revert to a previous rule version if an issue is detected

This feature should have limited accessibility (e.g. admin only)

When rolling back, reason for rollback must be provided

 |  | 
Rollback Case

 | must haveRed  

 | OH need capability to revert case to a previous state if an issue is detected

This feature should have limited accessibility (e.g. admin only)

When rolling back, reason for rollback must be provided

When rolling back, case assignee is notified

 |  | 
Rule updates have  to be reversable (rollback)

 | must haveRed    

 | OH admin needs capability to instantly revert to a previous rule version if an issue is detected

Roll back to previous good state with full audit trail

Soft deletes maintain audit history

This feature should have limited accessibility (e.g. admin only)

When rolling back, reason for rollback must be provided

Record rollback action itself for compliance

Please note, scope of this requirement is to roll back only configuration and rule definitions, not the actual PA case.

 | nice to haveBlue

OH Admin has access to all logs

Error handling

 | 
Error handling

 | must haveRed  

 | Rules engine has to be able to resolve conflicting rules triggering

Specific logic for this TBD, see questions in notes

Errors need to be tiered

Hard-stop

Warnings

Informational

 | REQUIRES DISCUSSION

Tie-breaker logic:

What if multiple rules at the same grain and hierarchy match? Last updated takes precedence?

What if rules produce conflicting actions (e.g., one allows, one denies)?

There should be automated test in place to prevent such rules from becoming active and coming to production

 | 
Error displaying

 | should haveYellow  

 | System needs to be able to distinguish between business errors and technical errors

Example rule: If member is INN and older than 18 years allow user to submit case 

Business error: member is <18 years old

Technical error: member&rsquo;s age could not be fetched, and rule can&rsquo;t make a determination

Rules engine has to be able to raise errors to user

Error messages should be user friendly and understandable for business users of the NewUM

Error messages need to be configurable 

 |  | 
Error logging

 | must haveRed  

 | System needs robust error logging for technical troubleshooting

 |  | 
Logs visibly

 | should haveYellow    

 | Read-only Logs should be available to non-technical persons within OH in order to troubleshoot cases

 |  | 
Testing & Validation

 | 
Create automated test

 | should haveYellow  

 | The rules engine must include a dedicated "Test Harness" to validate changes before they are promoted to production. This must allow users to "Test Rule" functionality by mocking inputs, comparing outputs and determinism checks 

Rules and configuration should be covered by batch tests that will test all rules en-masse to identify potential conflicts between rules or performance bottlenecks.

 |  | 
Create testing data sets

 | nice to haveBlue    

 | Test data set should provide real-looking data for all potential combinations of input parameters and expected outcomes

Must not contain PHI or PII

 |  | 
Regression test

 | nice to haveBlue    

 | Rules configuration and engine should be covered with regression tests that are run on staging environment before changes are implemented on production to ensure that introduced changes have not had effect on the logic and behavior of the system beyond the scope of change 

Please note, it might be not possible to cover all the rules and combinations with automated tests, especially when you take into account that OH configuration admin will be able to make changes on the fly without requiring engineering effort and those changes in theory could happen more often, so regression test suite update could lag behind current configurations.

 |  |

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Description (Use Case Format)

 | Notes

 | 
Select Main Regimen from Regimen Library

 | US 1: Enter Chemotherapy Treatment and Dosing for Prior Authorization

Primary Actors

CRS (OncoHealth staff)

Provider office staff

Health plan user

Supporting Actors / Systems

Admin Portal (Regimen Library, Master Drug Library, Payer Drug Library, Rules)

Eligibility Service

Rules Engine / Auto-Determination Logic

PBM / Formulary Data (pharmacy drugs)

User Goal: To enter a complete and clinically valid chemotherapy treatment request - including regimen, drugs, dosing, and payer-specific constraints - so that the prior authorization can be evaluated, automated where possible, and routed correctly.

Trigger: User initiates chemotherapy treatment entry after completing patient identification and diagnosis selection.

Preconditions

User is authenticated and authorized to submit a PA.

Member eligibility have been identified.

Diagnosis (ICD-10) and Diagnosis Group have been captured.

Treatment type is identified as Chemotherapy.

Admin Portal clinical and payer configuration data is available.

Postconditions

Success: Chemotherapy treatment data is saved to the case, including:

Selected main regimen or custom regimen

Drug records (main and ancillary)

Dosing details (medical and pharmacy)

Benefit type and payer drug statuses

Auto-approval status is set where rules allow.

Case proceeds to next workflow state (submission, determination, or review).

Failure: Case remains in intake state with validation errors clearly indicated:

No incomplete or invalid treatment data is persisted.

Main Success Scenario (Happy Path)

User searches and selects a main regimen from the Regimen Library.

System limits available regimens to those associated with the Diagnosis Group.

System prepopulates dosing tables using regimen defaults.

User reviews and edits dosing within allowed guardrails.

System applies payer drug configuration (PA, OOS, benefit type).

System applies non-preferred drug and formulary rules.

System evaluates auto-approval eligibility for main regimen and ancillary drugs.

Treatment entry is saved to the case.

Alternate / Extension Flows

Custom Regimen Entry; User creates a custom regimen; system validates against existing regimens and pends for auto-rules.

Ancillary-Only Request: User submits a request containing only ancillary drugs.

Crossover Drug Handling: User selects and may change benefit type; system revalidates dosing and status.

Non-Preferred Drug Handling: User switches to preferred drugs or provides a clinical exception reason.

Business Rules

Regimen selection is filtered by Diagnosis Group, not cancer stage.

Custom regimens always pend for auto-rules.

Dosing guardrails enforce Admin Portal&ndash;configured limits.

Non-preferred and formulary rules override indication-based auto-approval.

Medical and pharmacy drugs are evaluated together as a single protocol.

note1dfaf36f9115Height and weight are required for medical dosing calculations.

Brand vs generic selection impacts downstream identifiers and payer rules.

System must track drug changes for financial impact reporting.

Height and weight are required for medical dosing calculations.

Brand vs generic selection impacts downstream identifiers and payer rules.

 | Regimens are the preferred entry path for chemo

Regimens are curated in Admin Portal and associated with Diagnosis Groups

Regimen search supports fuzzy search (brand/generic/drug name)

Regimen search uses Diagnosis Group, not cancer stage (explicit decision to avoid protocol bloat)

Regimen selection pre-populates dosing table with default values

 | 
Allow Custom Regimens

 | Custom regimens are allowed but discouraged

Custom regimens require selecting individual drugs from Master Drug Library

Dosing table starts blank (no defaults)

Same dosing guardrails apply as standard regimens

System checks if an identical regimen already exists and forces reuse if found

CRS users can create custom regimens immediately; providers must search regimens first

 | 
Select Ancillary Drugs

 | Drugs are classified as Main / Ancillary / Main+Ancillary in Master Drug Library

Ancillary drugs are approved and reviewed in the context of the entire chemo protocol

Ancillary drug eligibility can be influenced by regimen attributes (e.g., febrile neutropenia risk, myelosuppression risk)

Ancillary drugs may be added during initial entry or later (e.g., symptom management)

 | 
Capture Basic Dosing Details

 | Dosing table pre-populated from regimen defaults

Users can edit dose, units, frequency, cycles, days per cycle

Guardrails enforce valid values based on Admin Portal data

Medical drugs require height & weight for dose calculations

Pharmacy drugs restrict selectable strength/form/route

Support for loading doses, ramp-ups, duplicate strength combinations

 | 
Apply Payer Drug Configurations

 | Payer Drug Library applies in scope / out of scope / PA required / PA exempt per drug

Configuration differs by benefit type (medical vs pharmacy vs crossover)

Drug status (pending, PA exempt, out of scope) is derived from payer configuration

Configuration directly affects workflow, routing, and auth file outputs

 | 
Apply Payer Non-Preferred Drug Rules

 | Non-preferred (step therapy) rules apply to chemo drugs

Rules may be mandatory or voluntary

Non-preferred rules override &ldquo;auto-approve by indication&rdquo;

Rules evaluated at individual drug line level

System must capture exceptions and support denial logic if rules are not met

 | 
Apply Formulary Configurations

 | Pharmacy drugs may be governed by PBM formularies

&ldquo;Per formulary&rdquo; status pulls PA, quantity, and coverage logic from PBM files

Payer configuration can override formulary when needed (trump logic)

Formulary logic applies only to pharmacy benefit, not medical

 | 
Auto Approve Main Regimen on Indication Only

 | Regimens can be flagged as auto-approvable by indication

Auto-approval applies when diagnosis group matches and no exceptions exist

Auto-approval is overridden by non-preferred rules or other constraints

Meaning: approval without full clinical review, not &ldquo;no validation&rdquo;

 | 
Auto approve ancillary Drugs

 | Ancillary drug approval can be driven by regimen attributes (risk levels)

Certain ancillary drugs may auto-approve based on regimen-level signals

Auto-approval logic is rule-driven and Admin-Portal-backed

Support Renewal Case Requests

 | UC 2: Submit Renewal Request for Previously Approved Chemotherapy Treatment

Primary Actors

CRS (OncoHealth staff)

Provider office staffHealt

h plan user

Supporting Actors / Systems

Admin Portal (clinical and payer configurations)

Eligibility Service

Rules Engine / Auto-Determination Logic

Historical Case Repository

User Goal: To renew a previously approved chemotherapy treatment efficiently by reusing prior treatment data, minimizing re-entry, and enabling automated approval when no clinical changes exist.

Trigger: User initiates a renewal request for chemotherapy treatment.

Preconditions

User is authenticated and authorized.

Patient has at least one previously approved chemotherapy case.

Prior approved case has a treatment end date within 30 days of the new requested start date.

Current eligibility is available.

Postconditions

Success: Renewal case is created and linked to the prior approved case: 

Treatment and provider details are prepopulated.

Renewal is auto-approved where rules allow or routed for review.

Case advances to determination or completion.

Failure: Renewal cannot proceed due to eligibility, timing, or validation issues:

User is prompted to submit a new intake if renewal criteria are not met.

Main Success Scenario (Happy Path)

System displays eligible previously approved chemotherapy cases.

User selects a prior case to renew.

System prepopulates treatment, dosing, and provider details.

User attests that treatment is working and unchanged.

System reapplies payer, non-preferred, and formulary rules.

System evaluates renewal auto-approval criteria.

Renewal case is approved or routed appropriately.

Alternate / Extension Flows

Modified Renewal: User edits dosing or drugs; system treats renewal as a modified request and re-evaluates rules.

Ancillary-Only Renewal: User renews ancillary drugs linked to a prior main regimen.

Configuration Change Impact: Updated payer or formulary rules cause renewal to pend for review.

Business Rules

Renewal eligibility is limited to cases within 30 days of prior treatment end date ( tbdRed subject to configuration?)

Auto-approval applies only when no material changes exist.

Payer and formulary rules are re-evaluated at time of renewal.

Historical approval does not guarantee renewal approval.

notee93f089a778bRenewal cases must maintain a reference to the prior case for audit and reporting.

Deviations from prior approval must be clearly indicated to reviewers.

Renewal logic is designed to reduce CRS and clinical workload without bypassing rules.

### Work Queues Product Requirements Document

This is a working document related to the queuing structures in NewUM.

Goals & Business Objectives

Define the necessary work queues within NewUM to support appropriate case and workforce management.

✅ Need for structured queues that align to case states

&ldquo;Queues should&hellip; align with case states.&rdquo;
&ldquo;Single queue by phase&hellip; attribute-based routing.&rdquo;

✅ Visibility for operators

Users must &ldquo;easily view the volume of cases.&rdquo;
Real-time dashboard with volume, state, staffing, TAT risk.

✅ Routing rules to manage case workflow

Detailed routing rules by intake type, clinical type, exception.
Dynamic routing based on case attributes + score-based prioritization.

✅ Capacity + workforce management awareness

WIP limits, surge handling.
Capacity forecasting, supply-demand alignment, skill-based assignment.

✅ Ability to support sub-queues / queue differentiation

Intake exception queues, pediatric, OOS, etc.
Sub-queues based on attributes (Out of Scope, Mixed OOS, NMI).
Ability to filter queues to manage workload and dynamically adjust views.

✅ Structure must capture/prevent lost and stuck cases

Queue definitions aim to ensure cases move and don&rsquo;t get stuck.
Backstop validation + &ldquo;Identify fallouts.&rdquo;

✅ Queue sequencing to support the full case lifecycle
Intake &rarr; Exceptions &rarr; Clinical &rarr; MD &rarr; P2P &rarr; Notifications &rarr; Completed
Opportunity to manage capacity based on standard timing and volumes (ie weekend anticipated volumes due to TAT).
Considerations for holding queues (NMI, awaiting P2P)

✅ Support for queue sorting/prioritization based on case attributes

Case attributes assigned and utilized to appropriate route and triage case priority.
Scoring system to capture case priority.

✅ Analytics and Process tracking

Ability to measure in real-time the number of cases in queue to provide

Background & Current State

A work‑queue is a virtual holding area of homogeneous work items that share:

Purpose (e.g., &ldquo;Clinical RN Review&mdash;Radiation Oncology&rdquo;)

Routing rules (which cases can land here)

Owner role(s) (who works it: Intake, RN, MD/Medical Director, Letters, Appeals)

SLA/priority (stat vs standard; parity-sensitive, state-specific rules)

Sort order (how items are ranked inside the queue)

State transitions (what happens after completion or timeout)

Capacity controls (WIP limits, auto-balancing, surge handling)

What are the standards in the UM industry?

Multiple queues are used to group work in similar &lsquo;states&rsquo; and user skilling can be used to determine work assignment. 

Work list driven case selection relies on the user to &ldquo;pull&rdquo; cases from one or many queues based on either scoring or independent decision making (current state for MATIS and SmartUM).

Work assignment via &ldquo;push&rdquo; model relies on the system to prioritize and serve-up a case to the user based on the alignment of their skills with the case attributes.

Recommended approach for V1:

Cases should be assigned (by the system based on triggers) to a queue, not to an individual user

Maintain &ldquo;pull&rdquo; model with opportunity for scoring to be presented to users

Recommended case attributes

&bull;	Case Priority: Classify as urgent or standard.
&bull;	Line of Business: Identify whether the case is Medicare, Medicaid, or commercial.
&bull;	Client: Specify which client the case pertains to.
&bull;	Request Type: Categorize by product type&mdash;e.g., chemo, GMT, XRT.
&bull;	TAT Status: Track time remaining on the clock and original case received time.
&bull;	Appeal Flag: Mark if the case is an appeal.
&bull;	Diagnosis/clinical tracks (HCC cat)
&bull;	Special workflows: Define based on attributes:

o	Out of Scope: Clinical code, provider, or medication not covered.
o	Mixed Out of Scope: Some parts in scope, others not.
o	Missing Info (NMI): Cases requiring further information.

Intake queues to manage cases entering the system

Fax intake

Faxed cases received but not yet processed (unique fax phone numbers allows for sorting of cases for SLA management)

Faxed cases pre-OCR to scrape basic case details

OCR Process/queue &ndash; capture Health Plan/Payer, Tracking Number to route to appropriate next step

Faxed cases post-OCR pending routing to holding queue for AI parsing (only payers allowing AI/automation)

Faxed cases post-OCR pending routing to holding queue for manual intake review (payers NOT allowing AI/automation)

Faxed cases post-OCR unable to OCR needing manual review (i.e. handwritten)

Anterior Fax Extraction &ndash; parse details from case to create new case vs attach to existing

Post-Anterior fax for case creation (manual vs automated process)

Post-Anterior fax for document attachment (manual vs automated process)

Email queue to manage cases that are not yet in the system

***Need more exploration on this intake stream***

Intake holding &ndash; holding space for cases without attached clinicals to allow for delayed upload

#### [DRAFT] Configuration Guide

13falsenonelisttrueIntroduction

This guide provides the essential technical framework required to configure newUM system for payer specific operational environment. This document is designed to lead you through initial setup, parameter tuning, and verification in a logical, step-by-step progression.

It is highly recommended that you perform these configurations in a staged environment prior to deploying them into production.

For full understanding and big picture of configuration and rules, please see Rules and configurations functional specification 

Practical implementation

Access to configuration management will be limited to OH configuration admin. 

Configuration&Rules repository is going to be a structured file (JSON) saved to data store and managed by config API. 

There will be very basic UI that will allow OH config admin to pull file from data store, view it, make updates (text editor level complexity), and save updated file back to data store. 

On file save, automatic test will trigger to validate updated file. Automatic test harness will also support testing of multiple interdependent files.

Configuration admin will have a dedicated test harness available to initiate robust configuration & rules testing.

Hierarchy level setup

Configurations and rules engine supports a hierarchical inheritance model that allows for the definition of "coarse-grain" rules at a high level while permitting "fine-grain" overrides at the local level. 

Rules engine logic prioritizes the lowest level grain available when executing rules. I.e. if a rule for a specific chemotherapy drug is defined at both the Line of Business (Commercial) level and the Employer Group (General Motors) level, the engine must execute the Employer Group rule.

Same approach is valid for configurations: if there is a configuration for MemberID format being varchar on payer level, and configuration on LoB level for the same payer that says that for LoB=Medicare MemberID format must be integer with 10 characters max, on cases where LoB selected is Medicare should enforce configuration from LoB level

Hierarchy can be set up distinctly for each payer to facilitate differing business requirements. How you decide to set up hierarchy will have an effect on system configurations and rule execution.

Default setting:

Order

 |

 |

 |

 | Payer Organization

 |

Configurations

Configuration parameters are static at runtime and don&rsquo;t change based on conditional logic. They are used to manage expected behavior of predefined options such as UI settings, simple Boolean or enumerated values setup, defaults, environment specific behavior etc. There are multiple types of configurations:

Configuration Type

 | Description

 | 
General

 | General - Configuration on OH level, these configuration apply for all payers. 

This is the highest level configuration, and as a rule, any lower level configuration with the same name overrides it

 | 
Workload

 | General - configuration of OH case assignment queues and linking employees to queue

 | 
Payer

 | Payer specific configuration and behavior feature flags

Business rules related settings

These can be drilled down further to LoB level->Product line level->Employer group level

 | 
UI configuration

 | UI configurations, configuration record name must correspond to interface name configuration refers to.

 | 
Outcomes (Determinations)

 | Payer related - Configuration related to outcomes of case processing, e.g. determinations (approval, denial, partial approval etc.)

 | 
TAT 

 | Payer related - Configuration of TAT calculation settings

 | 
Letters

Rules 

Rule engine evaluates IF-THEN conditional logic at runtime and changes behavior based on conditions and defined expected outcomes. Used whenever inputs need to be dynamically evaluated to produce an output, supports complex scenarios, branching, prioritization, chaining and nesting of multiple rules.

Rules are always defined for a specific payer.

Rule execution setup

When rule is to be triggered is defined by the workflow, step in workflow and event(s) within that step.

Workflows & Steps

Workflow setting will tell rule engine what steps exist in the workflow, their order, allowed transitions, define starting step, define final steps and to which workflow applies to which business process supported by NewUM (Prior authorizations (PA), appeals, etc.)

For v1, we're developing only prior authorization (PA) workflow, but should construct underlying functionality so that it can be scaled to additional business processes with individual workflows in the future.

Events

An event is essentially a signal that "something has happened." Instead of following a rigid, line-by-line script, rule engine will &ldquo;listen&rdquo; for these triggers and then executing specific code (event handlers) in response

Event

 | Description

 | 
submit

 | form (UI) event - sending data

 | 
change

 | form (UI) event - value of the input field changed (e.g. changing a dropdown or checkbox)

 | 
focus/blur

 | form (UI) event - clicking into or out of a input field

 | 
load

 | page, form or element finish loading

 | 
unload

 | page, form or element closing

 | 
error

 | error is thrown to FE

 | 
requestSent

 | HTTP event

 | 
responseReceived

 | HTTP event

 | 
timeout

 | HTTP event - server timeout

#### [DRAFT] Qronos integration and TAT configuration

Goals & Business Objectives

Enable NewUM to utilize Qronos subsystem for TaT calculations on case level. Depending on the business needs, NewUM should be able to communicate which timer configuration to use, initiate a start of the TaT timer, pause timer, resume timer and end time. 

NewUM should be able to fetch current TaT values for cases from Qronos

Background & Current state

TaT timers fall into different categories: compliance, informational, (potentially others)

For Compliance based timers, there are different levels of regulations (federal, state, or payer), we operate using the one with the shortest duration

Actions happen on a case, it may or may not impact TaT - we need to develop logic and rules to regulate that

Certain actions cause timers to be "paused" (e.g. requesting additional information pauses the case deadline timer for X days, or until a response is received)

Other actions cause a timer to be "completed"

Secondary actions can be triggered when a timer expires

NewUM will not have it&rsquo;s own logic for TaT calculation, instead it will used a 3rd party system called Qronos.

Qronos development plan includes migration of current times from old to new system

Current TAT config requirements (extracted from TAT tab in Client Implementation Guide_ Draft_082025 - Copy.xlsm )

Out of Scope

Audit of Qronos configurations - Qronos audit will be DB-based. It will be possible to see who made the change, when and implicitly extract what was changed from comparisons of new/previous state

Rollback - will be possible, will require engineering effort from Qronos team.

Migration of existing timers from current system - task will be done by Qronos team

i'm thinking payer specific configuration should live in admin portal and will support both products.

I can go into more detail at the meeting but the core of it is that Chronos (new TaT engine) will send the tat results to a servicebus queue but NewUM is responsible for digesting the results

#### [DRAFT]Testing

Rough draft of testing strategy and test cases:

Enable testing of individual config files

Enable testing of entire configuration (all files)

Exclude from testing:

any record that has status=inactive

any configuration that has ValidTo date < today

any rule or ruleset that has ValidTo date < today

draft test cases:

check do all repositories exist

check are all input parameters referenced in conditions available 

e.g. if rule expects value from configuration that is inactive or not set

NFR:

Must not contain PHI or PII

It would be really really useful to be able to de-identify cases on the fly as well. Not sure what would be involved with that, but Michal would be the one to ask on  the Newfire side. Right now OncoHealth has serious issues with foreign developers being unable to replicate bugs because of PHI access issues.

Background & Current State

TBD

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Description

 | Notes

 | 
Give users the ability to create a custom regimen on case entry

 | System shall provide a Custom Regimen path within chemotherapy workflow

Custom Regimen is defined by user-selected drugs (no predefined regimen selection)

User does not enter a regimen name; regimen is system-designated as &ldquo;Custom&rdquo;

Custom Regimen exists only within the case context

Internal users may initiate at any point

 External users may initiate only when no matching regimen is found or clinical trial is selected

 | Case-level construct only

 | 
Users must enter dosing information for the regimen

 | Dosing values are required for each drug in the Custom Regimen

Dosing is captured at the drug level

Case cannot proceed without required dosing values

Dosing guardrails applied to standard regimens must also apply here

Dosing data is stored as part of the case snapshot

 | Validation required prior to submission

 | 
Restrict custom regimen creation for external users to only after searching

 | External users must attempt to locate a standard regimen first

Custom Regimen path becomes available only if no matching regimen is found

Custom Regimen path is also allowed when clinical trial is selected

Internal users are not subject to this restriction

 | Role-based enforcement

 | 
System should check against the drugs in the custom regimen to see if there are existing regimens for that diagnosis

 | After drugs are entered, system shall compare drug set against existing regimens for the selected diagnosis

Matching logic based on configured drug equivalence rules

If matches are found, system shall present matching regimens

User may switch to a matched regimen or remain with Custom Regimen

 | Advisory comparison (not hard stop)

 | 
Custom regimens should always pend for auto-rules

 | If any drug in the Custom Regimen is PA-required for the payer, auto-determination shall be bypassed

Case shall pend for clinical review

Presence of Custom Regimen with PA-required drug overrides automation logic

 | Conditional pend rule based on payer drug status

 | 
Custom regimens should not save to regimen library, but be available for operational reporting purposes

 | Custom Regimens shall not be persisted to the Regimen Library

Regimen data (drugs + dosing) shall be stored as a case-level snapshot

Custom Regimen data shall be included in operational reporting datasets

Regimen snapshot must persist across post-denial and renewal workflows

 | No library persistence; reporting required

 |
