Units

 | Identifies the dose unit used for the drug and determines the calculation pathway

 | MedicalGreen

 

 | MDL: Dose Units

 | Enum (DDL)

 | RequiredRed

 | default :  blank

 

Editable. Drop Down Logic:

1. For Dose Drop Down: The allowed Units values should be inferred based on the associated Billable UOM (BUM) for the drug (Capture Basic Dosing Details )

1.1. Carboplatin is a defined exception. In addition to the standard Units derived from its Billable UOM, the Units dropdown should also include: Area Under Curve 1.5, Area Under Curve 2, Area Under Curve 3, Area Under Curve 4, Area Under Curve 5, Area Under Curve 6, Area Under Curve 7

3. The Units dropdown should always include &ldquo;Unknown&rdquo; as a selectable option.

 | Unit selection determines whether Allowed Dose is calculated (mg/kg, mg/m&sup2;, etc.) or equals Dosage (fixed units).

tbdRed validate if this mapping logic applies to Ancillary drugs as well/

Source of allowed Units values: should be determined based on the drug&rsquo;s associated Billable Unit of Measure (Billable UOM).

Billable UOM to Units mapping:
1. If Billable UOM = mg. Allowed Units:
mg, g, g/kg, mcg, mcg/kg, mcg/m2, mg/kg, mg/m2, g/m2

2. If Billable UOM = mcg. Allowed Units:mg, g, g/kg, mcg, mcg/kg, mcg/m2, mg/kg, mg/m2, g/m2

3.If Billable UOM = mCi. Allowed Units:mCi

4. If Billable UOM = IU. Allowed Units:IU/kg, IU/m2

5. If Billable UOM = Units. Allowed Units:International Unit, million units, million units/kg, units, units/kg, units/m2

6. If Billable UOM = Infusion. Allowed Units: Infusion

7. If Billable UOM = million Units. Allowed Units:
International Unit, million units, million units/kg, units, units/kg, units/m2

 | 
Allowed Dose

 | Calculated patient-specific dose

 | MedicalGreen

 | System calculation 

 | Decimal (calculated; 2 decimals)

 | calculatedGreen

 | Calculated automatically. Not editable. Formula:

1. If Units = Fixed units (mg, g, mcg), then  Allowed Dose = Dosage

2.  If Units = Carboplatin AUC (1.5&ndash;7), then Allowed Dose = Dosage
- Weight-based units (mg/kg, mcg/kg, g/kg) &rarr; Allowed Dose = Dosage &times; Weight (kg)

3. If Units = BSA-based units (mg/m&sup2;, g/m&sup2;, IU/m&sup2;, units/m&sup2;) &rarr; Allowed Dose = Dosage &times; BSA where BSA = &radic;(Height [cm] &times; Weight [kg] / 3600). 

noteb33cdf9b-8839-4c3a-8edb-9e6c4abe9a7fAllowed Dose must be expressed in the drug&rsquo;s Billable UOM (apply mg/mcg/g conversions as needed).
Rounding: 2 decimal places using the thousandths rule.

Allowed Dose must be expressed in the drug&rsquo;s Billable UOM (apply mg/mcg/g conversions as needed).
Rounding: 2 decimal places using the thousandths rule.

 |  
Rule: Recalculate Allowed Dose if Weight changes (for weight-based units), Height or Weight changes (for BSA-based units)

 | 
Max Billing Units/Auth

 | Calculated maximum medical authorization quantity expressed in billing units.

 | MedicalGreen

 | System calculation

 | Decimal (calculated; 2 decimals)

 | calculatedGreen

 | Auto-calculated for all medical drugs. 
Not editable.
Is blank if calculation cannot be performed

 | Formula: (Allowed Dose &times; Adm Per Day &times; Adm Days Per Cycle &times; Cycles) &divide; CMU BU (from Admin Portal). Cycles derivation: Duration per AP/Cycle in Days, rounded up to next whole number. 
Rounding: 2 decimals per standard thousandths rule. Rule: trigger alert if edited dosing exceeds Max BU/duration configured in Admin Portal.

 | 
Strength

 | Captures the selected pharmacy drug strength used for downstream pharmacy dosing (e.g., quantity) and drug identifier selection.

 | pharmacyBlue

 | MDL: Strength  

 | Enum (DDL)

 | RequiredRed

 | default    : blank. 
Editable. Allowed values sourced from Strength values on Representative NDC rows for the drug.

 

 | Interdependent with Form (RxNorm Dose Form): selecting Strength filters Form options; selecting Form filters Strength options. If only one valid value remains, system should auto-populate it; if user changes one, the other must update accordingly.

 | 
Form

 | Captures the selected pharmacy drug dose form used with Strength to determine the correct RxCUI tied to NDC and related identifiers for the drug.

 | pharmacyBlue

 | MDL: RxNorm Dose Form

 | Enum (DDL)

 | RequiredRed

 | default    : blank. 
Editable. Allowed values  sourced from RxNorm Dose Form values on Representative NDC rows for the drug.

 

 | Interdependent with Strength: selecting Form filters Strength options; selecting Strength filters Form options. If only one valid value remains (on load or after selection), auto-populate. If user changes one, update the other accordingly. Strength+Form combination determines which RxCUI tied to NDC, Representative NDC, and GPI are saved for the drug.

 | 
Quantity per Auth

 | Calculated pharmacy authorization quantity based on dose, strength, and administration schedule.

 | pharmacyBlue

 | System calculation

 | Decimal (calculated; 2 decimals)

 | calculatedGreen

 | Auto-calculated for all pharmacy drugs. 
Not editable. 
Is blank if calculation cannot be performed

 | Formula: (Dosage &divide; Strength) &times; Adm Per Day &times; Adm Days Per Cycle &times; Cycles. Cycles derived from Duration per AP/Cycle in Days, rounded up to next whole number. 
Rounding: 2 decimals 
Rule: trigger alert if edited dosing exceeds Qty per Auth/duration configured in Admin Portal.

 | 
Adm. Per Day

 | Defines number of administrations per day; multiplier used in authorization calculations.

 | MedicalGreen

pharmacyBlue

 | MDL: Frequency Per Day 

 | Enum 

 | RequiredRed

 | default :  blank
Editable. Allowed values: One Time, Twice, Every Other Day (QOD), Once a day (QD), Twice a day (BID), Three times a day (TID), Four times a day (QID), Unknown

 | Meaning: How many times the patient receives the drug within the same day.

Example: If the drug is given twice on Day 1, Adm. Per Day = 2.

Impacts Max Billing Units/Auth and Quantity per Auth calculations.

 | 
Adm. Days Per Cycle

 | Number of administration days within a treatment cycle; multiplier used in authorization calculations.

 | MedicalGreen

pharmacyBlue

 | MDL  : Administrations Per Cycle

 | Integer 

 | RequiredRed

 | default :  blank 

Allowed values: whole, positive number; min 1 - max 100
Examples: Allowed: 2 ; 20 ; 100 ; 4 ; 1. Not Allowed: 200 ; 1.5 ; -10

 | Meaning: How many distinct days within one cycle the drug is administered.

Example: If the drug is given on Days 1, 8, and 15 of a 28-day cycle, Adm. Days Per Cycle = 3.

Impacts Max Billing Units/Auth and Quantity per Auth calculations.

 | 
Cycles in Days

 | Defines cycle length (duration per AP/Cycle in days) used to derive Cycles for authorization calculations.

 | MedicalGreen

pharmacyBlue

 | MDL : Cycle Length

 | Enum 

 | RequiredRed

 | default :  blank

Editable. Allowed values (in the following order): as needed, every 5 days, every 7 days, every 14 days, every 15 days, every 21 days, every 25 days, every 28 days, every 30 days, every 35 days, every 42 days, every 49 days, every 56 days, every 60 days, every 84 days, every 90 days, every 112 days, every 120 days, every 168 days, every 180 days, every 365 days, every day, onetime, Unknown

 | Meaning: The length of one treatment cycle in calendar days.

Example: If the regimen repeats every 28 days, Cycles in Days = 28.

Used to derive Cycles (rounded up) for authorization calculations.

 | 
Cycles

 | Number of cycles used in authorization calculations.

 | MedicalGreen

pharmacyBlue

 | MDL : Cycles

 | Integer 

 | RequiredRed

 | default :  blank 

Editable. Editable. Allowed values: whole positive number, min 1 max 100. Not allowed: decimals, negative numbers, values >100.)

 | Meaning: The total number of planned treatment cycle repetitions.

Example: If treatment is planned for 6 cycles, Cycles = 6.

Impacts Max Billing Units/Auth and Quantity per Auth calculations.

Master Drug Library (MDL)

 | Source of truth for drug identifiers and attributes used for billing + switching logic: HCPCS, RxCUI (Ingredient/Precise Ingredient/Brand), Benefit Type, NDC/GPI linkages, and EADL flag used to exclude non-appropriate alternatives. Stored in DrugsMS and surfaced via Admin Portal UI.

User Stories 

The user stories listed below represent V1.0 implementation candidates only.
Each story is prioritized using the MoSCoW model:

Must Have &ndash; required for the workflow to function in V1.0

Should Have &ndash; important, but not required for initial operability

Could Have &ndash; optional enhancements, deferred if needed

User Story Title

 | Priority

 | Acceptance criteria

 | Notes

 | 
1 | Create Custom Chemotherapy Regimen During Case Entry

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green     

 | User can create a custom regimen instead of selecting from the Regimen Library

The system shall allow creation of a Custom Regimen during and post case entry

The system shall allow users to search for drugs using:

HCPCS code

Drug name (brand or generic)

The system should return matching drugs in Custom Regimen drug search results using the format  [HCPCS code] [Drug Name] ([Brand Name])when a brand name is available.

the system should exclude drugs flagged as Ancillary drugs from the search results

The system should use the same display format for Medical and Pharmacy drugs, with no Pharmacy-specific variation in result presentation.

The system should use the clinically recognizable drug name from the source record as the primary displayed drug name and shall append the brand name in parentheses as a qualifier.

Example:

Source Admin

Drug Name: 3-iodobenzylguanidine

Brand Name: Azedra [2053287]

HCPCS: A9590

Expected display: A9590  3-iodobenzylguanidine (Azedra)

The system should start returning matching results only after the user enters at least 3 characters.

The system should sort the search results in ascending alphabetical order

Users should be able to select one or more drugs to form the Custom Regimen.

Selected drugs shall be added to the regimen drug list within the case.

Drugs dosing information in dosing tables should be blank by default

Custom regimen should saved to the case only (not to the Regimen Library)

Custom Regimens should be available for Operational Reporting

 | Custom Regimens will not be saved to the Regimen Library; however, they must be stored at the case level and remain available for post-denial cases, renewals, and supportive care workflows.

 | 
2 | Restrict custom regimen creation for external users to only after searching

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green      

 | The system shall restrict Custom Regimen creation based on user role as follows:

External users  (Provider Office Staff (Provider Portal)) should not be allowed to create a Custom Regimen.

Internal users (CRS, CRR (NewUM)) should be allowed to create a Custom Regimen only after performing a regimen search and no applicable predefined regimen is found:

If one or more predefined regimens are identified, the system should not allow creation of a Custom Regimen.

 | Validated Assumption: 

The Add Custom Regimen option should be displayed by default for now. For future web entry workflows intended for external users, the option should be shown only when the user is unable to find an existing regimen.

 | 
3 | Validate Custom Regimen Against Existing Regimens

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green      

 | When a user creates or modifies a Custom Regimen, the system shall evaluate the selected drug combination against predefined regimens for the case&rsquo;s selected diagnosis to check whether the set of drugs in the custom regimen exactly matches an existing regimen for the diagnosis group

If no matching predefined regimens are identified, the user shall be allowed to proceed with the Custom Regimen without interruption.

If one or more matching predefined regimens are identified, the system shall:

notify the user that a matching regimen exists

display the list of matching predefined regimens for user selection.

The user shall be able to:

Select one of the matching predefined regimens and replace the Custom Regimen, or

Continue with the originally created Custom Regimen 

Selecting a matching predefined regimen shall replace the Custom Regimen drug list and apply the predefined regimen structure in accordance with:

Main Regimen Selection 

Capture Basic Dosing Details 

If the user selects to remain with the Custom Regimen, the system shall allow continuation without blocking submission.

If user deletes the drug from the drug set selected for a custom regimen, the system shall re-evaluate the selected drug combination against predefined regimens for the case&rsquo;s selected diagnosis to check whether the set of drugs in the custom regimen exactly matches an existing regimen for the diagnosis group

 |  | 
4 | Enter Dosing Information for Custom Regimen

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green      

 | When the user creates custom regimen and adds drugs , the system shall retrieve the Billing Method for each drug from the Payer Drug Library (PDL) to automatically render two dosing tables based on the Billing Method classification in accordance with Capture Basic Dosing Details 

Once the Medical and Pharmacy dosing tables are rendered, the system should:

populate dosing table in accordance with Capture Basic Dosing Details : 

only HCPCS and description will populate based on selected drugs

the rest fields should be blank by default

allow selection of alternate drugs through the HCPCS code field drop down in accordance with Main Regimen Selection  

User should be able to view/edit drugs dosing information in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537473/Allow+Custom+Regimens#Data-Dictionary , Capture Basic Dosing Details , Capture Basic Dosing Details 

Calculation logic for system calculated fields should align to:

Medical:

https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537473/Allow+Custom+Regimens#Allowed-Dose 

https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537473/Allow+Custom+Regimens#Max-Billing-Units%2FAuth 

Indicate if Max Billing Units/Auth exceeds the drug&rsquo;s configured Max BU per duration in Admin Portal - no threshold or guardrail exists at this time.

Pharmacy:

https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537473/Allow+Custom+Regimens#Quantity-per-Auth 

Indicate if Quantity/Auth exceeds the drug&rsquo;s configured Qty per Auth/duration in Admin Portal - 

no threshold or guardrail exists at this time.

 | Ensure that all dosing guardrails and validation rules are applied consistently across Custom Regimens, Existing regimens, Ancillary Drugs to maintain uniform clinical and data integrity standards.

 | 
5 | Pend Custom Regimens for Auto-Rules

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green      

 | When a Custom Regimen is created and if the Custom Regimen contains at least one drug  with a status of Pending , the system shall:

bypass auto-determination and auto-approval rules for the case, and

set the case outcome to pend for Clinical Review.

If all drugs in the Custom Regimen are PA Exempt or Out of Scope (OOS) for the payer, the system shall not pend the case for clinical review due to the Custom Regimen and shall allow it to proceed through the standard non-clinical processing path.

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Description

 | Notes

 | 
System should apply the PA, OOS, and Benefit Type configuration from the PDL based on the member's eligibility

 | The system should retrieve the active PDL configuration record for each drug added during Chemo Entry (predefined regimen, custom regimen, ancillary) where:

Insurance Provider matches the member&rsquo;s eligibility

Major LOB matches the member&rsquo;s eligibility

The record is effective on the case date used for configuration lookups.

Upon loading a regimen (predefined, custom, or ancillary) or adding/switching a drug, the system should automatically apply the retrieved PDL configuration to each drug and set:

Configured benefit type: Medical | Pharmacy | Crossover

Medical benefit status: OOS | PA Required | PA Exempt

Pharmacy benefit status: OOS | PA Required | PA Exempt | Per Formulary

Current drug status (display): OOS (Out of Scope) | Pending | PA Exempt (derived per rules below)

The system should interpret PDL benefit status values using the following direct mapping to current drug status:

OOS &rarr;OOS

PA Exempt &rarr; PA Exempt

PA Required &rarr; Pending

Per Formulary > OOS:

If pharmacy benefit status = Per Formulary, the system should set current drug status to Out of Scope (OOS), since payer formulary configuration is out of scope for this feature. Additional Per Formulary determination logic will  be addressed as part of the Formulary Configuration feature.

The system should display each drug&rsquo;s current drug status in the dosing table as one of: Pending, PA Exempt, OOS

 | 02/15 ACS: Link to Monarch Requirements - Payer Drug Library
02/02 ACS: We will need another Epic to handle the AP enhancements that are required

tbdRed  The derivation of overall case status based on combined drug-level PA and OOS statuses 

 | 
System should apply the PA Exempt or OOS statuses appropriately to the case - shown during case entry

 | For each drug line added during case entry (predefined regimen, custom regimen, ancillary), the system should automatically derive the current drug status and display it in the dosing table during case entry and post-entry.

The system should determine the applicable benefit status for the drug line based on benefit type:

If benefit type = Medical, use medical benefit status.

If benefit type = Pharmacy, use pharmacy benefit status.

If benefit type = Crossover, use the benefit status corresponding to the user-selected benefit (Medical or Pharmacy). If no selection is made, the status is not determined and submission should be blocked until benefit is selected.

The system should map the applicable benefit status to current drug status using the following mapping - https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537605/Apply+Payer+Drug+Configurations#Drug-Status-Determination-Logic 

Status derivation should occur (and re-occur) immediately when any of the following events happen:

regimen is loaded

drug is added

drug is switched to an alternative

benefit selection changes for a crossover drug line

At submission, drug statuses should collectively determine whether the case requires clinical review:

If any drug line is Pending, the case requires clinical review.

If no drug lines are Pending, the case bypasses clinical review (subject to other rules).

 | 02/02 ACS: We will need to discuss how we plan to handle statuses in general.

 | 
Require users to choose benefit type during case entry; and allow them to change it in dosing

 | If a drug is configured as Crossover, the system should require the user to select the benefit type (Medical or Pharmacy) before the drug line is placed into a dosing table and before the drug status is determined.

A crossover drug should not be added to the case without a benefit selection.

Once selected, the crossover drug line should be placed into the corresponding dosing table (Medical or Pharmacy).

Users should be able to change the selected benefit type for a crossover drug line at any time prior to case submission.

If the selected benefit type is changed, the system should:

move the drug line to the appropriate dosing table (Medical or Pharmacy), and

re-evaluate the drug line&rsquo;s applicable benefit status and current drug status immediately.

For drugs configured strictly as Medical or Pharmacy, the benefit type should be system-defined from PDL and users should not be able to modify it.

The selected benefit type for crossover drugs should apply at the drug-line level within the current case only and should not alter upstream configuration.

Benefit type should be defined for every crossover drug line in the case before submission is allowed.

User Stories

User Story Title

 | Priority

 | Acceptance criteria

 | Notes

1 | Apply Benefit Type from PDL

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | When a drug is added during Chemo Entry, including through an existing regimen, custom regimen, or ancillary drug selection, the system should determine and apply the drug&rsquo;s benefit type (billing method) from the Payer Drug Library (PDL) based on the member&rsquo;s eligibility context.

The PDL lookup should use payer ID, major line of business, and drug.

The system should retrieve the PDL record that is effective for the Treatment Start Date.

If the benefit type is Medical (Buy & Bill):

The drug line should appear in the Medical dosing table in accordance with Separate Medical and Pharmacy Drugs into Distinct Dosing Tables

The user should not be able to modify the benefit type.

If the benefit type is Pharmacy:

The drug line should appear in the Pharmacy dosing table in accordance with Separate Medical and Pharmacy Drugs into Distinct Dosing Tables

The user should not be able to modify the benefit type.

If the benefit type is Crossover - the logic defined in https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537605/Apply+Payer+Drug+Configurations#Require-Benefit-Selection-for-Crossover-Drugs  should apply 

If a benefit type of Neither:

No drug should be configured with a billing method of Neither, but if it is encountered, including during testing, the system should treat it as Crossover and apply the logic defined  in https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537605/Apply+Payer+Drug+Configurations#Require-Benefit-Selection-for-Crossover-Drugs

A benefit type should be defined for every drug line in the case before the case can be saved.

If the upstream benefit type configuration changes while a case is in progress, the case should retain the benefit type that was applied at the time of case entry.

 | Current state: line of business is returning null in the Drug API because it is not yet configured; Will require changes in OH Admin Portal.

Future roadmap: expand granularity beyond line of business (e.g., product line, employer group) while keeping the system scalable. Will require changes in OH Admin Portal.

 | 
2 | Require Benefit Selection for Crossover Drugs

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | When a drug configured in the PDL as Crossover is added during Chemo Entry, including through an existing regimen, custom regimen, or ancillary drug selection, the system should require the user to select a benefit type of Medical or Pharmacy before the drug line is placed into a dosing table.

The system should not assign a default benefit type for crossover drugs.

The system should prevent a crossover drug line from being placed into either dosing table until a benefit type of Medical or Pharmacy is selected.

If multiple crossover drugs are added simultaneously, such as through a regimen, the system should require a benefit selection for each crossover drug line.

If the same crossover drug appears multiple times within a regimen, the selected benefit type should be applied consistently to all instances of that drug within the case.

If user cancels the selection (crossover drug modal), the system should clear the selected regimen

The selected benefit type should determine:

whether the drug line is displayed in the Medical or Pharmacy dosing table; and

whether the Medical or Pharmacy benefit type context is used to derive the applicable benefit status in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537605/Apply+Payer+Drug+Configurations#Apply-benefit-status--from-PDL-during-Chemo-Entry 

The system should prevent case save and submission if any crossover drug line does not have a selected benefit type.

The selected benefit type should apply only to the current case and should not modify the PDL classification of the drug for future cases

 | Previously validated designs (may change for NewUM)

 | 
3 | Apply benefit status  from PDL during Chemo Entry

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | When a drug is added during Chemo Entry, including through an existing regimen, custom regimen, or ancillary drug selection, and the benefit type for that drug has been determined in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537605/Apply+Payer+Drug+Configurations#Apply-Benefit-Type-from-PDL , the system should determine the applicable benefit status for the drug line based on the benefit type.

If the benefit type is Medical, the system should use the Medical benefit status configured in the PDL for that drug:

In the PDL, the Medical benefit status for a drug may be configured as one of the following values:  OOS / PA Required / PA Exempt

When the drug is added to the case, the system should resolve and save a single applicable Medical benefit status for that drug line.

If the benefit type is Pharmacy, the system should use the Pharmacy benefit status configured in the PDL for that drug. 

In the PDL, the Pharmacy benefit status for a drug may be configured as one of the following values: OOS / PA Required / PA Exempt / Per Formulary, which should map to OOS for now

When the drug is added to the case, the system should resolve and save a single applicable Pharmacy benefit status for that drug line.

If the benefit type is Crossover, the system should use the benefit status corresponding to the user-selected benefit type, Medical or Pharmacy.

The system should derive the current drug status for display from the applicable benefit status in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537605/Apply+Payer+Drug+Configurations#Drug-Status-Determination-Logic 

The resulting current drug status  should be displayed in the dosing table during case entry and after save or submission.

The benefit status configuration applied at case entry should remain fixed for the duration of the case, even if the upstream configuration changes.

The same benefit status logic should apply consistently to existing regimen drugs, custom regimen drugs, and ancillary drugs.

The system should derive, or re-derive, the current drug status immediately when any of the following events occur:

a regimen is loaded in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5141135361/Main+Regimen+Selection?search_id=bfccec72-620f-43e4-bb87-17a96263ac98 

a drug is added in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537473/Allow+Custom+Regimens?search_id=04fddc78-9476-4767-943b-b96cd48c390a  and https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537539/Select+Ancillary+Drugs?search_id=04fddc78-9476-4767-943b-b96cd48c390a 

a drug is switched to an alternative in accordance with Main Regimen Selection 

the selected benefit type changes for a crossover drug line in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537605/Apply+Payer+Drug+Configurations#Change-Benefit-Type-for-Crossover-Drug-Before-Case-Submission 

 | AP:

Previously validated designs (may change for NewUM)

 | 
4 | Change Benefit Type for Crossover Drug Before Case Submission

 | should haveYellow  v1.r1.Green  

 | If a drug is configured as Crossover and has already been assigned a selected benefit type of Medical or Pharmacy, the user should be able to change the selected benefit type while the case remains in Draft status.

When the selected benefit type is changed, the system should:

remove the drug line from its current dosing table;

place the drug line into the corresponding dosing table based on the newly selected benefit type; and

immediately re-derive the applicable benefit status for that drug line.

Once the case is submitted, the selected benefit type for a crossover drug line should no longer be modifiable.

The updated selected benefit type should apply only to the current case and should not modify payer-level drug configuration for future cases.

 | Previously validated designs (may change for NewUM)

#### Apply Payer Non-Preferred Drug Rules

Project Specifics

Target Version

 | 1.0

Goals & Business Objectives

TBD

Background & Current State

TBD

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Description

 | Notes

 | 
System applies the NP drug rules from the AP based on the member's eligibility and display on the drug level within dosing

 | After selecting a main regimen, creating a custom regimen, or adding an ancillary drug, the system evaluates each selected drug against the applicable payer Non-Preferred (NP) drug rules. 

The evaluation identifies Non-Preferred drugs selected for Chemo Entry and determines their enforcement level in accordance with payer policy. 

NP rules must support both Medical and Pharmacy drugs

NP rule evaluation is executed for each selected drug when a main regimen is selected, a custom regimen drug is added, an ancillary drug is added.

The selected drug is evaluated against all applicable payer NP rule attributes by validating:

The drug matches the configured Non-Preferred Drug.

The member&rsquo;s Major LOB ( in future - LOB, Product Line etc.) matches

The drug&rsquo;s Billing Method matches 

The case diagnosis satisfies the configured Diagnosis Group logic (Include/Exclude).

The member&rsquo;s stage and state are not listed in the rule&rsquo;s exclusion criteria.

The Rule Type (Mandatory vs Voluntary) determines enforcement level once the rule is satisfied.

when all applicable rule conditions are satisfied:

The drug is marked as Non-Preferred.

An &ldquo;NP&rdquo; indicator is displayed at the drug row level within the dosing table.

Rule Type (Mandatory or Voluntary) determines enforcement level.

Rule Type determines visual representation of the NP indicator.

Case view should include verbiage to inform the user that the case contains an NP drug

If rule conditions are not satisfied, the drug is not marked as Non-Preferred and no NP indicator is displayed.

NP rule evaluation applies to both Medical and Pharmacy drugs.

 | 02/15 ACS: Link to Monarch Requirements - Non-Preferred Drug Rules

Downstream behaviors when NP exists

Case submission messaging (external users):

If the case is submitted with one or more Non-Preferred (NP) drugs in the main regimen or ancillary drugs, the system should display a submission message indicating the case contains NP drug(s) and supporting clinical documentation is required for the exception.

If the case contains NP drug(s), the system should suppress &ldquo;auto-approvable&rdquo; messaging in treatment request summary/submitted views, even if the regimen would otherwise qualify for auto-approval.

Post-submission processing classification (protocol/assignment)

If the main regimen contains at least one NP drug, the case should be processed as Non-Auto.

If any ancillary drug is NP, the case should be processed as Non-Auto.

The processing view should indicate NP presence and list the NP drug name(s) separately for:

main regimen NP drug(s)

ancillary NP drug(s)

Post-submission processing reasons display

If the case is processed as Non-Auto due to NP drug(s), processing summary should show the NP reason first.

If there are additional Non-Auto reasons, the system should display those reasons below the NP reason in the same processing summary.

 | 
Allow users to change to a preferred drug - track this change for FI reporting

 |  When a drug is identified as Non-Preferred, the user should be able to select a Preferred Drug 

If the user selects a Preferred Drug that shares the same ingredient RxCUI as the Non-Preferred drug, the drug is replaced within the existing regimen and dosing context.

If the user selects a Preferred Drug that does not share the same ingredient RxCUI as the Non-Preferred drug, the regimen must be updated. The system presents alternative regimen options that contain the selected Preferred Drug, and the user selects the appropriate updated regimen.

Any time a user changes from a Non-Preferred drug to a Preferred drug, the system captures the change for Financial Impact reporting. The captured data must include all dosing information associated with the drug at the time of change. Detailed reporting specifications are to be defined 

 |  | 
Allow users to enter a clinical exception reason (static list) for NP drugs

 | When a drug is identified as Non-Preferred, the user should be able to provide clinical exception reason.

The user should be able to select an Exception Reason from a predefined static list:

Exception reasons represent clinical justification for use of the Non-Preferred drug, including scenarios where preferred drugs have failed or where a clinical rationale supports use of the Non-Preferred drug.

If a regimen is otherwise auto-approvable based on indication but contains a Non-Preferred drug, the case must pend for clinical review.

 |   Downstream behaviors:

In post-submission dosing review, the system should support entering/updating the Exception Reason for NP drugs using the same behavior as case entry (where applicable by user type/permissions).

If a regimen would otherwise qualify for auto-approval but contains one or more NP drugs, the system should route the case to pend for clinical review.

 | 
Display the preferred products to the end user

 | When a drug is identified as Non-Preferred , the user should be able to select a preferred drug, including the following cases for Preferred drug selection:

Preferred Drug is present in Alternative DDL

Preferred Drug is not available in Alternative DDL but exist in another regimen

Preferred  Drug is not available in Alternative DDL and does not match another regimen

User Stories 

The user stories listed below represent V1.0 implementation candidates only.
Each story is prioritized using the MoSCoW model:

Must Have &ndash; required for the workflow to function in V1.0

Should Have &ndash; important, but not required for initial operability

Could Have &ndash; optional enhancements, deferred if needed

1 | Case Entry (Draft Case) v1.r1.Green

2 | Apply NP Drug Rules Based on Member Eligibility (incl. NP Drug Label Display at Dosing Level)

 | must haveRed  

 | The system should evaluate payer Non-Preferred (NP) rules for affected drugs whenever any of the following events occurs:

a main regimen is selected, changed, or replaced; 

the system should evaluate NP status for all drug lines in the regimen.

a custom regimen is created or edited; 

the system should evaluate NP status only for the affected added/changed drug line(s).

an ancillary drug is added or edited; 

the system should evaluate NP status only for the affected added/changed drug line(s).

the benefit type of a crossover drug is changed; 

the system should evaluate NP status only for the affected added/changed drug line(s).

a drug is switched to an equivalent alternative drug based on shared ingredient RxCUI; 

the system should evaluate NP status only for the affected added/changed drug line(s).

For each NP Drug check, the system should retrieve the active payer Non-Preferred rule record for the drug using: payer ID,  Major LOB (future: line of business, product line), Drug, Treatment Start Date effective dating:

The lookup should use payer ID, Major LOB and drug.

The system should retrieve the record that is effective for the Treatment Start Date.

The system should determine whether the drug is Non-Preferred by evaluating the all the attributes of the NP drug record:

Billing Method

Rule Type - used for Mandatory vs Voluntary type of NP drug

Diagnosis Groups - used to check whether this diagnosis is included or excluded for NP rules of this drug

Include / Exclude Diagnosis Groups - used to define whether diagnosis mentioned in "Diagnosis Groups" to be included or excluded while checking for preference of drugs.

Stage Excluded - Used to set the stage of cancer for which NP rules will not be applicable for this drug.

State of issue Excluded - /

Member State Excluded - /

If the drug meets the applicable NP rule conditions, the system should mark the drug as Non-Preferred

If a drug is marked as Non-Preferred, the dosing table should display an NP indicator on that drug row, and the indicator styling should distinguish Mandatory NP from Voluntary NP.

 | Post submission:  If the case contains a Non-Preferred drug, this is also reflected in case view and related case documentation.

NP indicator:

3 | Allow User to Change to Preferred Drug 

 | must haveRed  

 | When a Non-Preferred (NP) drug is present during case entry (in accordance with Apply NP Drug Rules Based on Member Eligibility (incl. NP Drug Label Display at Dosing Level)), the system should allow the user to change that NP drug to a Preferred drug : 

If the case contains at least one drug line marked as NP, the system should display the Change to Preferred action (Optional)

The Change to Preferred Agent action should be available only for drug lines currently marked as NP and should use the Preferred alternatives displayed for that NP drug in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5156700161/Apply+Payer+Non-Preferred+Drug+Rules#Display-Preferred-Drug-Alternatives-for-Non-Preferred-Drugs 

The user should be able to select a Preferred drug from the displayed Preferred alternatives for that NP drug:

If the selected Preferred drug is available in the Alternative Drug list (in accordance with Allow Switching Between Equivalent Drugs Based on Shared RxCUI), the system should:

replace the NP drug with the Preferred drug while keeping the regimen unchanged

remove the NP indicator for that drug line

If the selected Preferred drug is not available in the Alternative Drug list, the system should:

identify existing regimen options that match the updated drug combination (selected Preferred drug plus the other drugs from the current regimen) using the matching-regimen logic implemented in Validate Custom Regimen Against Existing Regimens

present the matching regimen options to the user and, upon selection, refresh the dosing tables using the selected regimen defaults while keeping dosing fields editable

If no matching existing regimen exists for the selected Preferred drug, the system should (for internal users):

notify the user that no matching regimen exists

return the user to the NP drug state with no change applied

Until case submission, 

if a Preferred selection is reverted for a drug line that was changed through direct replacement within the current regimen, the system should:

restore the last saved NP drug for that drug line

restore NP status and NP-related actions for that drug line

keep the rest of the current regimen unchanged.

if a Preferred selection is reverted for a case that was changed through matching-regimen replacement, the system should:

restore the last saved regimen that existed before the matching regimen was applied

restore the last saved drug lines and NP statuses associated with that prior regimen

discard the unsaved or interim regimen-replacement state.

After case submission,

 if a direct NP-to-Preferred change was made, the selected Preferred drug should persist on that drug line unless reverted before case submission.

if a matching-regimen selection was made, the selected regimen should persist as the current regimen unless reverted before case submission.

4 | Allow User to Enter Clinical Exception Reason for Non-Preferred Drug

 | must haveRed  

 | If a drug is flagged as Non-Preferred (NP), the system should allow the user to select an Exception Reason for that NP drug line from a predefined static list: 

If a drug line is marked as NP, the system should display the Exception Reason action/control for that NP drug line.

The system should store the selected Exception Reason at the drug-line level within the case record.

The selected Exception Reason should remain visible as the current saved value for that drug line during case entry

If the selected Exception Reason requires supporting text - for  &ldquo;Other&rdquo; option - the system should require text entry before allowing the user to save:

The system should store both the selected Exception Reason and any supporting text at the NP drug-line level and should restore the last saved values if the user cancels without saving.

v1.r1Green  Internal users: if one or more NP drugs remain on the case at Save and any NP drug line is missing an Exception Reason, the system should:

allow user to return to update the NP drug line(s), or

proceed without an Exception Reason.

5 | Display Preferred Drug Alternatives for Non-Preferred Drugs

 | must haveRed  

 | If the case contains at least one drug line marked as Non-Preferred (NP), the system should display the Change to Preferred action (Optional)

When the user initiates Change to Preferred, the system should display all current NP drug lines on the case in their current case order.

For each NP drug line, the system should display the available Preferred drug alternatives returned for that NP drug line.

For a given NP drug line, Preferred drug alternatives should be displayed in the following order:

Preferred drugs available in the Alternative Drug list

Preferred drugs not available in the Alternative Drug list.

If the user selects a Preferred drug that is available in the Alternative Drug list, the system should proceed with the direct replacement flow for that drug line.

If the user selects a Preferred drug that is not available in the Alternative Drug list, the system should proceed with the matching-regimen flow for that drug line.

If matching regimens are found for the selected Preferred drug, the system should display the matching regimen options and allow the user to select one.

If no matching regimen is found for the selected Preferred drug, the system should notify the user and return that drug line to the original NP state with no Preferred change applied.

If no Preferred drug alternatives are available for an NP drug line, the system should continue to display that NP drug line in the NP drug set, but should not display selectable Preferred drug alternatives for that line.

After a successful change to a Preferred drug, the system should no longer display Preferred drug alternatives for that resolved drug line while the Preferred selection remains active.

If a resolved drug line is returned to NP state, the system should display the Preferred drug alternatives for that drug line again.

Until case submission, if a drug line was changed from NP to Preferred, the system should display the Revert to non-preferred action for that resolved drug line while the Preferred selection remains active.

 | FE effort for https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5156700161/Apply+Payer+Non-Preferred+Drug+Rules#Allow-User-to-Change-to-Preferred-Drug

 | 
7 | Record Financial Impact (FI) for NP &rarr; Preferred Drug Change (Case Entry)

 | should haveYellowv1.r1.Green    

 | WThe system should create an FI record only for a drug change from Non-Preferred (NP) to Preferred made through the NP exception / Change to Preferred flow during case entry.

The system should create the FI record only when the NP &rarr; Preferred change is present in the final submitted case state.

The system should not create an FI record for: 

NP &rarr; Preferred changes reverted before submission

drug changes made through the  Alternative DDL 

The system should create one FI record per distinct NP &rarr; Preferred drug change included in the submitted case.

Each FI record should store, at minimum: case ID, user ID, submission timestamp, original NP drug, final Preferred drug, original NP drug dosing details, final Preferred drug dosing details

If the Preferred selection results in regimen replacement, the FI record should also store the original regimen context and the final regimen context.

The system should persist the FI record as a point-in-time snapshot of the submitted case and should not update it based on later library or configuration changes.

The system should prevent duplicate FI records for the same submitted case version and NP &rarr; Preferred change.

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Description

 | Notes

 | 
Medical drugs and pharmacy drugs should be separated into two different dosing tables with appropriate fields

 | Render two distinct dosing tables based on Billing Method (Medical vs Pharmacy) 

Display only fields applicable to each benefit type 

Medical table includes Allowed Dose and Max Billing Units/Auth 

Pharmacy table includes Strength, Form, and Quantity per Auth 

Dynamically re-render table if Billing Method changes

 | Billing Method sourced from Payer Drug Library. Crossover drugs require user selection.

 | 
Calculate Medical Billing Units/Auth and Pharmacy Quantity/Cycle

 | For Medical drugs, calculate Max Billing Units/Auth using Allowed Dose, frequency, cycle values, and CMU BU 

For Pharmacy drugs, calculate Quantity per Auth using Dosage, Strength, and cycle values 

Apply defined rounding rules (2 decimals) 

Display &ldquo;--&rdquo; if required inputs are missing

 | Calculation logic applies consistently to Existing, Custom, and Ancillary drugs.

 | 
Select appropriate Strength & Form for pharmacy drugs and save RxCUI Brand TTY, GPI, and Representative NDC

 | Provide dropdowns for Strength and Dose Form sourced from Representative NDC rows 

Filter Strength and Form values bi-directionally 

Auto-populate if only one valid option remains 

Persist RxCUI tied to NDC, Representative NDC, and GPI based on selected combination

 | Strength and Form are interdependent. Identifiers must be saved at case-drug level.

 | 
Calculate Allowed Dose based on Height & Weight

 | For fixed units, set Allowed Dose equal to Dosage 

For weight-based units, calculate Dosage &times; Weight (kg) 

For BSA-based units, calculate Dosage &times; BSA 

Recalculate when Height or Weight changes 

Apply rounding rules (2 decimals) 

Express result in Billable UOM

 | Carboplatin AUC treated as fixed-dose. Height/Weight assumed available.

 | 
Populate initial dosing details based on selected regimen details

 | Populate Dosage from Regimen Details (Dose per Administration) 

Populate Units, Frequency, Adm. Days per Cycle, Cycle Length, and Cycles from Regimen Details 

Apply defaults only for Existing Regimens 

Leave fields blank for Custom and Ancillary drugs where required

 | Defaults must remain editable where permitted by UI design.

 | 
Allow users to edit dosing details

 | Allow editing of fields with dropdown controls (per UI design) 

Recalculate dependent fields when editable values change 

Keep calculated fields read-only 

Enforce validation rules on dropdown selections

 | Only dropdown fields are editable per current design.

 | 
Indicate when a dosing change pushes Billing Unit/Auth or Quantity/Auth above default

 | Detect when recalculated Max Billing Units/Auth or Quantity/Auth exceeds configured default thresholds 

Display visual indicator or alert 

Do not block entry unless business rule requires 

Apply consistently to Medical and Pharmacy drugs

 | Post-MVP enhancement tied to Admin Portal configuration.

Units

 | Identifies the dose unit used for the drug and determines the calculation pathway

 | MedicalGreen 

 | Drug selected; Billable UOM available

 | Enum (DDL)

 | RequiredRed    

 | Regimen Details: Dose Unit ;

Master Drug Library: Billable UOM

 | Default from Regimen:  Dose Units. 

Editable. Drop Down Logic:

1. For Dose Drop Down: The allowed Units values should be inferred based on the associated Billable UOM (BUM) for the drug (https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5148737537/Capture+Basic+Dosing+Details#1.-Source-of-allowed-Units-values%3A-should-be-determined-based-on-the-drug%E2%80%99s-associated-Billable-Unit-of-Measure-(Billable-UOM). )

1.1. Carboplatin is a defined exception. In addition to the standard Units derived from its Billable UOM, the Units dropdown should also include: Area Under Curve 1.5, Area Under Curve 2, Area Under Curve 3, Area Under Curve 4, Area Under Curve 5, Area Under Curve 6, Area Under Curve 7

3. The Units dropdown should always include &ldquo;Unknown&rdquo; as a selectable option.

 | Unit selection determines whether Allowed Dose is calculated (mg/kg, mg/m&sup2;, etc.) or equals Dosage (fixed units).

1. Source of allowed Units values: should be determined based on the drug&rsquo;s associated Billable Unit of Measure (Billable UOM).

AssumptionRed The Drugs API returns the Billable UOM and the corresponding list of allowed Units for all drugs, including Existing Regimens, Custom Regimens, and Ancillary Drugs, so that NewUM will not be responsible for Billable UOM to Units mapping:

If Billable UOM = mg. Allowed Units:
mg, g, g/kg, mcg, mcg/kg, mcg/m2, mg/kg, mg/m2, g/m2
If Billable UOM = mcg. Allowed Units:mg, g, g/kg, mcg, mcg/kg, mcg/m2, mg/kg, mg/m2, g/m2
If Billable UOM = mCi. Allowed Units:mCi
If Billable UOM = IU. Allowed Units:IU/kg, IU/m2
If Billable UOM = Units. Allowed Units:International Unit, million units, million units/kg, units, units/kg, units/m2
If Billable UOM = Infusion. Allowed Units: Infusion
If Billable UOM = million Units. Allowed Units:
International Unit, million units, million units/kg, units, units/kg, units/m2

2. Drug-level overrides and extensions: The system should support configurableRed , drug-specific extensions to the standard Units list. This allows certain drugs to have additional or alternative Units without requiring code changes.

 | 
Allowed Dose

 | Calculated patient-specific dose 

 | MedicalGreen  

 | Dosage, Units, Height, Weight; Billable UOM

 | Decimal (calculated; 2 decimals)

 | calculatedGreen 

 | System calculation using Dosage, Units, and patient Height/Weight/BSA

 | Calculated automatically. Not editable
Formula:
- Fixed units (mg, g, mcg) &rarr; Allowed Dose = Dosage
- Carboplatin AUC (1.5&ndash;7) &rarr; Allowed Dose = Dosage
- Weight-based units (mg/kg, mcg/kg, g/kg) &rarr; Allowed Dose = Dosage &times; Weight (kg)
- BSA-based units (mg/m&sup2;, g/m&sup2;, IU/m&sup2;, units/m&sup2;) &rarr; Allowed Dose = Dosage &times; BSA where BSA = &radic;(Height [cm] &times; Weight [kg] / 3600). Allowed Dose must be expressed in the drug&rsquo;s Billable UOM (apply mg/mcg/g conversions as needed).
Rounding: 2 decimal places using the thousandths rule.

 |  
Rule: Recalculate Allowed Dose if Weight changes (for weight-based units), Height or Weight changes (for BSA-based units)

 | 
Max Billing Units/Auth

 | Calculated maximum medical authorization quantity expressed in billing units.

 | MedicalGreen  

 | Allowed Dose, Adm Per Day, Adm Days Per Cycle, Cycles, CMU BU from AP

 | Decimal (calculated; 2 decimals)

 | calculatedGreen  

 | System calculation 

 | Auto-calculated for all medical drugs. Not editable. Is blank if calculation cannot be performed

 | Formula: (Allowed Dose &times; Adm Per Day &times; Adm Days Per Cycle &times; Cycles) &divide; CMU BU (from Admin Portal). Cycles derivation: Duration per AP/Cycle in Days, rounded up to next whole number. 
Rounding: 2 decimals per standard thousandths rule. Rule: trigger alert if edited dosing exceeds Max BU/duration configured in Admin Portal.

 | 
Strength

 | Captures the selected pharmacy drug strength used for downstream pharmacy dosing (e.g., quantity) and drug identifier selection.

 | pharmacyBlue  

 | Drug selected; Representative NDC data available

 | Enum (DDL)

 | RequiredRed    

 | Master Drug Library:  Default: blank. 

DDL: Representative NDC rows &rarr; Strength

 | Default: blank. 
Editable. Allowed values sourced from Strength values on Representative NDC rows for the drug.

 | Interdependent with Form (RxNorm Dose Form): selecting Strength filters Form options; selecting Form filters Strength options. If only one valid value remains, system should auto-populate it; if user changes one, the other must update accordingly.

 | 
Form

 | Captures the selected pharmacy drug dose form used with Strength to determine the correct RxCUI tied to NDC and related identifiers for the drug.

 | pharmacyBlue  

 | Drug selected; Representative NDC data available

 | Enum (DDL)

 | RequiredRed    

 | Master Drug Library:

Default: blank. 

DDL: Representative NDC rows &rarr; RxNorm Dose Form

 | Default: blank. 
Editable. Allowed values  sourced from RxNorm Dose Form values on Representative NDC rows for the drug.

 | Interdependent with Strength: selecting Form filters Strength options; selecting Strength filters Form options. If only one valid value remains (on load or after selection), auto-populate. If user changes one, update the other accordingly. Strength+Form combination determines which RxCUI tied to NDC, Representative NDC, and GPI are saved for the drug. 

 | 
Quantity per Auth

 | Calculated pharmacy authorization quantity based on dose, strength, and administration schedule.

 | pharmacyBlue  

 | Dosage, Strength, Adm Per Day, Adm Days Per Cycle, Cycles

 | Decimal (calculated; 2 decimals)

 | calculatedGreen  

 | System calculation

 | Auto-calculated for all pharmacy drugs. Not editable. Is blank if calculation cannot be performed

 | Formula: (Dosage &divide; Strength) &times; Adm Per Day &times; Adm Days Per Cycle &times; Cycles. Cycles derived from Duration per AP/Cycle in Days, rounded up to next whole number. 
Rounding: 2 decimals 
Rule: trigger alert if edited dosing exceeds Qty per Auth/duration configured in Admin Portal.

 |

 | Defines number of administrations per day; multiplier used in authorization calculations.

 | MedicalGreen 

pharmacyBlue

Editable . Allowed values: One Time, Twice, Every Other Day (QOD), Once a day (QD), Twice a day (BID), Three times a day (TID), Four times a day (QID), Unknown

 | Meaning: How many times the patient receives the drug within the same day.

Example: If the drug is given twice on Day 1, Adm. Per Day = 2.

 | Meaning: How many distinct days within one cycle the drug is administered.

Preferred Measurement System 

 

 | Controls the units and input format for capturing patient height and weight.

 | Displayed once a member is selected and the case enters data capture for dosing-relevant workflows.

 | Enum:
Standard (ft/in/lb)

Standard (in/lb)

Metric (cm/kg)

 | RequiredRed  

 | Default to Standard (ft/in/lb). When changed, the system converts the currently stored Height and Weight into the newly selected input format and updates the displayed converted helper values. The system shall retain normalized values for calculation in centimeters and kilograms.

 | Weight, Height, and BSA recalculation; triggers recalculation of Patient Specific Dose / Allowed Dose and other dose-derived fields that use Height, Weight, or BSA.

 | 
Weight

 | Captures patient weight used for weight-based and BSA-based dosing.

 | Displayed once a member is selected and the case enters dosing context. Required for any dosing calculation that uses Weight or BSA.

 | Numeric input. Display/input unit depends on Preferred Measurement System: lb for Standard (ft/in/lb) and Standard (in/lb); kg for Metric (cm/kg).

 | RequiredRed  

 | If measurement system = Standard (ft/in/lb) or Standard (in/lb), user enters Weight in pounds and the system converts and stores normalized Weight_kg = Weight_lb &times; 0.453592. If measurement system = Metric (cm/kg), user enters Weight in kilograms and the system stores that value as normalized Weight_kg. The UI should display the converted equivalent value in the alternate unit beside the input. Value must be numeric and > 0.

 | Preferred Measurement System; normalized Weight_kg; BSA; Patient Specific Dose / Allowed Dose for weight-based and BSA-based dosing; Max Billing Units/Auth via Allowed Dose.

 | 
Height

 | Captures patient height used for BSA-based dosing.

 | Displayed once a member is selected and the case enters dosing context. Required for BSA-based dosing calculations.

 | Input format depends on Preferred Measurement System: Composite (ft + in) for Standard (ft/in/lb); Numeric (in) for Standard (in/lb); Numeric (cm) for Metric (cm/kg).

 | RequiredRed  

 | If measurement system = Standard (ft/in/lb), user enters Height as feet and inches; system converts and stores normalized Height_cm = ((ft &times; 12) + in) &times; 2.54. If measurement system = Standard (in/lb), user enters Height in inches; system converts and stores normalized Height_cm = Height_in &times; 2.54. If measurement system = Metric (cm/kg), user enters Height in centimeters and the system stores that value as normalized Height_cm. The UI should display the converted equivalent value beside the input, as shown in the existing system. Values must be numeric and > 0. For ft + in, inches should be constrained to 0&ndash;11.

 | Preferred Measurement System; normalized Height_cm; BSA; Patient Specific Dose / Allowed Dose for BSA-based dosing; Max Billing Units/Auth via Allowed Dose.

 | 
BSA 

BEBlue 

 | Patient Body Surface Area used for BSA-based dosing calculations.

 | Calculated and available when normalized Height_cm and Weight_kg are present and > 0.

 | Decimal, in m&sup2;

 | System-calculated, BE field

 | Calculated in the background using normalized values: BSA = &radic;((Height_cm &times; Weight_kg) / 3600). Rounded to 2 decimal places. Recalculated automatically when Height, Weight, or Preferred Measurement System changes. 

 | Height_cm, Weight_kg; drives Patient Specific Dose / Allowed Dose for BSA-based units; impacts Max Billing Units/Auth through Allowed Dose.

 | Defines standardized oncology treatment regimens. Provides default dosing parameters (Dose per Administration, Units, Frequency per Day, Administrations per Cycle, Cycle Length, Cycles) used to populate initial dosing details for Existing Regimens.

Master Drug Library (MDL)

 | Authoritative drug reference dataset. Provides HCPCS code, Drug Name, Billable UOM, Representative NDC rows, Strength, RxNorm Dose Form, RxCUI tied to NDC, GPI, and other core drug attributes used in both Medical and Pharmacy dosing tables.

 |  |

 | Payer-specific overlay to the Master Drug Library. Defines Benefit Type (Medical / Pharmacy / Crossover), Medical & Pharmacy Benefit Status, OOS flag, Prior Auth requirement, and effective dating. Drives table placement, workflow gating, and authorization context.

User Stories 

The user stories listed below represent V1.0 implementation candidates only.
Each story is prioritized using the MoSCoW model:

Must Have &ndash; required for the workflow to function in V1.0

Should Have &ndash; important, but not required for initial operability

Could Have &ndash; optional enhancements, deferred if needed

User Story Title

 | Priority

 | Acceptance criteria

 | Notes

 | 
1 | Separate Medical and Pharmacy Drugs into Distinct Dosing Tables

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | When the user selects Chemotherapy and adds drugs via Existing Regimen, Custom Regimen, or Ancillary Drug, the system shall retrieve the Billing Method for each drug from the Payer Drug Library (PDL):

Table placement shall be driven exclusively by the Billing Method value from the PDL and shall not rely on Master Drug Library data.

After drugs are added to the case, the system shall automatically render two dosing tables based on the Billing Method classification.

Drugs with Billing Method = Medical shall be displayed in the Medical Dosing Table:

Medical table column set (see Data Dictionary fields where Applies To (Benefit Type) contains MedicalGreen .

Drugs with Billing Method = Pharmacy shall be displayed in the Pharmacy Dosing Table:

Pharmacy table column set (see Data Dictionary fields where Applies To (Benefit Type) contains pharmacyBlue .

If both Medical and Pharmacy drugs are present, both dosing tables shall be displayed simultaneously.

If only one benefit type is present, only the corresponding dosing table shall be displayed.

If a drug is configured as Crossover, the system shall require the user to select Medical or Pharmacy before displaying the drug in a dosing table ( out of scope for this story)

A drug shall appear in only one dosing table at any time.

The dosing tables shall render immediately after regimen selection, custom regimen drug addition, or ancillary drug addition without requiring page refresh

 | Prerequisites:

Tx Type = Chemo.

Regimen-selected drugs are resolved, including HCPCS and drug name.

Drug alternatives sharing the same RxCUI are defined.

Billing Method / Benefit Type is resolved for each drug based on payer-member context.

 | 
2 | Select Strength and Form for pharmacy drugs 

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | The system shall require Strength and Dose Form selection for all Pharmacy drugs, including drugs from Existing Regimens, Custom Regimens, and Ancillary drugs.

Strength and Dose Form fields shall be empty by default and presented as required dropdown lists.

The Strength dropdown values shall be sourced from the Master Drug Library by collecting the Strength values from all Representative NDC rows for the selected drug.

The Dose Form dropdown values shall be sourced from the Master Drug Library by collecting the RxNorm Dose Form values from all Representative NDC rows for the selected drug.

Strength and Dose Form shall be interdependent; selecting a Strength shall filter the Dose Form options to only those that exist for the selected Strength in the Representative NDC rows, and selecting a Dose Form shall filter the Strength options to only those that exist for the selected Dose Form:

If only one valid Strength or Dose Form value exists either on initial render or after the user makes a selection, the system shall auto-populate the remaining field with the single valid value.

If the user changes a previously selected Strength or Dose Form, the system shall update the other dropdown to reflect the new valid combinations and shall clear any value that is no longer valid.

After a valid Strength and Dose Form combination is selected, the system shall identify the matching Representative NDC row and persist, at the case-drug level, the RxCUI tied to NDC, Representative NDC, and GPI from that row.

If the user changes Strength or Dose Form after identifiers were persisted, the system shall re-select the matching Representative NDC row and update the persisted RxCUI tied to NDC, Representative NDC, and GPI accordingly.

Quantity per Authorization calculation shall not execute for Pharmacy drugs until Strength is selected and the persisted identifiers are available for the selected Strength and Dose Form combination.- part of user story https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5148737537/Capture+Basic+Dosing+Details#Calculate-Pharmacy-Quantity-per-Auth 

 | Source mapping is based on the Master Drug Library &ldquo;Additional Drug Codes&rdquo; grid, where each Representative NDC row includes RxCUI tied to NDC, NDC, Representative NDC flag, GPI, RxNorm Dose Form, and Strength.

The matching algorithm should treat each Representative NDC row as a valid Strength&ndash;Dose Form pairing and select the row that matches the user&rsquo;s selected Strength and Dose Form.

Persisted identifiers should be stored as a snapshot on the case drug record to support downstream rule logic even if the Master Drug Library changes later.

Optional UX enhancements include a reset action for Strength/Dose Form and tooltips explaining that options are constrained by valid Representative NDC pairings.

 | 
3 | Capture Patient Height and Weight

 | must haveRed

v1.r1.Green    

 | The system should  support/introduce case-level fields for  Preferred Measurement System, Height, and Weight using one of three measurement systems: 

Standard (ft/in/lb)

Standard (in/lb)

Metric (cm/kg). 

Based on the selected measurement system, the system should : 

adjust the Height and Weight input format and units

display converted equivalent values for reference

normalize and store Height in centimeters and Weight in kilograms

calculate BSA in the background as a m&sup2; value

recalculate BSA and all dependent dosing fields whenever Measurement System, Height, or Weight changes. 

Height and Weight entry should be required before enabling Main Regimen selection, Custom Regimen drug addition, and Ancillary Drug selection for Chemotherapy.

Incorporate:  

Web and phone entry: Height and weight required fields, no exceptions.

Fax entry: Also required, but if missing and CRS can&rsquo;t find in documentation:

CRS selects &ldquo;unknown.&rdquo;

System auto-populates gender-based default height/weight (likely age-dependent as well).

Defaults used for allowed dose and all downstream calculated fields.

Prior logic removed: Old behavior &ldquo;use dosage when H&W missing&rdquo; is deprecated; dev to revert/remove that logic.

Release 1: Default values to be provided by Nichole and included in Release 1 ( confirm whether these default values should be configurable in future)

 | assumptionRed Height and Weight are mandatory fields

4 | Calculate Allowed Dose Using Height and Weight

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | The system shall calculate the Patient Specific Dose for each drug based on the patient&rsquo;s height and weight.

If the Patient Specific Dose is not calculated based on height, weight, or BSA, it shall always equal the Dose per Administration.

If patient Height and Weight are provided, Patient BSA should be calculated using the formula and used for calculations. Otherwise, an Average BSA of 1.95 m2 should be used: Patient BSA (m2)  = sqr(Height[cm] * Weight[kg] / 3600)

The same calculation logic should apply to all Medical drugs, including Existing Regimens, Custom Regimens, and Ancillary drugs:

when Dose per Administration is flagged as a fixed dose (mg, mCi, CAR-Positive viable T cells), the system should not calculate Patient Specific Dose and should use the Dose per Administration.

for Carboplatin, when the Dose per Administration follows Area Under the Curve (Area Under Curve 1.5, Area Under Curve 2, Area Under Curve 3, Area Under Curve 4, Area Under Curve 5, Area Under Curve 6, Area Under Curve 7), the system should not calculate Patient Specific Dose and shall use the Dose per Administration.

when Dose per Administration is in mg/kg, mcg/kg units:

if Pt Weight is not entered, Patient Specific dose should be displayed as (-- <Drug Units>)

 If Pt Weight is entered, Patient Specific dose should be calculated as: <Dose per Administration>* <Weight kg> (rounding: 2 decimal points, usual rounding rules)

If weight is updated, Patient Specific dose should  be re-calculated and displayed in the table

when Dose per Administration is in  mg/m2, g/m2, IU/m2, units/m2:

if Pt Height or Weight not entered, Patient Specific dose should be displayed as (-- <Drug Units>)

if Pt Height and Weight entered, Patient Specific dose should be calculated as:  <Dose per Administration>* <Pt. BSA> (rounding: 2 decimal points, usual rounding rules)

If weight or height is updated, then Patient Specific dose should be re-calculated and displayed in the table

 |  | 
5 | Calculate Medical Billing Units per Authorization

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | The system shall calculate Max Billing Units/Auth for all Medical drugs, including Existing Regimen, Custom Regimen, and Ancillary drugs.

Required inputs shall include Allowed Dose, Adm. Per Day, Adm. Days Per Cycle, Cycle in Days, Duration per Authorization, and CMU BU configuration.

The system shall derive Cycles as Duration per Authorization divided by Cycle in Days, rounded up to the next whole number. in accordance with Cycles logic in DD

The system shall calculate Max Billing Units/Auth as
Allowed Dose &times; Adm. Per Day &times; Adm. Days Per Cycle &times; Cycles divided by CMU BU.

The result shall be rounded to two decimal places using standard rounding rules.

If any required input is missing, the system shall display "--".

Max Billing Units/Auth shall be system-calculated and read-only.

Value is stored for inclusion in medical auth files

 | CMU BU and Duration per Authorization must be sourced from Admin configuration.

Calculation must re-execute when Allowed Dose or any schedule field changes.

validatedGreen should consider this for future releases

Assumption: The Cycles value used for Max Billing Units/Auth is not the same as the Cycles field in the dosing data dictionary. It is a separate derived value, calculated from Duration per AP/Cycle in Days and rounded up to the next whole number.

validatedGreen  yes. Assumption: Billing unit size is defined in the Master Drug Library by the combination of Billable Unit and Billable UOM. Example: Billable Unit = 1 and Billable UOM = mg means one billing unit equals 1 mg.

 | 
6 | Calculate Pharmacy Quantity per Auth

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green   

 | The system shall calculate Quantity per Auth for all Pharmacy drugs, including Existing Regimen, Custom Regimen, and Ancillary drugs.

Required inputs shall include Dosage, Strength, Adm. Per Day, Adm. Days Per Cycle, Cycle in Days, and Duration per Authorization.

The system shall derive Cycles as Duration per Authorization divided by Cycle in Days, rounded up to the next whole number. in accordance with Cycles logic in DD

The system shall calculate Quantity per Auth as Dosage divided by Strength multiplied by Adm. Per Day multiplied by Adm. Days Per Cycle multiplied by Cycles.

The result shall be rounded to two decimal places using standard rounding rules.

If any required input is missing, the system shall display "--".

Quantity per Auth shall be system-calculated and read-only.

 | Duration per Authorization must be sourced from Admin configuration.

 | 
7 | Populate initial dosing details based on selected regimen details

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green   

 | Once the Medical and Pharmacy dosing tables are rendered for Existing Regimen, Custom Regimen, or Ancillary Drug, the system shall populate dosing table fields based on their defined source and population logic

For Medical Drugs:

If the drug is part of an Existing Regimen, the system shall populate:

HCPCS Code and Description from the Master Drug Library (MDL).

Dosing fields:

Dosage, Units, Adm. Per Day, Adm. Days Per Cycle, Cycles in Days, Cycles - Defaulted to corresponding values from the Regimen Library.

Allowed Dose &ndash; system calculated.

Max Billing Units/Auth &ndash; system calculated.

Status from the Payer Drug Library (PDL) - out of scope for this story

If the drug is part of a Custom Regimen or Ancillary Drug, the system shall 

populate:

HCPCS Code and Description from the Master Drug Library.

Dosing fields:

Dosage, Units, Adm. Per Day, Adm. Days Per Cycle, Cycles in Days, Cycles - blank by default:

Allowed Dose &ndash; blank by default, calculated after required inputs are entered.

Status from the Payer Drug Library  - out of scope for this story

For Pharmacy Drugs

If the drug is part of an Existing Regimen, the system shall populate:

HCPCS Code and Description from the Master Drug Library.

Dosing fields: 

Dosage, Adm. Per Day, Adm. Days Per Cycle, Cycles in Days, Cycles - defaulted to corresponding values from the Regimen Library.

Strength &ndash; blank by default; dropdown options sourced from Master Drug Library (Representative NDC rows &rarr; Strength).

Form &ndash; blank by default; dropdown options sourced from Master Drug Library (Representative NDC rows &rarr; RxNorm Dose Form).

Quantity per Auth &ndash; system calculated once required inputs are available.

Status from the Payer Drug Library  - out of scope for this story

If the drug is part of a Custom Regimen or Ancillary Drug, the system shall 

populate:

HCPCS Code and Description from the Master Drug Library.

Dosing fields: blank by default.

Status from the Payer Drug Library  - out of scope for this story

8 | Allow User Edits to Dosing with Guardrails

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | The system shall allow users to enter or edit dosing values in the dosing tables for drugs added via Existing Regimen, Custom Regimen, and Ancillary Drug workflows.

For Medical drugs, the system shall allow editing of Dosage, Units, Adm. Per Day, Adm. Days Per Cycle, Cycles in Days, and Cycles.

For Pharmacy drugs, the system shall allow editing of Dosage, Adm. Per Day, Adm. Days Per Cycle, Cycles in Days, and Cycles, and shall require user selection of Strength and Dose Form.

The system shall keep the following fields read-only because they are system-calculated: Patient Specific Dose or Allowed Dose (as applicable), Max Billing Units/Auth, and Quantity per Auth.

The system shall enforce required-field rules before the user can proceed or submit:

Medical drugs require Dosage, Units, and schedule fields needed for calculations.

Pharmacy drugs require Dosage, Strength, Dose Form, and schedule fields needed for calculations.

The system shall constrain user-selectable values to configured dropdown lists where applicable:

Units shall be limited to allowed Units for the drug.

Adm. Per Day shall be limited to the allowed list.

Cycles in Days shall be limited to the allowed list.

When a user edits a value that was defaulted from an Existing Regimen, the system shall indicate that the value differs from the default.

When a user changes any editable dosing field, the system shall immediately recalculate dependent system fields for that row once prerequisite inputs are present.

When the user switches HCPCS to another drug with the same ingredient, the system shall preserve user-entered dosing values and update only drug identity fields (e.g., HCPCS and Description).

If a user changes an input such that an already-selected dependent value becomes invalid (e.g., changing Strength makes the selected Dose Form invalid), the system shall clear the invalid value and require a new valid selection.

 | Maintain both Default Value and Current Value per editable field to support &ldquo;changed from default&rdquo; indicators and downstream guardrails.

 | 
9 | Indicate When Calculated Medical Billing Units Exceed Default

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | The system should compare the recalculated Max Billing Units/Auth value for each Medical drug row against the configured Default Max Billing Units per Duration for that drug.

The system should mark the row as Exceeds Default when:
Calculated Max Billing Units/Auth > Configured Default Max Billing Units per Duration.

The system should display a row-level visual indicator on the Medical drug row when the row is in Exceeds Default status.

The system should re-evaluate the Exceeds Default status immediately after recalculation completes whenever any input affecting Max Billing Units/Auth changes, including:

Allowed Dose

Adm. Per Day

Adm. Days Per Cycle

Cycles in Days

Cycles

Duration per Authorization

The system should remove the indicator automatically when the recalculated Max Billing Units/Auth is less than or equal to the configured default.

The system should apply this logic to Medical drugs added through Existing Regimen, Custom Regimen, and Ancillary Drug workflows.

The indicator should be informational only and should not block save, progression, or submission unless a separate business rule explicitly requires workflow gating.

The evaluated Exceeds Default result should be tied to the individual case-drug row and should not affect other drug rows on the case.

 | validateRed  Nichole

revisit user story

Clinical Data Revalidation and Configuration Refresh

 | Nicole

 | Revalidation triggers - US

The system should revalidate case-level drug configuration when a user changes drug-related or clinical/dosing data during Draft case editing.

Revalidation-triggering changes should include, at minimum:

adding a regimen drug

adding an ancillary drug

removing a drug

changing the selected regimen / protocol

editing drug dosing

editing other clinical data that drives drug configuration checks

If no relevant drug or clinical/dosing data has changed, the system should not perform an additional configuration refresh.

API refresh scope and timing - US

When revalidation runs, the system should send all drugs currently on the case in the refresh request, not only the drug currently being edited.

The request should include both:

regimen drugs

ancillary drugs

For V1, configuration refresh should occur on save within the case, not continuously during edit and not as a background push from Admin Portal changes.

Upstream configuration changes for open cases - US

If Admin Portal / PDL configuration changes after a case has already been entered, the system should not automatically push those changes into open cases in V1.

In V1, impacted open cases should be identified through operational reporting, not automatic case flagging.

Automatic identification / flagging of impacted open cases may be considered for a future release.

Auditability and supervisory override - US

The system should record refresh / revalidation activity in case change history.

Audit history should indicate that a refresh occurred and that configuration values changed as a result.

Supervisory users should have the ability to override drug-level determinations.

Supervisory override workflow should prevent save-triggered refresh from immediately overwriting a supervisor&rsquo;s manual determination.
