Goals & Business Objectives

Enable configuration of NewUM system behavior without need to connect to external systems, such as Admin Portal

NewUM must inherit all existing configuration points, so that current clients can be migrated from existing systems to NewUM in the future

Support configuration categories as specified in Configuration and rules categories - NewUM Product Team - Confluence 

Enable semi-technical (non-engineer) users to manage configurations through a centralized administrative configuration file or interface

Enable seamless creation of new configuration categories and configuration points to ensure any future business needs can be supported

Enable configuration changes to be implemented without need to code changes and time-consuming SDLC.

Decrease time-to-update

Increase visibility into configuration options

Enable robust audit log for configurations

Background & Current State

A configuration repository serves as a centralized "source of truth" for storing and managing the settings, parameters, and environment variables that govern how NewUM software should behave. Instead of hard-coding values or feature flags directly into the application code, configuration should be in an externalized storage separate from the codebase. 

This separation will allow non-engineering teams to update system&rsquo;s behavior in real-time without needing to recompile or redeploy the entire codebase.

By utilizing robust auditing, OncoHealth will be able to track every change made to their environments, providing a clear audit trail for compliance and security. 

Configuration repositories enable automated pipelines to pull the latest settings during deployment, reducing human error and manual configuration drift. Ultimately, they enhance system scalability and reliability by making the entire infrastructure landscape predictable, reproducible, and easy to roll back if a misconfiguration occurs.

Currently a part of the payer configurations is being managed through Admin Portal. While Admin Portal has a benefit of user-friendly UI, its drawback is that it&rsquo;s a 3rd party system and additional integration for pulling data at runtime would be needed, and NewUM's data dictionary would need to explicitly map out all configuration options. Another drawback is that adding new configuration points to Admin Portal requires dedicated engineering effort.

With that in mind, decision has been made to develop dedicated configuration management features within scope of the NewUM.

Functional Requirements

note073819dab089Term User in this section refers to a Semi-technical OncoHealth employee with administrative access to configuration management features. Term Semi-technical is used to describe a person who is not an software engineer but possesses certain degree of computer literacy and is comfortable managing configurations and rules via structured-text languages.

Term User in this section refers to a Semi-technical OncoHealth employee with administrative access to configuration management features. Term Semi-technical is used to describe a person who is not an software engineer but possesses certain degree of computer literacy and is comfortable managing configurations and rules via structured-text languages.

Configurations will be saved in NewUM database in form of JSON data type. Depending on solutioning details, configurations could be saved all in one JSON file or split in multiple JSON files. This will enable NewUM application and its rules engine most direct and rapid access, ensuring best performance and reducing complexity by removing need to access external systems databases to fetch configurations. 

Below is an example payer configuration with 2 categories:

wide760Please note - depending on engineering decisions, suggested structure of configuration JSON might be extended to support additional parameters.

Suggested approach will allow JSON data structures to support:

Each health plan having its own dedicated configuration set that can be managed independently.

Distinction between configuration name that can be referenced by the rule engine, and display name to be displayed to application end-users

Dataset can easily be extended with additional helpful data such as description, tooltips. Any additional data is automatically added to data dictionary and can be consumed by rules engine.

Configuration categorization 

Global level as suggested in Configuration and rules categories 

These configurations apply to all health plans utilizing NewUM software to support their PA workflows.

Health Plan level as suggested in Configuration and rules categories 

Configuration points can also be specified for lower grains of data for each payer: LoB, Plan Type, Product Line & Employer Group

Implementations of ValidFrom-ValidTo logic

Configuration status (active/inactive) can be set explicitly or determined by looking at validity interval

Adding new configuration categories and configuration points- in case of expanding business needs, additional configuration categories can simply be added or existing retired by simply editing a JSON file

Tagging - custom tags can be assigned to configuration record in order to facilitate additional categorization requirements in the future that might not be clear at this time

For phase 1 of the project, configurations will be managed by OH Admin user via dedicated what-you-see-what-you-get editor.

Example WYSWYG configuration editor

User in OH Admin role will be able to view and edit configurations.

Additional read-only access can be provided to users in other roles if needed.

All changes made on configuration files will be saved to audit log:

Events that will be captured by Aduit log: creation of new configurations, update of existing configurations, delete actions 

Data that will be captured by Audit log: who triggered the event, timestamp, what was changed (old & new state)

A default configuration set will be created based on https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5083987995/Configuration+Management#v1-Configuration-repository  , this default configuration set will be used as a starting point for explicit payer configuration when launching new tenants for new payers.

Dedicated test harness system that will be able to run automated test cases to ensure that updated configuration files are valid. On file save, automatic test will trigger to validate updated file. Automatic test harness will also support testing of multiple interdependent files.

Goals & Business Objectives

Background & Current State

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Priority

 | Description (Use Case Format)

 | Notes

 | 
User must select an ICD-10 code for the prior authorization

 | must haveRed  

 | Primary Actor: CRS, Provider Staff, Health Plan User

Supporting Systems: Admin Portal (Diagnosis Library + configuration metadata), NewUM Rules/Config services 

Goal: Capture a valid ICD-10 diagnosis and cancer stage for the prior authorization (PA) case so the request can be processed, routed, and transmitted correctly, and so downstream treatment selection can be appropriately constrained.

Scope: NewUM &rarr; Case Entry &rarr; Diagnosis & Clinical Indication

Trigger: User reaches the Diagnosis section while creating or editing a case.

Preconditions

User is authenticated and authorized to create/update the case.

Case context is available (at minimum: payer/program/line-of-business; and if required by flow, treatment type).

NewUM can access the Admin Portal diagnosis library 

Postconditions:

Success: Case stores:

selected ICD-10 code + description (as selected)

derived Diagnosis Group (grouper) mapped from Admin Portal

selected cancer stage (if required/available)

audit metadata (who/when) and reference to diagnosis catalog version

User can proceed to downstream steps (e.g., Treatment/Regimen selection).

Failure

Case does not advance; missing/invalid selections are highlighted.

System logs the reason (validation error or data dependency failure).

Main Flow (Happy Path)

Load diagnosis options: System loads ICD-10 codes from Admin Portal diagnosis library (or cache), including mapping to Diagnosis Group and applicability metadata (e.g., XRT/GMT flags).

(If applicable) Establish Treatment Type context: If the intake flow already has a selected Treatment Type (e.g., XRT, GMT), the system uses it to filter diagnosis options.

Search and select ICD-10: User searches by ICD-10 code and/or diagnosis keywords. System returns matching ICD-10 options (filtered per rules). User selects an ICD-10.

Derive and persist Diagnosis Group (grouper): System maps the chosen ICD-10 to the appropriate Diagnosis Group using Admin Portal mapping, stores it on the case, and displays diagnosis summary context.

pending decisionRed Present cancer stage choices: System displays a Cancer Stage field with options relevant to the selected diagnosis (and treatment type, if required). User selects a stage.

Validate and save: System validates all required fields and persists diagnosis + stage. User proceeds.

Alternate / Exception Flows

A1 - User changes ICD-10 after selecting stage: System clears stage and any dependent downstream selections (e.g., regimen) and requires re-selection of stage; re-derives Diagnosis Group.

A2 - Treatment type is selected/changed after ICD-10 selection: System re-validates diagnosis applicability to the treatment type. If invalid, system prompts user to select a valid ICD-10 for that treatment type and clears stage/dependents.

E1 - ICD-10 mapping to Diagnosis Group missing: System blocks progression and displays an error (&ldquo;Diagnosis mapping unavailable&rdquo;). Logs a data stewardship defect reference (Admin Portal).

E2 - Admin Portal unavailable / sync failure: System uses last known good cached library if present; otherwise blocks diagnosis selection and shows a recoverable error.

Business Rules

ICD-10 is required for PA: A case cannot be submitted without a selected ICD-10.

Diagnosis Group is system-derived, not user-entered: Diagnosis Group must be mapped from Admin Portal based on ICD-10 selection.

Treatment Type diagnosis constraints (XRT/GMT): Only diagnoses marked as valid for the selected treatment type (especially XRT/GMT) may be selected/retained.

Payer constrains: Only diagnoses marked as valid for the selected payer (health plan) may be selected/retained.

Stage is captured for clinical context but must NOT drive regimen search: Stage is not used to filter regimen library

Auditability: Store the diagnosis library version/timestamp used for the selection for traceability.

Configuration Dependencies (Admin Clinical Data / Config)

Admin Portal Diagnosis Library must provide (or NewUM must derive via config):

ICD-10 code + display text

ICD-10 &rarr; Diagnosis Group (grouper) mapping

Diagnosis applicability by Treatment Type (XRT vs GMT)

Optional payer scoping metadata (if supported/required)

Cancer Stage configuration must provide: Stage value set(s) and the rule for &ldquo;relevant to diagnosis&rdquo; (source TBD: Admin Portal)

 | ICD-10 is mandatory for prior authorization:

Required for claims

Required for authorization files

Always present on provider submissions and fax forms

Diagnosis name (cancer type) is helpful context, but not sufficient on its own.

In current systems:

SmartUM requires ICD-10 and derives the diagnosis group in the background.

MATIS historically required selecting diagnosis name first, then ICD-10.

Monarch experimented with allowing either.

MATIS = 1 dx only, SmartUM = allowes to have multiple diagnosis (primary and others)

For NewUM, the intent is to support an ICD-first selection flow, with diagnosis grouping handled automatically.

 | 
Populate available ICD-10 codes from Admin Portal diagnosis library

 | must haveRed  

 | The Admin Portal is the authoritative source (system of record)  for:

ICD-10 codes

Diagnosis names (diagnosis groupers)

Relationships between ICD-10 codes and diagnosis groupers

Treatment-type applicability (Chemo, XRT, GMT)

Payer-specific diagnosis constraints (where applicable)

The same diagnosis library is shared across SmartUM and Monarch, and NewUM is expected to consume this data rather than recreate it.

Any changes to the diagnosis library must consider downstream impact to SmartUM / Monarch, because:

ICD-10 data is extracted and sent downstream (e.g., auth files).

Some clients rely on existing diagnosis mappings.

 | 
Associated ICD-10 code to the appropriate diagnosis group from the Admin Portal

 | must haveRed  

 | Diagnosis groupers (e.g., Head & Neck, NSCLC) are:

Logical groupings of multiple ICD-10 codes

Maintained in the Admin Portal

Purpose of groupers:

Drive regimen availability and filtering

Reduce protocol / regimen bloat

Improve usability for clinical review and case scanning

Groupers are:

Derived, not user-editable

Determined automatically once ICD-10 is selected

Regimens are associated to diagnosis groupers, not to individual ICD-10 codes.

 | 
Ensure that only certain diagnoses that are appropriate for XRT and GMT can be associated with that treatment type

 | should haveYellow    

 | Treatment-Type-Specific Diagnoses ( XRT vs GMT)Some diagnoses are valid only for specific treatment types:

XRT-only diagnoses

GMT-only diagnoses

Non-oncology diagnoses used for XRT (e.g., RA)

The Admin Portal stores:

Treatment-type applicability at the diagnosis level

System behavior:

Diagnosis list must be filtered by treatment type

Invalid combinations must not be selectable

Examples discussed:

XRT diagnoses restricted by treatment type and sometimes payer/state

GMT diagnoses handled similarly

This filtering is required to:

Prevent incorrect case setup

Reduce downstream clinical corrections

Payer-Specific Diagnosis ConstraintsCertain diagnoses:

Are payer-specific

Exist due to historical agreements (e.g., unusual non-oncology diagnoses)

Admin Portal supports:

Payer-scoped diagnosis visibility

NewUM is expected to:

Respect payer-specific diagnosis applicability

Consume this logic rather than duplicating it

 | 
User can select from appropriate cancer stages based on chosen diagnosis

 | must haveRed  

 | Cancer stage is:

Captured during case entry

Clinically meaningful for reviewers

Explicit decision from meetings:

Stage must NOT be used to filter regimens

Using stage in regimen lookup caused severe protocol bloat in the past

Stage is:

Contextual information only

Used for clinical review and documentation

Not part of diagnosis-to-regimen matching logic

 | 
Apply payer restrictions on diagnoses - there are few diagnoses that are only used for certain health plans.

 | should haveYellow

Field Name

 | Description

 | Data Type

 | Validation Rules

Diagnosis Search

 | Allows the user to search for an ICD-10 diagnosis by code or description.

 | String 

 | User may search by:
-  full or partial ICD-10 code (e.g., &ldquo;C50&rdquo; returns C50.*)
-  by keyword in the description (e.g., &ldquo;breast&rdquo;). 
Search is case-insensitive. If multiple words are entered, results must contain all words. Only Active ICD-10 codes applicable to the case context are returned. User must select exactly one ICD-10 before proceeding.

 | 
Diagnosis Group (Derived)

 | System-derived diagnosis grouping associated with the selected ICD-10. Used for regimen search and downstream rule evaluation. May not be displayed to the user.

 | Object 

 | Automatically derived from ICD-10 mapping. Required once ICD-10 is selected. Must exist in reference data. Not editable by user. Updated only if ICD-10 changes.

 | 
ICD-10 Code (Selected)

 | The ICD-10 diagnosis code selected for the case.

 | String (ICD-10 format)

 | Required . Must exist in reference data. Must be mapped to a valid Diagnosis Group. Exactly one ICD-10 allowed per case (R1).

 | 
ICD-10 Description / Label

 | The description associated with the selected ICD-10 code. Stored for display and audit purposes.

 | String

 | Automatically populated from reference data upon ICD selection. Required once ICD-10 is selected. Not editable by user. Remains unchanged even if reference description changes later.

 | 
Cancer Stage pending decisionRed  

 | Cancer stage associated with the selected diagnosis. Captured for clinical context. Does not drive regimen filtering in R1.

 | Enum 

 | Required. Allowed values must come from the configured stage list applicable to the selected Diagnosis Group. Must be selected after ICD-10 selection. Cleared automatically if ICD-10 changes.

Diagnosis Group: Is Diagnosis Group a custom AP-defined grouping or based on a standard clinical classification? Is it global or payer-specific?

 | Nicole

 | Diagnosis Groups are custom, platform-defined groupings. They are based on NCCN, with some OncoHealth-specific combinations added to simplify maintenance. They are global across all payers and are not intended to be payer-specific at this time.

 | ResolvedGreen   

 | 
Cancer Stage: Is cancer stage associated at the ICD-10 level or Diagnosis Group level? Are stage values global or payer-specific?

 | Nicole / Alison

 

 | For NewUM, if stage granularity is introduced, cancer stage would be associated at the Diagnosis Group level, not the ICD-10 level. Possible values could include global values such as Stage I&ndash;IV, NA. This would need to be added in the Admin Portal. Nicole indicated this should be considered a future enhancement and is not required for MVP. Existing MATIS and SmartUM behavior differs, and final NewUM approach is still to be confirmed.

Feedback from Nicole:

Cancer StageMATIS current state (Dx and stage are tied together), SmartUM current state (Stage is not recorded), and preferred NewUM future state (TBD) are separate.  For NewUM, if we want to parse down to this level of granularity, Cancer stage can be associated at the Dx Group using a global Stage I-IV plus NA, Extensive, Limited, etc. but this would  need to be added at the AP level if we would like to add this level of granularity.  However, I would consider this for a future enhancement and not MVP necessary build.  It will always be applied as a clinical qualifier if added to NewUM. 

I was thinking about Stage more and think we may want to add to AP and allow to record for MVP.  As we continue forward, I believe the goal is to leverage AI to help with front end case processing.  In that instance, I think recording Stage would become much easier.

Cancer stage / diagnosis

Current Drugs API does not expose Cancer Stage.

Stage data currently exists in MATIS DB.

Decision required to agree on the option to support Cancer Stage in NewUM:

Option 1: expose the existing stage table through or add it to the Drugs API ( Bogdan/Jason King)

Option 2: add Cancer Stage configuration to Admin Portal and expose it through the Drugs API

Option 3: validate whether Cancer Stage is actually needed for V1, since it appears to be informational only and may not drive downstream logic(Alison)

decisionGreen

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Description

 | Notes

 | 
Search and select a main regimen from the Regimen Library using drug name(s), HCPCS codes

 | System must support search by generic drug name, brand drug name, HCPCS code, and regimen name (library-defined).

Search returns regimen-level results only (not individual drugs).

Only active regimens are searchable/selectable (effective + status driven).

Results list supports interactive search (typeahead/fuzzy/partial match); pagination/incremental load allowed.

Result row displays : Regimen name, abbreviated key drugs,

Exactly one main regimen must be selected per case.

Ancillary-only drugs must not appear as separate &ldquo;main regimen&rdquo; options.

 | Regimen data sourced from DrugsMS (Admin Portal UI). 
Search must support partial match. 
Respect effective dates and status from DrugsMS. 
Required before moving to dosing step.

 | 
List of regimens available to the user is limited to those associated with the diagnosis group

 | Regimen search must read the Diagnosis Group already stored on the case (derived from ICD-10 selection). 

Search results must be filtered to regimens mapped to that Diagnosis Group. 

If Diagnosis Group is missing, regimen selection must be blocked. 

 | Diagnosis Group derived from Admin Portal ICD-10 mapping earlier in flow. 
Regimen &harr; Diagnosis mapping maintained in DrugsMS. 
This is a hard constraint.

 | 
System saves the regimen and drug records to the case

 | On Save, system must persist selected regimen and all associated regimen drug rows. 

Persist regimen identifier and source version/effective context (if available). 

Persist each drug row including: regimen identifier, regimen drugs, default drugs dosing metadata

Save points:

Save Regimen on Save (draft persistence; user can navigate away and return).

Save Regimen on Submit (final validation + persistence required for submission).

Save/Submit failure must rollback completely.

 | Snapshot stored in NewUM Case + Drugs schema. 
Persist enough identifiers to:

rehydrate dosing tables 

support later alternative-drug switching 

 | 
User can switch between drugs in a regimen where multiple drugs have the same associated RxCUI in the regimen build

 | Switching is available only after a main regimen has been selected and dosing table is populated.

Switching is enabled only for regimen drugs where:

The drug is built off Ingredient (IN) or Precise Ingredient (PIN) RxCUI.

Multiple billable drug options exist sharing the same RxCUI.

The system identifies alternative drugs based on Shared RxCUI at IN or PIN level.

If only one eligible billable option exists, the switching control is hidden or disabled.

The alternative drug dropdown:

Displays drug name and HCPCS code (minimum).

Defaults to generic drug when available.

Groups and orders options as follows:

Generic IV (alphabetical)

Generic Other (incl PO) (alphabetical)

Brand (incl 505(b)(2) and brand-name orals) (alphabetical)

Biosimilars (alphabetical)

 | notef08e3843ec97The Regimen Library API explicitly supports alternative-drug retrieval via GetAlternativeDrugs, which returns alternatives based on Ingredient RxCUI or Precise Ingredient RxCUI.

The Regimen Library API explicitly supports alternative-drug retrieval via GetAlternativeDrugs, which returns alternatives based on Ingredient RxCUI or Precise Ingredient RxCUI.

 | 
Drugs from the Master Drug Library (MDL) that have the 'EADL' flag are not selectable in the regimen drug selection

 | In the alternative-drug dropdown (switching list), exclude any drug flagged EADL in the MDL (&ldquo;Excluded from alternate drug list&rdquo;).

If all alternatives are EADL/invalid, hide/disable switching for that row.

 | EADL is maintained by clinical team in MDL (DrugsMS-backed) and must be enforced when presenting switch options.

Treat as a hard filter: EADL drugs never appear as selectable alternatives, even if they match RxCUI grouping.

Drug Concept

How Drugs, Brands, Codes, and Regimens Connect

Relevant Clinical Data Libraries in Admin Portal

Admin Library

 | Purpose / Data Source Role

 | Screenshots from Admin

 | 
Regimen Library (Published Chemotherapy)

 | Source of truth for regimen definitions + variants + regimen-level metadata (effective dates/status, NCCN linkages, dosing defaults shown in the regimen details). Stored in DrugsMS and surfaced via Admin Portal UI.

 |  | 
Master Drug Library (MDL)

 | Source of truth for drug identifiers and attributes used for billing + switching logic: HCPCS, RxCUI (Ingredient/Precise Ingredient/Brand), Benefit Type, NDC/GPI linkages, and EADL flag used to exclude non-appropriate alternatives. Stored in DrugsMS and surfaced via Admin Portal UI.

 |  | 
Diagnosis Library / ICD-10 &rarr; Diagnosis Group mapping

 | Drives regimen filtering by Diagnosis Group (case derives group from ICD-10 selection; regimen search uses this context). (Your earlier Dx PRD establishes this dependency.)

User Stories 

The user stories listed below represent V1.0 implementation candidates only.
Each story is prioritized using the MoSCoW model:

Must Have &ndash; required for the workflow to function in V1.0

Should Have &ndash; important, but not required for initial operability

Could Have &ndash; optional enhancements, deferred if needed

User Story Title

 | Priority

 | Acceptance criteria

 | Notes

 | 
1 | Select Assignment Type

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | After Diagnosis and cancer stage selection is successful, the user should be able to proceed with treatment type (assignment) selection

The following treatment types (assignments) should be available:

Assign Chemo to Patient (v1.r1.Green ) 

Assign Radiation to Patient (v1.r2.) )

Assign Test to Patient  (v1.r2.) )

Each action represents a distinct assignment type.

Selecting an assignment action initiates the corresponding assignment workflow.

Selecting an assignment action routes the user to the appropriate assignment entry screen.

The selected assignment type is recorded as part of the case context.

The user cannot proceed to assignment details without selecting one of the assignment actions.

Technical Considerations

Each assignment type has different data points associated with it and routes to a different workflow, even though many workflow steps are similar.

 | Each Treatment Type should map to a distinct workflow configuration and associated data model.

 | 
2 | Retrieve Diagnosis-Scoped Regimens from Regimen Library 

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green   

 | Retrieval of regimens from the Regimen Library.

Filtering regimens based on Diagnosis Group stored on the case.

Ensuring only active and effective regimens are returned.

No Diagnosis selection logic (precondition: Diagnosis Group exists).

 |  | 
3 | Search Regimens by Drug Composition (Drug Name or HCPCS) 

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | Search operates on drugs included in the regimen build.

Supports:

Generic drug names

Brand drug names

HCPCS codes

Results remain limited to regimens associated with the case&rsquo;s Diagnosis Group:

The system shall display each Existing Regimen search result as a single normalized regimen title:

 the system should not show the Diagnosis Group in the result row.

the system should not show protocol-status values (for example, Auto, Non-Auto, S2)

The system shall use the descriptive text inside parentheses from the Admin Portal regimen label as the preferred regimen display name

If the descriptive parenthetical text cannot be extracted reliably, the system shall display the full Admin Portal regimen label as fallback and shall not show a truncated, partially parsed, or reconstructed title.

Search should support partial match (fuzzy/typeahead behavior):

The system shall return diagnosis-filtered regimen results when the user enters at least 3 characters of a regimen-related search term, including partial text matches on HCPCS code or drug name.

The system shall support limited typo tolerance for drug-name searches only and shall rank exact HCPCS code matches and exact drug-name matches above partial or approximate matches.

Search does not modify case data.

 | Example

Source Admin Portal label
carboplatin, paclitaxel, pembrolizumab (Pembrolizumab + Weekly PACLitaxel + Weekly CARBOplatin (Neoadjuvant Course 1 for Early Stage TNBC))

Expected display
Pembrolizumab + Weekly PACLitaxel + Weekly CARBOplatin (Neoadjuvant Course 1 for Early Stage TNBC)

Valid fallback if extraction is not reliable
carboplatin, paclitaxel, pembrolizumab (Pembrolizumab + Weekly PACLitaxel + Weekly CARBOplatin (Neoadjuvant Course 1 for Early Stage TNBC))

 | 
4 | Select Main Regimen and Persist Regimen + Drug Records to Case 

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green   

 | User can search regimens by drug name(s) (brand or generic) and HCPCS codes

Regimen list is limited to those associated with the case Diagnosis Group (from Admin Portal)

Cancer stage does not filter regimen results

Selected regimen and its drug records are saved to the case

Regimen selection pre-populates dosing tables with default values from Admin Portal

 |  | 
5 | Allow Switching Between Equivalent Regimen Drugs Based on Shared RxCUI

 | must haveRed  v1.r1.Green  

 | Applies after a main regimen has been selected.

Applies within the populated dosing table.

Allows selection of alternate drugs through the HCPCS code field.

If a regimen contains drugs sharing the same Ingredient or Precise Ingredient RxCUI, user can switch between them

Switching must be auditable

out of scope for this story 

Switching must preserve clinical equivalency (RxCUI unchanged)

Switching affects billing representation only

Switching triggers recalculation + status refresh  

 |  | 
6 | Exclude EADL-Flagged Drugs from re

 | must haveRed v1.r1.Green   

 | Applies during  drug switching.

Evaluates EADL indicator from drug reference dataset.

Prevents EADL-flagged drugs from appearing as selectable alternatives.

Drugs flagged as EADL (Excluded from Alternate Drug List) in MDL are not selectable during regimen drug selection

System prevents saving a regimen with EADL drugs selected

UX

<>

Rules related UX/UI requirements:

UI needs to support 2 tiered error handling:

Critical error - error message should be displayed to user and user should not be allowed to proceed to next step in the workflow

Example: &ldquo;Payer X requires clinical reviewer to be explicitly named. Please populate Reviewed By field in order to proceed&rdquo;

Warning - warning message should be displayed to user, but user should be able either ignore or explicitly confirm they would like to proceed to next step in the workflow

Example: &ldquo;Selected administrations per cycle and entered cycle length don't match entered maximum dosage, are you sure you want to proceed?&rdquo;

Business rules related notifications/tooltips

Example: while creating a case for payer A, user selects regiment B, which contains drug C. That triggers the system to display notification/tooltip/other related to field &ldquo;Payer A requires a phone call validation for drug C. Please call payer customer service on 123-456-7890&rdquo;

Glossary

Attribute

 | Type

 | Meaning & Relationship to Other Attributes

 | 
RxNorm

 | Clinical Standard

 | U.S. National Library of Medicine standard vocabulary that normalizes drug names and assigns unique identifiers (RxCUI). Serves as the foundational mapping layer between clinical drug identity and billing identifiers (HCPCS, NDC).

 | 
RxCUI

 | Clinical Identity 

 | Unique identifier for a drug concept in RxNorm. Used as the clinical equivalency key. Drugs sharing the same IN or PIN RxCUI are considered clinically equivalent for switching purposes. Switching must preserve RxCUI.

 | 
TTY (Term Type)

 | Clinical Identity rity

 | Defines the level of drug concept (IN = Ingredient, PIN = Precise Ingredient, SCD = Clinical Drug, SBD = Branded Drug). Regimens are typically built at IN or PIN level. Determines how equivalency sets are constructed.

 | 
Ingredient (IN)

 | Clinical Identity

 | Base active substance of the drug. All alternatives sharing the same IN RxCUI represent the same core therapy. Used when broader equivalency is acceptable.

 | 
Precise Ingredient (PIN)

 | Clinical Identity

 | More specific ingredient form (e.g., salt or ester). Used for finer-grained equivalency. EADL exclusion logic references PIN-level grouping.

 | 
Generic Drug Name

 | Clinical Identity 

 | Standard scientific name used as default display and default selection in alternative dropdown. Often corresponds to IN-level concept.

 | 
Brand Name

 | Clinical Identity 

 | Manufacturer-specific marketed name. Associated with a specific HCPCS or NDC. Used to distinguish billing representations within same RxCUI group.

 | 
Biosimilar Indicator

 | Clinical Classification

 | Identifies drug as biosimilar to a reference biologic. Biosimilars share RxCUI equivalency but differ in manufacturer and billing code. Ordering logic places biosimilars last in dropdown.

 | 
Drug Type Classification

 | UI / Clinical Classification

 | Categorizes drug as Generic IV, Generic Other (incl PO), Brand, or Biosimilar. Used solely for dropdown grouping and ordering logic. Derived from route + product classification.

 | 
Strength

 | Clinical Specification

 | Amount of drug per unit (e.g., 150 mg). Used with dosage form and route to define billable product. May influence quantity-per-cycle calculations.

 | 
Dosage Form

 | Clinical Specification

 | Physical form (vial, tablet, solution). Must align with route of administration and billing code. Switching may change strength/form combination but must remain RxCUI-consistent.

 | 
Route of Administration

 | Clinical Specification

 | Method of administration (IV, PO, SQ). Impacts benefit classification and billing logic. Also contributes to Drug Type Classification grouping.

 | 
EADL Flag

 | Alternative Control

 | &ldquo;Excluded from Alternative Drug List.&rdquo; If flagged, drug must not appear in alternative dropdown even if it shares RxCUI with others. Maintained in MDL; enforced in NewUM.

 | 
Benefit Type

 | Coverage Classification

 | Indicates whether drug is covered under Medical, Pharmacy, or Crossover. Determines which dosing table the drug appears in and how billing method is selected.

 | 
Billing Method

 | Billing Execution Logic

 | Defines how claim is processed (e.g., Buy & Bill vs Pharmacy claim). Derived from Benefit Type; affects downstream billing identifiers and calculation logic.

 | 
HCPCS Code

 | Medical Billing Identifier

 | Code used for medical benefit billing. Multiple HCPCS codes may exist for drugs sharing same RxCUI. Switching changes HCPCS but not RxCUI.

 | 
NDC

 | Pharmacy Billing Identifier

 | 11-digit code identifying specific packaged drug product. Used when Benefit Type is Pharmacy. May change when switching within same RxCUI set.

 | 
GPI

 | Pharmacy Classification Identifier

 | Pharmacy benefit classification code used for formulary and claim adjudication logic. Derived from RxCUI or product configuration.

 | 
Representative NDC

 | Outbound Identifier

 | Default NDC used in outbound authorization files when Pharmacy benefit applies.

 | 
Billing Unit

 | Billing Logic

 | Measurement unit used for claim calculation (mg, vial, unit). Must align with strength and HCPCS configuration.

 | 
Max Billing Units

 | Billing Constraint

 | Upper limit allowed per cycle for billing. Used in calculation validation.

 | 
PA Required Indicator

 | Review Control

 | Indicates drug requires prior authorization review. Evaluated after benefit scoping.

 | 
PA Exempt Indicator

 | Review Control

 | Indicates drug bypasses medical necessity review.

 | 
Out of Scope Indicator

 | Scope Control

 | Indicates drug should not be reviewed by UM for this payer/program.

 | 
Non-Preferred (NP)

 | Payer Attribute

 | Indicates non-preferred formulary status. May block auto-approval logic.

 | 
Quantity Limit Indicator

 | Payer Attribute

 | Indicates payer-imposed quantity limit rules.

 | 
Dose Calculation Method

 | Dosing Logic

 | Defines how dose is calculated (mg/m&sup2;, mg/kg, flat). Depends on patient height/weight inputs.

 | 
Calculated Dose

 | Dosing Output

 | System-calculated dose per administration. Used to derive Quantity per Cycle.

 | 
Number of Cycles

 | Dosing Plan

 | Planned number of treatment cycles.

 | 
Frequency

 | Dosing Plan

 | Interval between doses (e.g., every 21 days).

 | 
Quantity per Cycle

 | Billing Calculation Output

 | Derived billing quantity based on calculated dose, strength, and billing unit. Must recalculate if alternative product is selected.

 | 
Loading Dose Indicator

 | Dosing Variant

 | Indicates presence of a loading dose before maintenance schedule.

Goals & Business Objectives

TBD

Background & Current State

TBD

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Description (Use Case Format)

 | Notes

 | 
Member Search

 | Goal: Accurately identify the correct member at the start of Case Entry to ensure Oncology UM intake is initiated for the intended individual, prevent HIPAA violations, and avoid downstream rework caused by incorrect member selection.

Primary Actors: Provider Office Staff (Provider Portal),  CRS, CRR (NewUM)

Preconditions:

Intake has been initiated via an approved intake channel (web, phone, fax).

Required intake information is available (payer context and member identifiers).

The user is authenticated and authorized.

The user&rsquo;s visibility is limited to health plans they are permitted to access. 

Product Team Decision Log 

Trigger: The user initiates a new oncology authorization request  and must identify the member who is requesting oncology treatment.

Main Flow (Happy Path &ndash; Member Found)

The user enters member search criteria as part of Case Entry, including health plan, member date of birth, and either member ID or partial name information

The system searches existing health-plan-provided eligibility data for members associated with health plans the user is authorized to access. 

The system identifies a single matching eligibility record.

The system opens the Member Information Form and pre-populates available member demographic and eligibility information from the eligibility record.

Case Entry proceeds to complete member information. - Product Team Decision Log 

Alternative Flows: 

A1. Member Not Found

The system determines that no existing member meets the search criteria.

The system informs the user that no member was found.

The user may proceed to initiate a new member record through manual data entry, subject to payer and program rules.  - Product Team Decision Log 

Only CRS users may initiate a new member record via manual entry

External users cannot create member records. 

Intake continues under the complete member information use case.

A2: https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5078581249/Member+Identification+and+Coverage#Edge-Cases-%2F-Additional-Scenarios%3A 

Exception Flows

E1. Unauthorized Health Plan Access: If an eligibility record exists under a health plan outside the user&rsquo;s authorized access, the system does not return or display that record. Case Entry cannot proceed under the current user context.

Postconditions:

If Success: A member record is initiated and associated with an existing member, or a new member pending manual entry.

If Failure: No member record is initiated and Case Entry does not proceed.

Business Rules - https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5078581249/Member+Identification+and+Coverage#Business-Rules  

Data Dictionary - https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5078581249/Member+Identification+and+Coverage#Member-Search.1 

 | REQUIRES DISCUSSION

Dual Eligibility Handling:
Rules for surfacing and selecting dual-eligible members (e.g., DSNP) require further definition. (Product Team Decision Log )

Manual Member Creation:
CRS SMEs indicate this is currently cumbersome and time-intensive. A decision is required on whether this remains a standard capability.

Provider Web Entry Guidance:
Guidance for providers when a member cannot be found requires definition.

Edge Cases / Additional Scenarios:

Coverage continuity across plan years for retrospective and concurrent cases
A member may have multiple eligibility records spanning different plan years, where prior-year coverage is no longer present in current inbound data. Member Search may be executed for retrospective or concurrent cases in which the treatment start date falls within a prior coverage period rather than the member&rsquo;s currently active eligibility (e.g., treatment started in December 2025, case created in January 2026).

Missing member identifier from Health Plans
Some Health Plans do not provide a persistent member identifier, resulting in multiple eligibility records that cannot be reliably linked (e.g., same name and DOB appearing as separate records).

Multiple eligibility records for the same individual
The same individual may appear as multiple eligibility records due to renewals, benefit tier changes, or enrollment file behavior (e.g., annual re-enrollment creates a new record).

Dual eligibility under the same Health Plan
A member may have more than one active eligibility record under the same Health Plan due to dual coverage arrangements (e.g., Medicare primary with supplemental commercial coverage).

Dual Special Needs Plan (DSNP) representation
DSNP members may be represented as a single eligibility record with indicators rather than separate Medicare and Medicaid records (e.g., one record flagged as DSNP).

 | 
Complete Member Information (Initiate Draft Case Creation)

 | Goal: Ensure all required member demographic, contact, and coverage information is completed to allow Case Entry to proceed for an PA request.

Primary Actors: Provider Office Staff (Provider Portal),  CRS, CRR (NewUM)

Preconditions:

Search for Member has completed. An existing member was found and member information is pre-populated OR

No member was found and Create Member was initiated. 

Trigger: Completion of the member identification process resulting in either an identified member or initiation of a new member 

Main Flow: 

Existing Member Found:

The system displays member demographic, contact, and coverage information pre-populated from available member data. 

The user reviews the displayed information. 

The user enters any missing required fields.

The user saves the member information.

New Member :

The system displays the Member Information section with all required fields empty. 

The user manually enters all required member demographic, contact, and coverage information. 

The user saves the member information.

Alternative Flows: If one or more required member information fields are missing or incomplete, the system does not allow Case Entry to move to the next step. The system indicates which information is missing. The user may enter the missing information and attempt to continue.

Exception Flows: If the user cannot provide all required member information during the intake interaction, the system allows the Case Entry to be saved as a draft with incomplete member information.

Postconditions:

If all required member information is completed, the information is saved and Case Entry moves to the next step.

If required member information is not completed, Case Entry does not move to the next step and remains in draft status.

 | Assumption to Validate &mdash; Treatment Timing Availability

Treatment Start Date will be captured during Case Entry rather than during Protocol Assignment, in order to support eligibility verification against the planned treatment start date.

 | 
Verify Eligibility

 | Goal: Determine whether the member has active health plan eligibility for the requested oncology treatment as of the planned treatment start date, in order to decide whether Case Entry may continue.

Primary Actors: Provider Office Staff (Provider Portal),  CRS, CRR (NewUM)

Preconditions: A member has been identified or created. 

Trigger: member information has been completed and saved with Treatment Start Date.
Main Flow (Happy Path):

The system evaluates the member&rsquo;s eligibility by comparing the planned Treatment Start Date to the member&rsquo;s eligibility effective and expiration dates and enrollment information. 

Eligibility is active for the Treatment Start Date. 

The system allows Case Entry to proceed to scope validation.

Alternative Flows: If eligibility data indicates coverage is not active for the planned Treatment Start Date, the system allows Case Entry to continue when an eligibility override is applied, if override is permitted for the health plan and user role. tbdRed 

Exception Flows: If eligibility data is not available for evaluation, the system does not allow Case Entry to proceed beyond eligibility verification.

Postconditions:

If eligibility is active for the planned Treatment Start Date, or an eligibility override is applied, Case Entry proceeds to the next step.

If eligibility cannot be evaluated, Case Entry does not proceed beyond eligibility verification.

 | Eligibility Override Support

Case Entry may support an Eligibility Override option to allow case creation when eligibility verification indicates the member is not eligible, subject to payer configuration and operational rules. The availability, conditions, and users permitted to apply an eligibility override require validation.

 | 
Validate Scope for OH Review  

out of scope for r1Blue 

 | Primary Actor: Provider Office Staff (Provider Portal),  CRS, CRR (NewUM)

Supporting Systems: Eligibility Data Source, Payer Configuration (Scope Rules), Rules Engine

User Goal: To determine whether a member and requested coverage are in scope for OncoHealth (OH) review before proceeding with case intake.

Trigger: User performs member search and initiates eligibility validation during prior authorization intake.

Preconditions:

User is authenticated.

Member search criteria have been entered.

Eligibility data is retrieved from the eligibility source.

Payer and line of business are identified.

Postconditions

Success &ndash; In Scope

Member is confirmed as in scope for OH review.

Case intake may proceed to treatment entry.

Success &ndash; Out of Scope

Member or coverage is identified as out of scope.

Case is flagged as Out of Scope.

User is informed that OH review will not proceed.

No further clinical intake steps are required.

Main Flow

Scope determination can be initiated only after eligibility verification returns outcome Eligible:

Scope determination is driven by payer configuration and eligibility attributes.

Out-of-scope status supersedes treatment and dosing review.

Out-of-scope cases do not trigger OH clinical review workflows.

Scope determination uses eligibility attributes received from the Health Plan for the eligible member.

Scope determination is executed in the context of the selected Health Plan and payer configuration defined in the Admin Portal.

The system evaluates the member&rsquo;s eligibility attributes required by payer configuration, including (when present): Line of Business, Product Line, Product Offering, State of Plan Issue, Carrier ID, Account ID, Insurance Group ID, Benefit Package, ASO Indicator, Member Benefit.

If any evaluated attribute matches a payer-configured carve-out condition or indicates non-delegation for OncoHealth review, the system returns outcome Out of Scope.

If no carve-out condition is met, the system returns outcome In Scope.

Scope determination occurs prior to draft case creation and prior to any clinical workflows.

If the outcome is In Scope, the user may proceed to draft case creation.

If the outcome is Out of Scope, the system blocks progression to standard case creation and returns an Out-of-Scope outcome.

The system records the scope outcome and the eligibility attributes used for the evaluation for audit

Alternate / Exception Flows

No Data Available: Case cannot proceed until resolved

Scope (Member In/Out of Scope) Validation Rules:1. Rule Name: Line of Business Validation

Rule Description: Validates that the member&rsquo;s Line of Business (LOB) is active and delegated for OncoHealth review under the selected Health Plan.

Step: Determine Member Scope

Event: Eligibility verification returns Eligible

Conditions:

Eligibility field: Line of Business

Admin configuration: Active LOB defined for the selected Health Plan

LOB must exist and be marked Active

Action:

Success: Matching active LOB found &rarr; Continue to next rule

Fail: No matching active LOB &rarr; Outcome = Out of Scope

2. Rule Name: Product Line / Product Offering Validation

Rule Description: Validates that the member&rsquo;s Product Line and/or Product Offering are active and delegated under the matched LOB.

Step: Determine Member Scope

Event: LOB validation successful

Conditions:

Eligibility fields: Product Line, Product Offering

Admin configuration: Active Product Line / Product Offering under the matched LOB

Action:

Success: Matching active Product configuration found &rarr; Continue

Fail: No matching or inactive configuration &rarr; Outcome = Out of Scope

3. Rule Name: State of Plan Issue Restriction

Rule Description: Validates that the member&rsquo;s State of Plan Issue is supported for delegation under payer configuration.

Step: Determine Member Scope

Event: Product validation successful

Conditions:

Eligibility field: State of Plan Issue

Admin configuration: Allowed states defined (if applicable)

Action:

Success: State allowed or no restriction configured &rarr; Continue

Fail: State not allowed &rarr; Outcome = Out of Scope

4. Rule Name: Identifier-Based Scope Validation

Rule Description: Validates eligibility identifiers against configured allowed or carve-out populations.

Step: Determine Member Scope

Event: State validation successful (or not applicable)

Conditions: 

Eligibility fields: Carrier ID, Account ID, Insurance Group ID, Benefit Package (if configured)

Admin configuration: Allowed identifiers, Configured carve-out identifiers

Action:

Success: Identifier matches allowed configuration and does not match carve-out &rarr; Continue

Fail: Identifier does not match allowed configuration OR matches carve-out &rarr; Outcome = Out of Scope

5. Rule Name: ASO Delegation Rule

Rule Description: Determines whether ASO populations are delegated to OncoHealth.

Step: Determine Member Scope

Event: Identifier validation successful (or not applicable)

Conditions:

Eligibility field: ASO Indicator

Admin configuration: ASO delegation setting

Action:

Success: ASO delegated or ASO Indicator = No &rarr; Continue

Fail: ASO Indicator = Yes AND ASO excluded from delegation &rarr; Outcome = Out of Scope

6. Rule Name: Benefit-Level Delegation Rule

Rule Description: Validates whether the member&rsquo;s Medical and Pharmacy benefits are delegated to OncoHealth for review.

Step: Determine Member Scope

Event: ASO validation successful (or not applicable)

Conditions: 

Eligibility fields: Medical Benefit, Pharmacy Benefit, Prescription Benefit Carve-Out, OON Benefit

Admin configuration: Pharmacy Benefit Out-of-Scope setting, Prescription carve-out configuration, OON delegation configuration

Action:

Success: Benefits configured as delegated &rarr; Outcome = In Scope

Fail:

Medical Benefit not applicable for oncology review

Pharmacy Benefit marked Out-of-Scope

Prescription Benefit Carve-Out = Yes

OON Benefit excluded from delegation
&rarr; Outcome = Out of Scope

Identifies the business rules applicable to this feature(-s) and links to the centralized Rules Inventory where rule definitions are maintained. This section enables traceability while avoiding duplication of rule logic within the PRD.

Member Level RulesUser Stories 

The user stories listed below represent V1.0 implementation candidates only.
Each story is prioritized using the MoSCoW model:

Must Have &ndash; required for the workflow to function in V1.0

Should Have &ndash; important, but not required for initial operability

Could Have &ndash; optional enhancements, deferred if needed

2 | Search for a member using required inputs (guardrails)

 | must haveRed 

 | Member Search is available during Case Entry and requires Health Plan + Date of Birth + (Member ID or First & Last Name). Users may search only within authorized Health Plans.

Member Search requires Health Plan + Date of Birth + (Member ID or First & Last Name) and is limited to authorized Health Plans.

Validation & Matching enforce only allowed search combinations with strict matching when multiple identifiers are provided (no fuzzy logic).

Configuration applies payer Admin Portal rules at runtime, including mandatory Max Member ID Length and optional Member ID pattern and messaging.

Outcomes return Found / Not Found, log results, and exclude duplicate resolution, coverage span handling, and downstream case processing from R1.

For R1, the assumption is that all users have access to all health plans.

 | Multiple Eligibility Records / Coverage Spans

Current system handles this poorly

Preferred future model:

One member record with multiple eligibility records behind it

System selects applicable eligibility later based on context (e.g., treatment start date)

Continuous coverage periods should ideally be merged

Non-continuous coverage periods should remain separate eligibility records

Key dependency:

Requires member identifier from Health Plans

If not provided (legacy plans), system cannot safely reconcile records

4 | Validate Member Eligibility at Treatment Start Date

 | must haveRed 

 

 | When eligibility verification is triggered, the system evaluates member coverage at the Treatment Start Date (mandatory field in Member Information Form

If multiple eligibility records exist, the system selects the applicable eligibility record(s) based on the Treatment Start Date.

If at least one eligibility record is active for the Treatment Start Date, the member is considered eligible.

If no eligibility record is active for the Treatment Start Date, the system returns a &ldquo;Not Eligible at Time of Service&rdquo; outcome and blocks further progression.

Eligibility verification outcome is recorded for audit.

Considerations

Treatment Start Date is the authoritative reference date for eligibility verification.

Dual eligibility may result in more than one active record on the Treatment Start Date; R1 assumes eligibility passes if at least one valid record exists.

No eligibility override is allowed in R1.

 | Treatment Start Date Timing

Only Blue Cross currently verifies eligibility against treatment start date

Treatment start date does not need to be captured during Member Search

Eligibility verification can occur later in the flow

Inclusive/exclusive rules for effective and expiration dates must be defined tbdRed : 

Whether the expiration date should always be treated as inclusive, or if any Health Plans require exclusive handling.

How to handle eligibility records with no expiration date (assumed active until further notice vs invalid).

Whether inclusive/exclusive rules should be:

Global (same for all Health Plans), or

Configurable per Health Plan.

How to handle overlapping eligibility records that are both active on the Treatment Start Date. 

 |

6 | Create Draft Case and Save Progress

 | must haveRed 

  

 | The system allows creation of a Draft Case once minimum prerequisites are met (member identified, eligible, in scope).

The user may choose one of two actions:

Create a draft case and remain on the current step.

Create a draft case and proceed directly to Diagnosis and Treatment selection.

Draft Case creation persists all data captured to date and assigns a unique case identifier.

The user may return later to resume case entry from the draft.

Considerations

Draft cases must support attachment carry-forward from earlier steps.

No downstream clinical review, determination, or routing occurs until the case is submitted (out of scope for this story).

 | Define the minimum required data set for draft case creation tbdRed

8 | Determine Member Scope (In-Scope vs Carve-Out)

 | must haveRed 

 

 | The system determines whether the eligible member/request is In Scope or Out of Scope (Carve-Out) for OncoHealth review.

Scope determination is based on configured rules tied to the selected eligibility context.

If In Scope, the user may proceed to draft case creation.

If Out of Scope, the system blocks progression to standard case creation and returns an Out-of-Scope outcome.

 | tbdRed  : Define scope determination rules and coverage attributes, such as:

Line of Business

Employer Group / Benefit Package

State of Plan Issue

Should a case record be created at all?

Scope logic must be configuration-driven and auditable.

9 | Attach Documents

 | should haveYellow

 | The system allows the user to attach documents as part of Case Entry and associate them to the in-progress work (draft case once created; otherwise session context if draft not yet created): 

https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5078581249/Member+Identification+and+Coverage#Attach-Documents  - Data Dictionary

For each uploaded document, the user must specify Document Type from a configured list 

The system stores and displays document metadata, including at minimum: document name, document type, date/time attached, attached by, and status.

Attached documents can be viewed/downloaded based on user authorization.

If a document upload fails, the system provides a clear failure outcome and does not mark the document as successfully attached.

 | 
10 | Enforce Member Visibility Based on User Authorization

 | should haveYellow  

 | The system determines the set of Health Plans a user is authorized to access based on the user&rsquo;s identity and entitlements.

Only authorized Health Plans are presented to the user for selection during Member Search.

Member Search requests are executed only within the scope of the selected, authorized Health Plan.

Member data associated with unauthorized Health Plans is not retrievable, returned, or inferred under any circumstances.

Authorization rules are enforced server-side and cannot be bypassed by client-side input manipulation.

Search behavior does not disclose the existence of members outside the user&rsquo;s authorized scope.

Authorization enforcement is consistent across all supported search input combinations.

Authorization decisions and denied access attempts are logged for audit and security purposes.

 | 02/02 ACS: We have an open decision (#2) on defining the policy around this. This could have a dependency on understanding user roles and security, which will be a separate Epic. We may move this to R2. 

 | 
11 | View/Edit Member Information Form When Multiple Matches Are Returned

 | should haveYellow

    

 | When Member Search identifies a member, the system displays the Member Information form once, even if multiple eligibility records exist for that member.

The system represents the member as a single member  entity, with eligibility information reflecting one or more associated eligibility records.

The system does not require the user to select a specific eligibility record at this stage.

Eligibility details are displayed to provide visibility only; no eligibility prioritization or selection occurs at this step.

The user may proceed to enter the Treatment Start Date and trigger eligibility verification.

Considerations

tbdRed UI/UX for displaying multiple eligibility records

Preferred model: one member with multiple eligibility records behind it.

Continuous coverage periods should be treated as a single coverage span where possible; non-continuous periods remain separate.

If a Health Plan&ndash;provided member identifier is not available (legacy plans), the system may not be able to reliably group eligibility records; behavior in such cases must be defined (TBD).

No eligibility filtering or resolution is performed in this story.

 | validateRed  Member Search Results - Edge Cases:

Multiple coverage spans for the same member (effective date handling): A single member may have multiple eligibility records with different coverage effective periods under the same Health Plan. 

https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5078581249/Member+Identification+and+Coverage#Multiple-Eligibility-Records-%2F-Coverage-Spans 

Dual eligibility under the same Health Plan (multiple Lines of Business). A member may legitimately have more than one active eligibility record under the same Health Plan due to dual eligibility (e.g., Medicare + Medicaid, Medicare + supplemental coverage). Assumption: Member Search returns all active matching records:

Acknowledged as a valid scenario

May result in multiple eligibility records for the same member 

 |

#### Non-Functional Requirements (NFRs)

Purpose

This page defines the Non-Functional Requirements (NFRs) for the NewUM platform, which represent platform-level quality constraints that apply across the entire end-to-end (E2E) case workflow

Scope

In Scope

The NFRs documented on this page apply to:

All NewUM workflows

All user roles (Provider, CRS, Clinical Reviewers, Health Plan users)

All payer-specific configurations

All deployment environments

Out Of Scope

Business rules

Workflow logic

Decision criteria

Data model definitions

UI behavior

noteb7a0896dbdd5If a requirement describes what the system does, it is not an NFR.
If it constrains how safely, how fast, or how reliably it does it, it is an NFR.

If a requirement describes what the system does, it is not an NFR.
If it constrains how safely, how fast, or how reliably it does it, it is an NFR.

Environmental considerations

This section outlines few considerations to keep in mind when creating engineering solutions and could be considered as non-functional requirement.

 | 
Best practices

 |  | Configuration and rules updates need to be tested on stable environment, ideally a staging database with same product version as on production environment before being released on production

 When NewUM release candidate is being prepared, it should be tested with current configuration and rules 

We should avoid &ldquo;deploying&rdquo; new versions of newUM and updating configuration/rules at the same time to reduce brittle surface

Ideally there should be no downtime when deploying new configuration or rules

If downtime is expected, every effort should be made to minimize duration of it and advance notification to users should be sent

Source Inventory

 | 8.0 Servicing/Treating Provider AND Place of Treatment? 

OneUM Provider Data UI-UX Fields_2026-02-26.xlsx

OncoHealth Data Integration Specifications v4.3 MASTER_20251009

 | 
Goals & Business Objectives

The goal of this feature is to enable accurate capture of provider and office details during NewUM case entry so that the system can support case creation, downstream authorization processing, provider/member/facility communications, and payer outbound integrations.

Objectives:

Enable the user to identify and capture the correct Ordering Provider, Servicing/Treating Provider, and Place of Treatment at the case level.

Reduce provider-selection errors that can contribute to authorization-to-claims mismatches and payer denials.

Capture provider office contact information needed for operational follow-up, notifications, and case processing.

Support payer-specific differences

Ensure provider capture is driven by Health Plan provider data and aligned with provider/network data available 

Background & Current State

Provider capture needs to distinguish:

Ordering Provider - the provider requesting the treatment

Servicing/Treating Provider -  the provider or organization delivering and/or billing for the service

Place of Treatment -  the facility or location where treatment occurs

In some workflows, Place of Service / Site of Care is also required because it affects downstream authorization and claim alignment.

8.0 Servicing/Treating Provider AND Place of Treatment? 

Current Pain Points

provider roles are not always captured separately

servicing provider, billing entity, and treatment location may be conflated

users may not see enough address/location detail to select the correct record

provider visibility and required data elements vary by payer

downstream processes may require provider details that were not captured clearly at intake

These issues create downstream risk:

incorrect provider or facility selected

mismatch between authorization details and billed service

manual follow-up, rework, or claim issues during processing

What Is Working Well

The current ecosystem already provides a foundation for this functionality:

provider data exists as a managed data domain with demographics, location, and network-related inputs - see OncoHealth Data Integration Specifications v4.3 MASTER_20251009

payer-specific controls already exist for some provider-related behavior

downstream integrations already use structured provider data elements such as provider identifiers, contact details, and location details

NewUM should implement provider selection as a structured, case-level, and configuration-driven capability. The feature should support clear role separation, accurate provider selection, sufficient address/location context, and preservation of provider details needed for downstream processing.

In scope:

Selecting provider and office details during case entry.

Capturing and persisting case-level provider selections and office contact details.

Out of scope 

Create a Provider on the Fly	(V1.0 R2 )

Out of Network Checks (V1.0 R2) 

Provider Intervention (CCF, P2P)	(V1.0 R2)

Provider Office Case Views	(V1.0 R2)

Support Email Notifications for Providers & Members (V2+ TBD)

Send Provider Networks to NewUM	(V1.0 R2)

Functional Requirements

Define what the system must do, specifying behavior, data processing needs, and business rules - no technical specifications

Requirement

 | Priority

 | Description (Functional Requirements)

 | Notes

 | 
User can search & select from Health Plan provider data for an Ordering Provider and Servicing / Treating Provider

 | must haveRed 

 | The system should allow the user to search Ordering Provider across all Health Plans provider data 

The system should limit Ordering Provider selection to Type 1 NPI (individual) records. 

The system should allow the user to search for a Servicing / Treating Provider when this section is enabled  (configuration, ON by default)

The system should require provider selection and should not rely on manual entry of provider identity details for V1.R1

The system should store Ordering Provider and Servicing / Treating Provider as separate provider roles on the case. 

The system should auto-populate provider details from the selected provider record.

 | Ordering Provider and Servicing / Treating Provider are captured separately. Provider details should come from the health plan data source.

 | 
User can search & select from Health Plan provider data for a Place of Treatment

 | must haveRed  

 | The system should allow the user to search any Health Plan provider data for a Place of Treatment. 

The system should allow the user to select a facility/location record representing where treatment will occur. 

The system should limit Place of Treatment selection to Type 2 NPI (facility/location) records 

The system should store Place of Treatment separately from Ordering Provider and Servicing / Treating Provider. 

The system should auto-populate Place of Treatment details from the selected record.

 | Place of Treatment is captured separately and should not be assumed from the provider selection.

 | 
Provider addresses are viewable within provider search to ensure the correct location is selected

 | must haveRed  

 | The system should display provider and facility address details within search results. 

The system should display sufficient address/location context to distinguish between multiple records for the same provider, facility, or organization (include visual indicator to help differentiate different Health Plans locations)

The system should allow the user to identify and select the correct provider/location combination before saving the selection. 

The system should display address context for Ordering Provider, Servicing / Treating Provider, and Place of Treatment search results where available.

 | Address details help the user choose the correct record when similar providers or locations exist.

 | 
User must enter the providers&rsquo; office contact information (email, phone, name, etc.)

 | must haveRed  

 | The system should provide fields for capturing provider office contact information on the case. 

The system should require the user to enter office contact details including: Name (required), Phone (required), Fax(required), Email (optional)

The system should store office contact information at the case level. 

The system should validate entered office contact values based on field type, including phone and email format where applicable. 

The system should not treat office contact details as provider master data.

 | Office contact details are entered for this case only and do not update provider source data.

 | 
User is only able to view the providers in which the health plan has access to

 | obsolete

Product Decision Log

 | The system should restrict provider search results to provider data available to the health plan. 

The system should restrict provider and location visibility based on the configured provider dataset for the member&rsquo;s payer/plan context. 

The system should prevent selection of providers outside the health plan&rsquo;s accessible provider data scope. 

The system should not require the platform user to manually key or reconcile missing provider identity records during case entry.

 | Users should only see providers and locations available to the health plan for that case.

 | 
For servicing provider and POT, user has the option to select &ldquo;Same as Ordering Provider&rdquo; and can change the location if needed

 | must haveRed  

 | The system should provide a Same as Ordering Provider option for:

 Servicing / Treating Provider

 Place of Treatment

When selected, the system should prepopulate the corresponding provider or location details from the Ordering Provider selection. 

The system should allow the user to override the prepopulated location when treatment will occur at a different site. 

The system should support capture of Place of Service (POS) codes when enabled by payer configuration. 

The system should allow Place of Service codes to be configurable at payer level. 

The system should enforce workflow guardrails so Place of Service is displayed only at the correct point in the workflow, such as after protocol and/or benefit selection where applicable.

 | Same as Ordering Provider is optional. Place of Service should appear only when needed and at the right step.

Consolidated Search Requirements

Search Area

 | What user can search by

 | Standard behavior

 | Result Search and  Display

 | 
Provider Search

 | Provider Name, Practice / Organization Name, full NPI, full TIN

 | Provider search is not restricted to the selected Health Plan. Search should return matching provider records across all available health plans.

For Servicing Provider, Results must include a visible Health Plan indicator at the row level so users can identify which provider location is associated with which Health Plan.

Search by name returns records that begin with or include the entered name text. Search by NPI or TIN runs only when the full number is entered. Results are shown as one row per unique provider + organization + TIN + location.

 | Search parameters: Provider Name (min 3 characters), Type 1 NPI (10 digits) , TIN (9 digits)

Search  Results Display Format:

Ordering Provider: Name |Specialty  |NPI |  TIN | Org | Address

Servicing Provider: Name |Specialty  |NPI |  TIN | Org | Address | Health Plan Indicator

option 1Blue

 option 2Blue

 | Facility Name, full Type 2 NPI, full TIN

#### Rules Repository

A Rules Repository is a centralized database or storage system designed to manage, store, and version business logic independently from a primary application's source code. It acts as a "single source of truth" where complex decision-making criteria such as eligibility requirements, medication validation or treatment protocols are organized. 

The repository is primarily used to provide transparency and agility to both engineering staff and non-technical stakeholders, like configuration analysts or product managers. It should also enable OH configuration admin to view, edit, and test rules in a controlled environment before they are pushed to production. This centralized approach should prevent "logic fragmentation," where different parts of a system might otherwise apply inconsistent rules to the same data. Ultimately, it serves as the brain of a Business Rules Management System (BRMS), enabling the newUM software to remain flexible and responsive to rapidly changing market conditions or regulatory requirements

v1 Rule Repository

Goals & Business Objectives

Enable users to add ancillary drugs during chemo entry in a way that is clinically accurate, operationally scalable, and consistent with payer and regimen configuration.

Support:

efficient ancillary drug search and selection

ancillary-only chemo requests

category-based ancillary display in the UI

consistent dosing initialization using Admin Portal and main regimen defaults where applicabl

Background & Current State

Ancillary drugs are part of chemo entry and may be added either:

together with a selected main regimen, or

without a main regimen in an ancillary-only case

Functional Requirements

The functional requirements listed above describe the complete end-to-end behavior for this step of the prior authorization workflow, independent of release phasing. They define what the system must be capable of doing to support the use case

Requirement

 | Description

 | Notes

 | 
Ability to search and select ancillary drugs during chemo entry

 | The system shall allow the user to search for ancillary drugs during chemo entry.

The search shall return only drugs designated as Ancillary in the Master Drug Library ( Drug type = Ancillary)

The system shall support search by HCPCS code, generic drug name, and brand drug name.

Search shall support partial and case-insensitive matching.

The system shall begin returning search results after the user enters at least 3 characters.

Each search result shall display Clinical Category, HCPCS code, generic drug name, and brand drug name, when available, using a consistent format.

Example display: Bone-Modifying Agents: Q5159 denosumab (Xbryk). 

The system shall allow the user to select one or more ancillary drugs from the search results.

The system shall allow multiple ancillary drug line items within the same Clinical Category tbdRed  

The system shall persist each selected ancillary drug as a separate drug line on the case, together with its associated Clinical Category10. 

 |  tbdRed  Should support for duplicate ancillary drug lines be postponed until Loading Dose functionality is implemented?

 | 
Ability to create ancillary-only case

 | The system shall allow the user to create a chemo case containing ancillary drugs without selecting a main regimen.

The system shall allow an ancillary-only case to be saved in Draft status.

The system shall allow an ancillary-only case to be submitted when at least one ancillary drug is present on the case.

All ancillary drugs in an ancillary-only case shall be persisted as individual drug lines.

 | Main regimen selection is not required for ancillary-only workflow.

 | 
Grouping ancillary drugs together in UI based on Clinical Categories

 | After selection, the system shall group ancillary drugs into separate UI sections by Clinical Category.

Within each Clinical Category section, the system shall display ancillary drugs in separate Medical and Pharmacy tables, where applicable, based on payer drug configuration and benefit classification.

Ancillary drugs shall be displayed separately from main regimen drugs.

If an ancillary drug is configured as a crossover drug, the system shall support crossover benefit-type behavior consistent with the other chemo drug workflows.

 |  | 
Defaulting dosing fields for ancillary drugs

 | The system shall prepopulate ancillary drug dosing fields from Admin Portal where ancillary default values are available.

If no ancillary default value exists for a given field, the system shall leave that field blank 

The system shall source ancillary field defaults as follows where available in Admin Portal:

Dosage from Dose per Administration

Units from Dose Unit

Adm per Day from Frequency per Day

Form from Administration Method, if retained in the NewUM UI design

The system shall calculate or derive ancillary Strength and Allowed Dose in accordance with the approved ancillary dosing logic.

The system shall retrieve Benefit Type from the Payer Drug Library (PDL) for each ancillary drug and use it to determine table placement and downstream display behavior.

 | tbdRed 

Current Pharmacy mockup rendering for Strength and Dosage should be corrected. 

Form field visibility requires confirmation.

 | 
Mirror the main regimen cycle fields by specific Clinical Categories of ancillary drugs

 | The system shall apply main-regimen mirroring logic only to ancillary drugs in the following Clinical Categories:

Antiemetics

Long-GCSF

Short-GCSF

For eligible Clinical Categories, the system shall mirror the following fields from the main regimen when qualifying main-regimen values are available:

Administration Days per Cycle

Cycles in Days

Cycles

If the main regimen provides a single consistent value for a mirrored field, the system should default the ancillary field from the main regimen.

If no consistent main-regimen value exists, the system should use the ancillary Admin Portal default when available; otherwise, leave the field blank. 

User-entered ancillary values must not be overwritten, but system-populated ancillary values should stay aligned when the main-regimen value changes.

notead855cf0e174Main-regimen mirroring applies only when the main regimen is an existing regimen and all regimen drug lines share the same default values for Cycles , Cycles in Days, Administration Days per Cycle.  When these conditions are met, the system should set ancillary drug Cycles , Cycles in Days, Administration Days per Cycle to match the main regimen.

When these conditions are met, the system should set ancillary drug Cycles , Cycles in Days, Administration Days per Cycle to match the main regimen.

 |  | 
User is only able to select 1 ancillary drug per group ( except for the Nausea drugs)

obsoleteRed  

 | System enforces a maximum of one drug per ancillary diagnosis group.

Exception: Nausea group allows multiple drug selections.

Restriction is validated prior to save and submit.

Validation message displayed if user attempts to exceed group limit.

Enforcement applies whether ancillary drugs are added with a main regimen or in ancillary-only cases.
