Editable. Drop Down Logic:

1. For Dose Drop Down: The allowed Units values should be inferred based on the associated Billable UOM (BUM) for the drug (Capture Basic Dosing Details )

1.1. Carboplatin is a defined exception. In addition to the standard Units derived from its Billable UOM, the Units dropdown should also include: Area Under Curve 1.5, Area Under Curve 2, Area Under Curve 3, Area Under Curve 4, Area Under Curve 5, Area Under Curve 6, Area Under Curve 7

3. The Units dropdown should always include &ldquo;Unknown&rdquo; as a selectable option.

 | Unit selection determines whether Allowed Dose is calculated (mg/kg, mg/m&sup2;, etc.) or equals Dosage (fixed units).

tbdRed validate if this mapping logic applies to Ancillary drugs as well/

Source of allowed Units values: should be determined based on the drug&rsquo;s associated Billable Unit of Measure (Billable UOM).

Billable UOM to Units mapping:
1. If Billable UOM = mg. Allowed Units:
mg, g, g/kg, mcg, mcg/kg, mcg/m2, mg/kg, mg/m2, g/m2

2. If Billable UOM = mcg. Allowed Units:mg, g, g/kg, mcg, mcg/kg, mcg/m2, mg/kg, mg/m2, g/m2

3.If Billable UOM = mCi. Allowed Units:mCi

4. If Billable UOM = IU. Allowed Units:IU/kg, IU/m2

5. If Billable UOM = Units. Allowed Units:International Unit, million units, million units/kg, units, units/kg, units/m2

6. If Billable UOM = Infusion. Allowed Units: Infusion

7. If Billable UOM = million Units. Allowed Units:
International Unit, million units, million units/kg, units, units/kg, units/m2

 | 
Allowed Dose

 | Calculated patient-specific dose

 | MedicalGreen

 | System calculation 

 | Decimal (calculated; 2 decimals)

 | calculatedGreen

 | Calculated automatically. Not editable. Formula:

1. If Units = Fixed units (mg, g, mcg), then  Allowed Dose = Dosage

2.  If Units = Carboplatin AUC (1.5&ndash;7), then Allowed Dose = Dosage
- Weight-based units (mg/kg, mcg/kg, g/kg) &rarr; Allowed Dose = Dosage &times; Weight (kg)

3. If Units = BSA-based units (mg/m&sup2;, g/m&sup2;, IU/m&sup2;, units/m&sup2;) &rarr; Allowed Dose = Dosage &times; BSA where BSA = &radic;(Height [cm] &times; Weight [kg] / 3600). 

noteb6cb83084b5fAllowed Dose must be expressed in the drug&rsquo;s Billable UOM (apply mg/mcg/g conversions as needed).
Rounding: 2 decimal places using the thousandths rule.

Allowed Dose must be expressed in the drug&rsquo;s Billable UOM (apply mg/mcg/g conversions as needed).
Rounding: 2 decimal places using the thousandths rule.

 |  
Rule: Recalculate Allowed Dose if Weight changes (for weight-based units), Height or Weight changes (for BSA-based units)

 | Decimal (calculated; 2 decimals)

 | calculatedGreen

 | Auto-calculated for all medical drugs.

 | Formula: (Allowed Dose &times; Adm Per Day &times; Adm Days Per Cycle &times; Cycles) &divide; CMU BU (from Admin Portal). Cycles derivation: Duration per AP/Cycle in Days, rounded up to next whole number. 
Rounding: 2 decimals per standard thousandths rule. Rule: trigger alert if edited dosing exceeds Max BU/duration configured in Admin Portal.

1. default to the AP Cycle Length, if available
2. else leave blank

For Ancillary drugs associated with the following Ancillary Clinical Categories - Antiemetics, Long-GCSF, Short-GCSF:  If the main treatment is an Existing Regimen and all regimen drugs share the same default Cycles in Days:
1. default to the main regimen
2. otherwise default to the AP Cycle Length, if available
3. else leave blank

For Ancillary drugs NOT associated with the following Ancillary Clinical Categories - Antiemetics, Long-GCSF, Short-GCSF:  If the main treatment is an Existing Regimen and all regimen drugs share the same default Cycles in Days:
1. default to the AP Cycle Length, if available
2. else leave blank

Editable. Allowed values (in the following order): as needed, every 5 days, every 7 days, every 14 days, every 15 days, every 21 days, every 25 days, every 28 days, every 30 days, every 35 days, every 42 days, every 49 days, every 56 days, every 60 days, every 84 days, every 90 days, every 112 days, every 120 days, every 168 days, every 180 days, every 365 days, every day, onetime, Unknown

 | Meaning: The length of one treatment cycle in calendar days.

Example: If the regimen repeats every 28 days, Cycles in Days = 28.

Used to derive Cycles (rounded up) for authorization calculations.

Identifies the business rules applicable to this feature(-s) and links to the centralized Rules Inventory where rule definitions are maintained. This section enables traceability while avoiding duplication of rule logic within the PRD.

User Stories 

The user stories listed below represent V1.0 implementation candidates only.
Each story is prioritized using the MoSCoW model:

Must Have &ndash; required for the workflow to function in V1.0

Should Have &ndash; important, but not required for initial operability

Could Have &ndash; optional enhancements, deferred if needed

User Story Title

 | Priority

 | Acceptance criteria

 | Notes

 | 
1 | Search and Select Ancillary Drugs

 | should haveYellow   

 v1.r1.Green  

 | During chemo entry, user can add ancillary drugs to a selected main regimen (existing or custom)

Only drugs designated as Ancillary in the Master Drug Library (MDL) are available for selection.

Search supports: 

drug name (brand or generic), HCPCS code

partial and case-insensitive matching.

The system should return matching Ancillary Drugs using the format: [Clinical Category]:  [HCPCS code]  [Generic Name] [Brand Name]) when a brand name is available.

The system should use the same result structure across all Ancillary Drug search results

Example:

Source Admin: Clinical Category: Bone-Modifying Agents, Drug Name: denosumab , Brand Name: Xbryk, HCPCS: Q5159 

Expected display: Bone-Modifying Agents: Q5159 denosumab (Xbryk)

The system should start returning matching results after the user enters at least 3 characters.

The system should support partial-match search and limited typo tolerance for drug-name searches, while ranking exact matches above partial or approximate matches.

The user should be able to add multiple ancillary drugs within the same Clinical Category.

The system should allow multiple ancillary drugs to be selected within the same Clinical Category.  tbdRed 

Each selected ancillary drug should be saved as a separate drug line within the chemo case, with its associated Clinical Category persisted on the backend.

 | AP source for Clinical Category:

Added:

Multiple ancillary drugs can be added for the same category, moving away from the one-per-category restriction. However we will not allow duplicates to be added.

 | 
2 | Create Ancillary-Only Chemotherapy Requests

 | should haveYellow   

 v1.r1.Green    

 | During chemo entry, user should be able to create and submit a case with ancillary drugs only:

user should be able to add ancillary drugs without selecting a main regimen (either from the pre-built library or a custom regimen).

The user must add at least one ancillary drug to submit the request.

The system allows saving ancillary only chemo entry (without a main regimen) as Draft Case

The system allows submission when ancillary drugs are present, even if no main regimen exists.

All ancillary drugs are saved as individual drug lines within the chemotherapy request.

3 | Enter dosing information for Ancillary Drugs

 | should haveYellow   

 v1.r1.Green  

 | When ancillary drugs are added during chemo entry - either in addition to a main regimen (pre-built or custom) or as part of an ancillary-only case - the system should retrieve the Billing Method for each drug from the Payer Drug Library (PDL) to automatically render two dosing tables based on the Billing Method classification in accordance with  Apply Benefit Type Configuration from PDL (Medical vs Pharmacy Drug)

In addition to the main regimen dosing tables, ancillary drugs should be displayed in separate sections/tables by Clinical Category, where the section header displays the Clinical Category

Once the Medical and Pharmacy dosing tables are rendered, the system should :

 populate dosing table in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537539/Select+Ancillary+Drugs#Data-Dictionary 

allow selection of alternate drugs through the HCPCS code field drop down in accordance with Main Regimen Selection 

For Ancillary Drugs Dosing Fields values, the system should pull forward any available default dosing values from Admin Portal.

If no Ancillary Drugs default dosing values are available,  the fields should remain blank. 

User should be able to view/edit drugs dosing information in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537539/Select+Ancillary+Drugs#Data-Dictionary 

Calculation logic for system calculated fields should align to:

Medical:

https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537539/Select+Ancillary+Drugs#Allowed-Dose 

https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537539/Select+Ancillary+Drugs#Max-Billing-Units%2FAuth 

Flag if Max Billing Units/Auth exceeds the drug&rsquo;s configured Max BU per duration in Admin Portal.

Pharmacy:

https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537539/Select+Ancillary+Drugs#Quantity-per-Auth 

Flag if Quantity/Auth exceeds the drug&rsquo;s configured Qty per Auth/duration in Admin Portal.

 | Ensure that all dosing guardrails and validation rules are applied consistently across both Custom Regimens. Existing regimens, Ancillary Drugs to maintain uniform clinical and data integrity standards.

Ancillary drugs are displayed separately from main regimen drugs and are rendered in distinct Medical and Pharmacy dosing tables based on their billing classification.

4 | Align Ancillary Drug Cycle Fields with Main Regimen

 |   should haveYellow   

 v1.r1.Green    

 | The system should apply Main Regimen alignment only to ancillary drugs in the following Clinical Categories:

Antiemetics

Long-Acting GCSFs

Short-Acting GCSFs

The system should evaluate the following ancillary fields independently:

Administration Days per Cycle

Cycles

Cycles in Days

The system should treat a Main Regimen value as qualifying for a given field only when:

the Main Treatment is an Existing Regimen; AND

all Main Regimen drug lines have the same default value for that field.

For each in-scope field, the system should apply the following defaulting order:

first, the qualifying Main Regimen value, when available;

otherwise, the ancillary drug default from Admin Portal, when available;

otherwise, blank.

If a field was system-populated from an ancillary Admin Portal default and a qualifying Main Regimen is later added, the system should update that field to match the Main Regimen.

If a field is currently system-aligned to the Main Regimen and the corresponding Main Regimen value later changes to a new qualifying shared value, the system should update the ancillary field accordingly.

If a field has been manually entered or modified by the user, the system should not overwrite that value.

If a field is currently system-aligned to the Main Regimen and the corresponding Main Regimen field later no longer has a qualifying shared value, the system should retain the current ancillary value.

The system should allow the user to edit Administration Days per Cycle, Cycles, Cycles in Days in accordance with https://oncologyanalytics.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/NewUM1/pages/5154537539/Select+Ancillary+Drugs#Data-Dictionary 

The system should support the following scenarios: Ancillary Cycles Scenarios 

 |  | 
Ancillary Administration Days per Cycle, Cycles in Days, and Cycles Scenarios

Applicable Clinical Categories: Antiemetics, Long-GCSF, Short-GCSF

Ancillary Cycles and Cycles in Days should default from the Main Regimen when a qualifying Existing Regimen is present and all regimen drug lines share the same default value.

#### Standard Compliance Reports

Purpose

This page defines the product requirements for NewUM to support CMS‑mandated Part C and Part D compliance reporting. It outlines the data, workflow, and reporting capabilities required to ensure accurate, timely, and audit‑ready ODAG and CDAG submissions.

Audit & Compliance Reporting Objectives

NewUM must enable OncoHealth to meet all CMS reporting obligations for Medicare Advantage (Part C) and Prescription Drug Plans (Part D):

Validate adherence to regulatory and accreditation standards (CMS, NCQA, state-specific rules).

Demonstrate compliance with contractual service-level agreements.

Support audit preparation, audit response, and delegation oversight.

CMS universe generation with 100% field completeness.

Traceability from reported metrics back to source data.

Full audit logs for all case actions.

Retention policies aligned with CMS requirements. 

Included Standard Compliance Reports

NewUM must support the following compliance reports as part of the standard reporting suite:

Part C ODAG (Organization Determinations, Appeals & Grievances)

Part D CDAG (Coverage Determinations, Appeals & Grievances)

Audit Sampling Report

Delegation Oversight Report

Each report includes functional, data, and delivery requirements below.

Part C ODAG

Purpose

Demonstrate compliance with CMS timeliness standards for determinations, appeals, and grievances.

Functional Requirements

Capture all CMS‑required ODAG data elements in structured fields.

Enforce standardized workflows for determinations, appeals, and grievances.

Automatically classify cases as standard or expedited based on CMS rules.

Validate required fields before case closure.

Timestamp all workflow events with millisecond precision.

Support multi‑reviewer workflows with role‑based restrictions.

Allow case reopening with full version history and audit traceability.

Data Requirements

Provide real‑time operational dashboards for case activity and timeliness.

Provide daily batch reports for historical trends and compliance monitoring.

Support filtering by payer, reviewer, case type, and date range.

Maintain historical snapshots for audit lookbacks.

Delivery Requirements

Monthly automated and ad hoc generation.

Export formats: CSV and Excel.

Report Spec

Sample ODAG Spec

CMS ODAG Requirements

Sample ODR Spec

Part D CDAG

Purpose

Demonstrate compliance with CMS timeliness standards for drug coverage decisions and appeals.

Functional Requirements

Capture all CMS‑required CDAG data elements in structured fields.

Enforce standardized workflows for coverage determinations, redeterminations, and grievances.

Automatically classify cases as standard or expedited based on CMS Part D rules.

Validate required fields before case closure, including drug identifiers and prescriber information.

Timestamp all workflow events with millisecond precision.

Support multi‑reviewer workflows (pharmacist &rarr; RN &rarr; MD) with role‑based restrictions.

Allow case reopening with full version history and audit traceability.

Support linking of appeals to original determinations.

Data Requirements

Provide real‑time dashboards for case activity, timeliness, and drug‑related trends.

Provide daily batch reports for historical trends and compliance monitoring.

Support filtering by drug, prescriber, payer, reviewer, case type, and date range.

Maintain historical snapshots for audit lookbacks.

Delivery Requirements

Monthly automated generation.

Export formats: CSV and Excel.

Report Spec

Sample CDAG Spec

CMS CDAG Requirements

Sample CDR Spec

Audit Sampling Report Requirements

Purpose

Provide structured samples of UM cases for internal or external audits.

Functional Requirements

Must support random and criteria-based sampling.

Must allow configuration of sample size and sampling rules.

Must include all required case-level fields for audit review.

Must maintain reproducibility of samples using seed-based logic.

Data Requirements

Case identifiers and metadata.

Decision details, timestamps, reviewer roles.

Clinical documentation indicators.

Delivery Requirements

On-demand generation.

Export formats: Excel and CSV.

Delegation Oversight Report Requirements

Purpose

Support customer delegation oversight requirements by summarizing UM performance, compliance, and documentation quality.

Functional Requirements

Must include operational and compliance metrics required for delegation oversight.

Must support customer-specific oversight templates.

Must include documentation completeness indicators.

Must provide summary and detailed views.

Data Requirements

Case-level and appeal-level data.

Timeliness metrics.

Documentation completeness fields.

Audit findings (if applicable).

Delivery Requirements

Monthly or quarterly or ad hoc generation.

Export formats: CSV and Excel.

System-Level Requirements Supporting Compliance Reporting

Auditability

All compliance reports must include generation timestamp, data source version, and logic version.

All fields must have documented lineage.

Reports must be reproducible for audit validation.

Access & Permissions

Role-based access must restrict PHI and sensitive compliance fields.

Customer users must only access their own data.

Performance

Reports must generate within defined SLAs.

System must support concurrent generation of compliance and operational reports.

#### Standard Operational Reports

Purpose

This page defines the product requirements for the operational reporting suite. These reports provide customers with visibility into UM activity, performance, and financial impact. Requirements emphasize data consistency, scalability, and multi‑tenant support across all OncoHealth customers.

Operational Reporting Objectives 

Operational reporting in NewUM must enable customers and internal stakeholders to:

Monitor UM activity and decision trends at both summary and detailed levels.

Evaluate operational performance against contractual and regulatory expectations.

Understand financial implications of UM decisions.

Integrate case‑level and element‑level data into internal analytics systems.

Access consistent, validated, and audit‑ready datasets.

Included Standard Operational Reports

Must support the following operational reports:

Activity Report

Turnaround Time (TAT) Report

Financial Impact Report

Case‑Level Flat File

Element‑Level Flat File

Each report includes functional, data, and delivery requirements below.

Activity Report Requirements

Purpose 

Provide a consolidated view of UM case activity and decision trends. 

Functional Requirements

Must aggregate case volumes by service category, request type, and decision outcome. 

Must allow filtering by payer, line of business, provider, and date range. 

Must include logic for categorizing service types

Data Requirements

Case identifiers, received dates, decision dates. 

Decision outcomes (approved, denied, withdrawn, appeals, reopens). 

Service category, diagnosis, treatment type. 

Provider and practice identifiers. 

Delivery Requirements

Monthly automation generation 

Export formats: Excel

Report Spec

Activity Report Spec

Turnaround Time (TAT) Report Requirements

Purpose

Measure timeliness of UM decisions relative to contractual and regulatory expectations. 

Functional Requirements

Must calculate average, median, and percentile-based TAT.

Must classify cases by urgency (standard, urgent, concurrent, retrospective).

Must calculate compliance percentages against customer-specific SLA rules.

Must flag outliers and categorize root-cause drivers when available.

Data Requirements 

Received timestamp, clinical review timestamp, decision timestamp.

SLA configuration per customer.

Case urgency and request type.

Delivery Requirements 

Monthly automated generation

Export formats: Excel

Report Spec

Turnaround Time (TAT) Report Spec

Financial Impact Report Requirements

Purpose

Quantify cost savings and cost avoidance associated with UM decisions.

Functional Requirements

Must calculate estimated allowed amounts for approved vs. denied services.

Must support financial impact attribution logic (e.g., alternative treatment recommendations).

Must identify high-cost cases and categorize by service type.

Must support customer-specific financial fields when contractually required.

Data Requirements

Allowed amounts, billed amounts, negotiated rates (if available).

Decision outcome and rationale.

Service category and treatment details.

Delivery Requirements

Monthly

Export formats: Excel

Report Spec

Financial Impact Report Spec

Case‑Level Flat File Requirements

Purpose

Provide a structured dataset with one record per UM case for customer analytics and integration.

Functional Requirements

Include all core case‑level fields required for customer reporting.

Support multi‑tenant logic ensuring customers only receive their own data.

Maintain consistent field names and definitions across all customers.

Support historical data retention for trend analysis.

Data Requirements

Member demographics.

Case metadata (request type, service category, urgency).

Dates (received, clinical review, decision).

Decision outcome and reviewer role.

Financial fields (if contractually included).

Delivery Requirements

Monthly automated generation.

Export format: CSV or pipe‑delimited flat file.

Report Spec

Case Flat File Spec

Element‑Level Flat File Requirements

Purpose

Provide granular detail for each clinical or administrative element associated with a case.

Functional Requirements

Generate one record per element tied to a case‑level identifier.

Include element‑level decision outcomes and timestamps.

Support audit and compliance workflows requiring element‑level traceability.

Maintain referential integrity with the Case‑Level Flat File.

Data Requirements

Case ID, element ID.

Clinical criteria or documentation element.

Element‑level decision outcome.

Reviewer role and timestamps.

Additional metadata supporting audit or analytics needs.

Delivery Requirements

Monthly automated generation.

Export format: CSV or pipe‑delimited flat file.

Report Spec

Element Flat File Spec

System‑Level Requirements 

Scheduling & Automation

All operational reports must support automated monthly scheduling.

On‑demand generation must be available for internal users with appropriate permissions.

Performance

Standard monthly reports must be able to reflect near real-time activity. 

Flat files must support large‑volume extraction without performance degradation.

Access & Permissions

Role‑based access must restrict PHI and financial fields to authorized users.

Customer users must only access their own data.

Auditability

All reports must include generation timestamp, data source version, and logic version.

Report logic must be fully traceable and documented.

Data Dictionary

Defines the business meaning, usage, and validation expectations for data elements used by this feature (-s).  This section provides a common reference for field definitions.

Capture Basic Dosing Details

#### V1. Reopens

Project Specifics

Target Release

Goals & Business Objectives

Goal Statement  
Design NewUM to support a standard, predictable, and fully compliant reopen process for any case across all lines of business, so that:

Internal users can reliably determine the correct reopen pathway from the case status, and

Reopens and appeals are handled in a way that supports CMS‑compliant access to care, minimizes unnecessary overturned denials, and protects/optimizes double‑weighted Star Rating measures (Member Experience and Access).

Main Personas for Reopens: 

Only a CRS Operations Staff (Case Review Specialist) or CRS Operations Manager can reopen a case: 

Faye the Front Liner (CRS)

Clinical is needed for reopens that require medical necessity review: 

Naomi the Navigator (OneUM Nurse) 

The following personas may be impacted (i.e., notification, financial impact, reporting) downstream by a reopen: 

Patrick the Prescribing Provider 

Cas the Current Onboarding Client 

Background & Current State

Problem Statement  
Reopens are handled inconsistently across UM platforms and lines of business, creating clinical risk, process gaps, and non‑compliance with CMS, NCQA, and URAC. This directly affects CMS Medicare Star Ratings&mdash;especially double‑weighted Member Experience and Access&mdash;through late appeals, avoidable overturned denials, and PA‑related complaints that can pull plans below the 4‑star threshold and jeopardize Quality Bonus Payments.

Reopenings are governed by CMS, NCQA, URAC, and payer policy and are intended as an administrative action to correct errors or review new information without triggering a formal appeal.

Federal standards (Medicare/CMS)

Reopenings are allowed for minor clerical/technical errors (e.g., CPT, DOB, NPI).

Timeframes:

&le; 1 year: may be reopened for any reason.

&le; 4 years: requires &ldquo;good cause.&rdquo;

Accreditation standards (NCQA & URAC)

NCQA: requires objective, evidence‑based criteria for all determinations, including reopenings.

URAC: emphasizes transparency and efficiency, and requires a clear separation between reopen/reconsideration and formal appeals to preserve member rights.

Current Pain Points within OncoHealth&rsquo;s Platforms

OncoHealth&rsquo;s platforms do not yet support CMS‑compliant reopens as a separate, standardized process across all LOBs and case types.

Key gaps:

No predictable workflow; relies on CRS knowledge of systems, regulations, accreditation requirements, and payer policy.

Missing UI and data structures for CMS‑aligned decision reasons (uphold, overturn, dismiss, withdraw) and linkage between original and reopened cases.

Incomplete notification templates/workflows (provider/member, oral and written) and insufficient data/reporting to satisfy CMS/ODAG and client‑specific reopen requirements.

No end‑to‑end support for reopens on any case across all LOBs with CMS‑verbatim reopen reasons.

Incomplete intake rules for all channels (especially member mail/email) and missing configurable TAT/timer logic for receipt, eligibility, extensions, and notifications by LOB, state, and regulator.

Lack of structured reopen eligibility rules, withdrawal handling, extension/tolling capability in MATIS, and clear separation from concurrent appeals.

Links to Initial Reseach Documentations

UX designs from 2020: Reopens pages 13-22 - these are not to be taken as final, providing for historical context

Reopening a prior authorization in NewUM follows a standard four‑step UM pattern. A reopen is adding a new review event to a closed case; NewUM must create a new event linked to the original authorization, not just flip the status.

Step

 | Requirement

 | Priority

 | Description (Use Case)

 | Notes

 | 
1.0 Identify Case Status

 | System must determine and display the current case status for any prior authorization.

 | MUST HAVERed

 | As a CRS, I need NewUM to clearly show whether a case is Closed &ndash; No Decision, Closed &ndash; Approved, Closed &ndash; Denied (non-final), Closed &ndash; Denied (final), Withdrawn, or Expired so I can understand what type of reopening is allowed.

 | Certain statuses cannot be changed without a compliant workflow; reopen eligibility is driven off status.

 | 
2.0 Select Reopen Pathway

 | System must expose only the valid reopen action(s) based on case status.

 | MUST HAVERed

 | As a CRS, when I choose to reopen a case, I want NewUM to present only appropriate options (Reopen Review/Reactivate Case, Add Clinical Update/Add Clinical, Reconsideration, Appeal, Extensions) so I cannot select a non-compliant pathway.

 | These are the only 5 pathways in standard UM workflows. See linked Reopen Pathways documentation for detailed rules.

 | 
3.0 Attach New Information

 | System must require new information or justification before a reopen can be submitted.

 | MUST HAVERed

 | As a CRS, I must provide new clinical documentation, corrected data, provider reconsideration request, updated service dates, or a change in medical necessity before submitting a reopen so that the action complies with audit rules.

 | Reopening without new information is not allowed and should be prevented by validation.

 | 
4.0 Route Back into UM Workflow

 | System must route the reopened event to the correct queue based on the selected pathway.

 | MUST HAVERed

 | As a CRS, once I submit a reopen, I want NewUM to automatically send it to Intake, Clinical (UM Nurse), Medical Director, or Appeals according to the reopen type so processing is consistent and compliant.

 | Routing logic is driven by the reopen event chosen in Step 2.0. For applicable statuses, see Reopens Statuses.

 | 
Functional Requirements: 

These describe what the system must do to support compliant reopen processing: 

Core Functional Capabilities

Identify original case status and determine whether reopening is allowed (Approved, Denied, Withdrawn, Expired, Closed- No Decision) 

Trigger the correct reopen pathway (Clinical Update, Reconsideration, Appeal, Reactivation, Administrative Correction) 

Create a new review event wthout overwriting the original determination 

Capture the reason for reopen (new clinical information, provoder request, correction, appeal) 

Allow document upload for new clinical information 

Route the reopened case to the correct queue (Intake (CRS), UM Nurse (Clinical), MD, Appeals) 

Apply TAT rules based on the pathway (UM vs. Appeals timelines) 

Generate reopen outcome statuses (Reopen-Pending, Upheld, Overturned, Withdrawn, Dismissal) 

Lock or restrict actions when reopen is not allowed (e.g., final denial without appeal) 

Maintain a complete audit trail linking original case &rarr; reopen event &rarr; outcome 

User-Facing Functional Requirements: 

Display clear action options based on role and case status 

See RBAC 

Provide inline validation (e.g., cannot reopen without new information) 

Support notes, comments, and attachments 

Allow withdrawal of a reopen request by provider or staff 

Prevent duplicate requests on the same case unless allowed by policy 

General Requirements: 

Notifications

See Reopens - Notifications section  

Compliance and Audit 

Preserve the original decision; never overwrite it 

Maintain a chronological event history showing all reopen attempts 

Enforce NCQA UM 5 and CMS 42 CFR TAT standards

TATS  

Require new or corrected information before allowing a reopen (except administrative corrections)

Ensure appeals follow seperate regulatory workflows 

See Appeal workflow

Original decision date 

Original reviewer

Original determination rationale 

Ensure reopened events have: 

New timestamps

New reviewer assignments 

New rationale fields

Resources

 | V1.0 UM Case Model: RBAC, States, Statuses & Determinations 

 | 
Goals & Business Objectives

This initiative aligns UM case states, statuses, and determinations with industry standards and CMS/NCQA-accepted terminology for oncology utilization management prior authorization workflows in the NewUM platform. These states, statuses, and determinations outlined remain the same *regardless of line of business, payer terminology, or delegation level.

*What we mean by "regardless of line of business, payer terminology or delegation level."1800notedbcd4fc4-7904-4a6d-bb1b-c4bca2edfbadBased on the NewUM concept, we will not differentiate determination terminology between delegated and non-delegated payers. Instead, the driver for letter generation will be the delegation-level indicator. This reduces confusion during audits, case processing, and reporting (including data, engineering, and analyst workflows).

Based on the NewUM concept, we will not differentiate determination terminology between delegated and non-delegated payers. Instead, the driver for letter generation will be the delegation-level indicator. This reduces confusion during audits, case processing, and reporting (including data, engineering, and analyst workflows).

NewUM Rules of Thumb1800NewUM RULES of THUMB

States and statuses describe the lifecycle of the case. 

Determinations describe decisions made on what the case contains.

A determination is never a state or status.

A drug‑level org determination represents the formal UM decision for an individual drug or service within a case.

A case‑level org determination reflects the overall outcome of the authorization request after evaluating all included drugs or services.

Determinations are what is transmitted to the health plan, member and reported to the governing entity at state or federal level (where applicable).

A single UM case can contain multiple drugs / services &mdash; and the organization may make different determinations at each level.

Based on the NewUM concept, we will not differentiate determination terminology between delegated and non-delegated payers. Instead, the driver for letter generation will be the delegation-level indicator. This reduces confusion during audits, case processing, and reporting (including data, engineering, and analyst workflows).

Background & Current State

States, Statuses, and Determinations

In the UM system, states, statuses, and determinations serve distinct purposes and must not be used interchangeably.

States represent internal workflow progression (for example, received, under review, pending appeal) and support operational routing, timing, and auditability.

Statuses are the external‑facing expressions of where a request stands from a user perspective and are intentionally simplified to communicate progress or outcome without exposing internal processing steps.

Determinations are the formal adjudicative outcomes of a UM request&mdash;such as approved, denied, withdrawn, or dismissed&mdash;and are produced only at defined decision points by authorized roles. States drive work, statuses communicate progress, and determinations represent final or reportable decisions.

Concept

 | Answers

 | Changes How Often

 | Defined Where

 | 
State

 | Where is it in the lifecycle?

 | Infrequent

 | Workflow / System Design

 | 
Status

 | What&rsquo;s happening now?

 | Frequent

 | Workflow / Ops

 | 
Determination

 | What decision was made?

 | Event‑based

 | Clinical / Regulatory

 | 
Hierarchy & relationship

wide1800Current Pain Points

Non‑standard terminology for case progress
Current case progress labels are not aligned with industry‑standard UM terminology, making it harder for external users (providers, payers, auditors) to intuitively understand where a case is in the process. This is especially complicated for deviations in terminology for delegated vs. non-delegated clients.

Increased support burden for internal teams
Because external users cannot easily interpret case status from the UI (SmartUM) or are not granted access to the UI once a case is submitted (MATIS), internal operations and support teams spend additional time handling calls and inquiries to explain case status and progress.

Conflation of status and determination in the UI and in Data used for Analytics & Reporting
The current UI terminology blurs the distinction between &ldquo;status&rdquo; (where the case is in the process) and &ldquo;determination&rdquo; (the adjudicative outcome), which creates confusion for both internal and external users and increases risk of misinterpretation, as well as creates circumstances in which the data team must derive determinations for cases and drugs based on &ldquo;status&rdquo;.

No separate capture of case‑level vs. item‑level determinations
The system does not currently distinguish between overall case‑level determinations and drug/code‑level line item determinations, limiting the ability to perform accurate data analytics, reporting, audits, and notifications that require both levels of decision detail.

Lack of engineering context for determination capture
Current UX and data gaps make it unclear to engineering why we can&rsquo;t simply add a user‑selected &ldquo;status&rdquo; field to capture determinations, even though determinations must be system‑controlled outcomes set only at defined decision points by authorized roles.

Current Strengths

Data model contains needed elements: states, statuses, determinations (just not aptly named and not appropriately mapped).

Case vs. line‑item concepts are present for building accurate outcomes.

We can build on these foundations with configuration, naming, and UX updates.

NewUM documentation: V1.0 UM Case Model: RBAC, States, Statuses & Determinations 

NOTE: This document has multiple tabs and includes RBAC, Permissions, Review-Stage-Specific requirements, LOB-Specific requirements, & Post-Determination case requirements.

Functional Requirements

1. Core architectural principles (non‑negotiable)

These are assumptions already embedded in the UM Case Model and Determinations discussions and should be treated as foundational requirements, not design preferences.

The system must support:

✅ One case lifecycle

✅ Multiple services/drugs per case

✅ Drug/Code‑level determinations

✅ Derived case‑level determinations

✅ LOB‑specific rules without duplicating workflows

2. Functional requirements by capability area

A. Case & Service (Drug or Code) Structure

The system must:

Allow a single UM case to contain multiple services / drugs

Treat each drug/service as:

independently reviewable

independently determinable

Maintain a parent&ndash;child relationship:

Case = parent

Drugs/services = children

✅ This directly supports partial approvals, mixed outcomes, and appeal logic.

B. Determinations (Drug‑Level)

The system must support drug‑level determinations including:

Approved

Denied

Dismissed

Cancelled

Out of Scope

Upheld

Overturned

Functional behaviors required:

Determination applied per drug/service

Determination must:

require appropriate role authority (RBAC‑controlled)

require reason codes where applicable

be immutable except via allowed appeal/reopen paths

Determination history must be append‑only and auditable

These behaviors are explicitly aligned with separation‑of‑duties and audit guardrails as outlined in the source of truth document.

C. Case‑Level Determination (Derived Outcome)

The system must:

Automatically derive a case‑level organizational determination based on drug‑level outcomes

Prevent users from manually setting case‑level determinations

Minimum derivation logic (example only, see source of truth for detailed requirements):

All drugs Approved &rarr; Case = Approved

Mixed Approved / Denied / Out of Scope &rarr; Case = Partially Approved

All Denied &rarr; Case = Denied

All Cancelled &rarr; Case = Cancelled (Cancelled replaces &ldquo;Entry Error&rdquo; status)

All Out of Scope &rarr; Case = Out of Scope

✅ This preserves:

reporting clarity

external communication accuracy

regulatory defensibility

Why we distinguish determination levels

In Utilization Management, decisions are often made at the drug or service level, even though work is managed at the case level.

To reflect real UM operations &mdash; and to support accurate reporting, appeals, and regulatory compliance &mdash; we distinguish between:

Drug‑level determinations (decisions on individual services), and

Case‑level determinations (the rolled‑up outcome of the request as a whole).

Simple example

A prior authorization request includes three drugs:

Drug A &rarr; Approved

Drug B &rarr; Approved

Drug C &rarr; Denied

Each drug receives its own drug‑level determination.

The case‑level determination is Partially Approved, because the overall request includes mixed outcomes.

note69c3f750d8c7In the NewUM model, determinations include a set of determination reasons, which may vary by LOB. Engineering and Data & Analytics require these reason codes, which must be configurable by LOB and by payer programs (e.g., SOC, Vial Rounding, Gold Carding).

In the NewUM model, determinations include a set of determination reasons, which may vary by LOB. Engineering and Data & Analytics require these reason codes, which must be configurable by LOB and by payer programs (e.g., SOC, Vial Rounding, Gold Carding).

E. Internal vs External Visibility Controls

The system must:

Support visibility mapping, not duplication

Allow:

detailed internal states (e.g., Escalated to Physician)

simplified external representations (e.g., In Review)

Functional requirements:

Each state/status must be tagged as:

Internal‑only

External‑visible

External‑mapped (different label)

Determinations must be:

externally visible when meaningful

suppressed when administrative (as appropriate by LOB)

This is consistent with CMS/NCQA guidance and our prior internal/external state discussions to date.

F. Appeals & Reopen Logic

The system must:

Support appeals at the drug level

Preserve original determinations

Record appeal outcomes as:

Upheld

Overturned

Re‑derive case‑level determinations after appeal resolution

Functional safeguards:

Separation of duties enforced (original reviewer &ne; appeal reviewer)

Appeal outcomes must not overwrite original determinations

Appeal outcomes must be time‑stamped and role‑stamped

These requirements directly reflect determinations and appeal handling decisions discussed in SME sessions.

3. LOB‑specific overlays (without branching the system)

Medicare (Part C / D)

 | Medicaid

 | Commercial

 | 
Additional functional requirements:

Support CMS‑defined appeal terminology:

Redetermination

Reconsideration

IRE

Ability to flag:

IRE decisions as final

deemed approvals separately from clinical approvals

Enforce Medicare‑specific timelines and visibility rules

✅ These behaviors are Medicare‑only and non‑transferable to other LOBs. 

 | Additional functional requirements:

Configurable appeal paths by:

state

payer

Ability to:

enable/disable external review

vary terminology (e.g., upheld vs affirmed)

Maintain the same determination set, but allow state‑specific rules

✅  Medicaid must be configurable, not hard‑coded. 

 | Additional functional requirements:

Internal appeal handling only (no IRE)

Contract‑driven visibility rules

Simpler appeal sequencing

✅ Uses the same determination framework, without Medicare constructs. 

 | 
4. Why this requirement set improves organization-wide outcomes 

This design allows the system to support real UM operations &mdash; including partial approvals, appeals, and regulatory variation &mdash; without multiplying workflows or states.

Drug‑level determinations capture clinical reality.

Case‑level determinations provide clarity, reporting, and compliance.

States and statuses remain stable, auditable, and understandable.

#### WorkqueuesNon-Functional Requirements (NFRs)

Purpose

This page defines the Non-Functional Requirements (NFRs) for the NewUM platform, which represent platform-level quality constraints that apply across the entire end-to-end (E2E) case workflow

Scope

In Scope

The NFRs documented on this page apply to:

All NewUM workflows

All user roles (Provider, CRS, Clinical Reviewers, Health Plan users)

All payer-specific configurations

All deployment environments

Out Of Scope

Business rules

Workflow logic

Decision criteria

Data model definitions

UI behavior

noteb7a0896dbdd5If a requirement describes what the system does, it is not an NFR.
If it constrains how safely, how fast, or how reliably it does it, it is an NFR.

If a requirement describes what the system does, it is not an NFR.
If it constrains how safely, how fast, or how reliably it does it, it is an NFR.

Environmental considerations

This section outlines few considerations to keep in mind when creating engineering solutions and could be considered as non-functional requirement.

 | 
Best practices

 |  | Configuration and rules updates need to be tested on stable environment, ideally a staging database with same product version as on production environment before being released on production

 When NewUM release candidate is being prepared, it should be tested with current configuration and rules 

We should avoid &ldquo;deploying&rdquo; new versions of newUM and updating configuration/rules at the same time to reduce brittle surface

Ideally there should be no downtime when deploying new configuration or rules

If downtime is expected, every effort should be made to minimize duration of it and advance notification to users should be sent

#### Accessibility Requirements

Project Specifics

Target Release

 |  

 | 
Document Status

 |  in progressYellow   

 |

 |   

 | 
Designer

 |  

 | 
ADO Epic

 |

Stakeholders / SMEs

Background & Current State

Assumption to confirm

OnchoHealth&rsquo;s newUM platform needs to be compliant with HHS accessibility standards - updated section 504 and section 508.

While OnchoHealth might not be a direct federal contractor or direct recipient of federal funds, it&rsquo;s clients are, and by extension any 3rd party employee-facing software OncoHealth&rsquo;s clients use has to be compliant to HHS accessibility standards, which would include newUM.

Functional Requirements

WCAG 2.1 Level AA requirements

Requirement

 | Priority

 | Description (Use Case Format)

 | Notes

 | 
Category: Perception

 | 
Color Contrast

 |  | Ensure all text has a contrast ratio of at least 4.5:1 against its background. 

For large text or UI components like buttons/borders, the ratio must be 3:1.

 |  | 
Text Resizing

 |  | Users must be able to zoom up to 200% without the interface breaking or functionality disappearing.

 | Can be accomplished by browser&rsquo;s OOTB features.

 | 
Reflow 

 |  | The tool must support vertical scrolling only (no horizontal scrolling required) when viewed at a width equivalent to 320 CSS pixels

 |  | 
Non-Text Content 

 |  | Every meaningful icon or image (e.g., a "Warning" triangle next to a lab result) must have a text alternative (alt text) that a screen reader can announce.

 |  | 
Sensory Characteristics 

 |  | Avoid instructions like "Click the green button on the right." Use labels like "Click the 'Submit' button."

 |  | 
Category: Operable

 | 
Keyboard Access 

 |  | Every function (tabs, dropdowns, modal closes, and data entry) must be reachable and usable using only the Tab, Enter, and Space keys.

 |  | 
Focus Visible

 |  | When a user tabs through the tool, there must be a clear, highly visible "focus ring" (border) around the element they are currently on.

 |  | 
No Keyboard Traps

 |  | Ensure users can move focus out of a component (like a calendar picker or a modal) as easily as they moved into it.

 |  | 
Pointer Gestures

 |  | Any action requiring a complex gesture (like "pinch to zoom" or "swiping" a record to delete) must also have a single-click alternative.

 | Probably does not apply as newUM will be web-first

 | 
Meaningful Sequence

 |  | Ensure the "Tab order" follows a logical flow (usually top-to-bottom, left-to-right).

 |  | 
Category: Predictability

 | 
 Form Labels & Instructions

 |  | Every input field (e.g., Member ID, Dosage) must have a persistent, clear <label>. Do not rely solely on placeholder text that disappears when the user starts typing (ghost text).

 |  | 
Error Identification

 |  | If a user makes a mistake (e.g., wrong date format), the error must be described in text. Don't just turn the box red.

 |  | 
Predictable Navigation 

 |  | Navigation menus and common UI elements should appear in the same relative order on every screen of the application.

 |  | 
 Error Suggestion

 |  |  If an error is detected, the tool should provide suggestions for a fix (e.g., "Use MM/DD/YYYY format") unless it compromises security.

 |  | 
Category: Robustness

 | 
Name, Role, Value

 |  | For custom widgets (like a custom-built toggle switch), you must use ARIA labels so a screen reader knows it is a "Toggle" and whether it is currently "On" or "Off."

 |  | 
Status Messages

 |  | If a "Success" message pops up after saving a record, it must be programmatically announced to a screen reader user, even if their "focus" isn't on that message.

 |  | 
Sources:

HHS imposes accessibility standards for health websites, mobile apps, kiosks

HHS.gov Section 504 Final Rule Fact Sheet

HHS.gov Digital Accessibility & Section 508 Policy

W3C WCAG 2.1 Technical Standard

Background & Current State

Assumption to confirm

OnchoHealth&rsquo;s newUM platform needs to be compliant with HHS accessibility standards - updated section 504 and section 508.

While OnchoHealth might not be a direct federal contractor or direct recipient of federal funds, it&rsquo;s clients are, and by extension any 3rd party employee-facing software OncoHealth&rsquo;s clients use has to be compliant to HHS accessibility standards, which would include newUM.

Functional Requirements

WCAG 2.1 Level AA requirements

Requirement

 | Priority

 | Description (Use Case Format)

 | Notes

 | 
Category: Perception

 | 
Color Contrast

 |  | Ensure all text has a contrast ratio of at least 4.5:1 against its background. 

For large text or UI components like buttons/borders, the ratio must be 3:1.

 |  | 
Text Resizing

 |  | Users must be able to zoom up to 200% without the interface breaking or functionality disappearing.

 | Can be accomplished by browser&rsquo;s OOTB features.

 | 
Reflow 

 |  | The tool must support vertical scrolling only (no horizontal scrolling required) when viewed at a width equivalent to 320 CSS pixels

 |  | 
Non-Text Content 

 |  | Every meaningful icon or image (e.g., a "Warning" triangle next to a lab result) must have a text alternative (alt text) that a screen reader can announce.

 |  | 
Sensory Characteristics 

 |  | Avoid instructions like "Click the green button on the right." Use labels like "Click the 'Submit' button."

 |  | 
Category: Operable

 | 
Keyboard Access 

 |  | Every function (tabs, dropdowns, modal closes, and data entry) must be reachable and usable using only the Tab, Enter, and Space keys.

 |  | 
Focus Visible

 |  | When a user tabs through the tool, there must be a clear, highly visible "focus ring" (border) around the element they are currently on.

 |  | 
No Keyboard Traps

 |  | Ensure users can move focus out of a component (like a calendar picker or a modal) as easily as they moved into it.

 |  | 
Pointer Gestures

 |  | Any action requiring a complex gesture (like "pinch to zoom" or "swiping" a record to delete) must also have a single-click alternative.

 | Probably does not apply as newUM will be web-first

 | 
Meaningful Sequence

 |  | Ensure the "Tab order" follows a logical flow (usually top-to-bottom, left-to-right).

 |  | 
Category: Predictability

 | 
 Form Labels & Instructions

 |  | Every input field (e.g., Member ID, Dosage) must have a persistent, clear <label>. Do not rely solely on placeholder text that disappears when the user starts typing (ghost text).

 |  | 
Error Identification

 |  | If a user makes a mistake (e.g., wrong date format), the error must be described in text. Don't just turn the box red.

 |  | 
Predictable Navigation 

 |  | Navigation menus and common UI elements should appear in the same relative order on every screen of the application.

 |  | 
 Error Suggestion

 |  |  If an error is detected, the tool should provide suggestions for a fix (e.g., "Use MM/DD/YYYY format") unless it compromises security.

 |  | 
Category: Robustness

 | 
Name, Role, Value

 |  | For custom widgets (like a custom-built toggle switch), you must use ARIA labels so a screen reader knows it is a "Toggle" and whether it is currently "On" or "Off."

 |  | 
Status Messages

 |  | If a "Success" message pops up after saving a record, it must be programmatically announced to a screen reader user, even if their "focus" isn't on that message.

 |  |
